It didn't take long for Purdue to make a significant hire. Last night, we learned that Tim Tibesar would not continue as the defensive coordinator. Today, it was announced that Greg Hudson, who previously served as the linebackers coach at Florida State, will assume the role. According to Scout.com, Hudson has accepted the offer to become Purdue’s new defensive coordinator. I’m excited about this appointment. Florida State’s defense excelled this season, stifling opposing offenses. In the two games I watched closely—against Miami and Northern Illinois—the Seminoles dominated both teams’ offenses. Hudson’s tenure at East Carolina from 2005 to 2009 saw the Pirates compile a record of 5-6, 7-6, 8-5, 9-5, and 9-5, including back-to-back Conference-USA championships. Notably, in 2008, East Carolina defeated Virginia Tech and West Virginia to start the season, showcasing a formidable defense. Prior to Florida State, he coached linebackers at Cincinnati (1997-2000), Minnesota (2001-2004), and Notre Dame for two seasons. His experience spans multiple programs, including the Golden Gophers and the Fighting Irish, where the team thrived under Glen Mason. This season, Florida State achieved a 12-2 record, won the ACC, and secured a victory in the Orange Bowl with a strong defensive focus. They allowed just 14.7 points per game, ranking sixth nationally, and limited opponents to 10 or fewer points six times in 14 games. Christian Jones, a top-ranked linebacker, and Telvin Smith are key contributors who Hudson mentored. Hudson’s expertise can address the significant need at linebacker that Purdue hasn’t seen since Niko Koutouvides and Landon Johnson dominated the position a decade ago. Since then, Purdue has had a series of solid but not exceptional linebackers, leading to defensive struggles.
TOKYO — Once hailed as a prolific musical genius whose compositions graced popular video games and the competitive routines of top figure skaters for the upcoming Sochi Olympics, Mamoru Samuragochi, 50, revealed he had been running a significant deception. It emerged that he had hired a ghostwriter since the 1990s to compose most of his renowned pieces. These include Symphony No. 1 “Hiroshima,” the theme music for Resident Evil and Onimusha video games, and Sonatina for Violin, set to be used by the Japanese figure skater Daisuke Takahashi at the Sochi Games. The revelation sparked shock and outrage across Japan, a nation long enamored with Western classical music, as it emerged that Samuragochi may have also pretended to be deaf to gain public sympathy and cultivate the image of a modern-day Beethoven.
A coalition of feminist scholars has opposed efforts to criminalize street harassment in France, arguing that such measures might "stigmatize" men from migrant backgrounds. They argue that "working-class, racially profiled young men already endure more police violence and oppression," according to a letter they issued against Equality Minister Marlène Schiappa's proposal. The 15 signatories contend that training harassers would be more effective than creating a new offense, which they believe would exacerbate the control and repression of disadvantaged men. The letter, published in Libération, criticizes the plan to restrict penalties to street harassment, ignoring abuses in homes and workplaces. It warns that criminalizing street harassment could obscure harassment in affluent neighborhoods and corporate offices. The minister previously defined street harassment as a man repeatedly asking a woman for her phone number on public transport after she boards another train. This crackdown came after surveys highlighted widespread street harassment in certain French regions. A 2015 study in migrant-dense areas found nearly universal reports of sexual harassment or assault. In May, Breitbart London reported that some Parisian neighborhoods were effectively "no-go" zones for women due to severe verbal and physical harassment by immigrants.
Act immediately: Cisco has identified vulnerabilities in several of its Adaptive Security Appliances (ASA) due to a remote code execution bug. This issue arises from an improper handling of fragmented Internet Key Exchange (IKE) payloads in the ASA's implementation of the fragmentation protocol. Specifically, a bounds-checking flaw exists, allowing an attacker to overflow a heap buffer with controlled data, leading to the potential for remote code execution. Affected models include the ASA 5500 series, ASA 5500-X, ASA Services Module for Catalyst 6500 switches and 7600 Series routers, ASA 1000V Cloud Firewall, Adaptive Security Virtual Appliance, Firepower 9300 ASA module, and ISA 3000 industrial security appliance. Both IPv4 and IPv6 traffic can trigger this vulnerability. According to Exodus Intelligence, the core of the problem lies in Cisco's queue limitations, which are set to 8 bits despite the fragment length being 16 bits. Exploitation involves creating a reassembly queue where a fragment's length is less than the default fragment header size, causing a reload of the target system. However, further steps can be taken to place attacker code in a writable memory location, granting control over the device. Cisco has provided patches for the affected software versions.
In a pub with six friends, the first remarks, "My glass is half empty; time for another one." The second replies, "My glass is half full; I’m fine for now." The third suggests, "The bar is busy; let’s wait a bit." The fourth chimes in, "Since we’re waiting, we might as well join the queue and get thoroughly intoxicated." The fifth departs, avoiding arguments, waiting, or getting drunk. Meanwhile, the sixth downs everyone's drinks, eager to move forward. The lesson here is that pessimists want more, optimists are content, realists are bothersome, cynics create conflict, quitters are irrelevant, and opportunists enjoy themselves. Thus, when you go out for drinks, try to avoid arguments and seek enjoyment; otherwise, someone else will seize the fun at your expense.

Malaysian police have arrested four individuals suspected of ties to terrorism between August 2 and September 17, including three foreigners who were subsequently deported. Among those arrested is a Bangladeshi restaurant owner, suspected of involvement in smuggling weapons for international terror groups, with Interpol issuing a "Red Notice" for him. A Nepalese citizen managing an entertainment venue was also apprehended for allegedly forging travel documents for members of international terror groups. Another suspect is a Moroccan believed to be affiliated with the Islamic State, who was previously detained by Turkish authorities for attempting to smuggle into Syria. The fourth suspect is a Malaysian personal chauffeur for a businessman, suspected of connections to Muhammad Wanndy Mohamad Jedy, who has been actively promoting Islamic State activities on his Facebook page.
Take down the door knockers, lower the shutters, and act as if no one is home. Your adult children are returning—forever. A recent report from Fidelity Investments and the Stanford Center on Longevity, based on a survey of 9,000 employees, reveals that one in nine baby boomer parents has a child who has come back home within the past year. While these adult children benefit by saving on rent and household expenses, their parents bear the brunt: 68% of parents reported increased stress, 53% felt less happiness, and 53% experienced reduced leisure time. Over three-quarters (76%) of parents also noted taking on additional costs. Even those in their 40s and 50s consider moving back home a viable option. According to Trulia, older millennials are 2.7 times more likely to live with their parents than those under 55 were in 1999, and Gen Xers are 2.2 times more likely, reflecting a significant shift. "Parents should be realistic about their financial situation when helping their children," noted Katie Taylor, Fidelity's vice president of thought leadership. In the U.S., 19% of the population (nearly 61 million people) now live in multigenerational households, up from 17% (42 million) in 2009 and 12% (27.5 million) in 1980, according to the Pew Research Center. Not all millennials are perceived as "lazy" or "entitled"; about one in four 25- to 34-year-olds living at home without working or studying do so due to health reasons or caregiving responsibilities. Moreover, over a third of Americans, including millennials, plan to support their parents financially in the near future, as another survey indicated. Some are even assisting their parents in saving for retirement.

Images from Hanson's Auctioneers Image caption These vivid pictures offer a glimpse into the Second Boer War, uncovering the harsh realities of the conflict. A collection of previously unseen photographs, alongside medals and badges, from the Second Boer War has been discovered in a Derbyshire home and will be auctioned in late July. According to auctioneer Charles Hanson, "This find is akin to a time capsule, illuminating the war in new ways." The photographs were captured by Robert Oliver, who served in the 1899-1902 war and was later awarded the Queen's Medal for South Africa. Mr. Hanson notes, "These graphic images capture the grim truth of war, a stark contrast to the portrayal by Victorian press, which often depicted the British Empire as invincible." Included in the collection are images of fallen soldiers, funerals, and even a war dog. Other items in the auction include pairs of original kid gloves, spurs, an ammunition bandolier, various hats and caps, a South African feathered headdress, and a cartridge belt. It is revealed that Robert Oliver had an adventurous early life, running away at 16 to work as a lumberjack in Canada before joining the Staffordshire Police and owning a pub in Hartington, Derbyshire. The auction is scheduled for July 25th.

I’m still not sure if I like how it turned out. An alternate, darker version can be found [here]. The original sketch is [here]. It all began with a single line: “Shall I pity you, then?” I had scribbled it down somewhere, and it eventually transformed into something like this: “The spirits believe I owe you my pity, for you are merely mortal. You will know the ills of humankind; you will know of suffering, hatred, fear, and disappointment. Your eyes will cloud with the tears of sorrows that come with the passing of those you love... In time, your soul and your memory will fade from existence. Should I pity you, then, because you will suffer and die while I shall live eternally?” The response would have been: “No. I pity you. For, while I will die, you will never again live.” I didn’t always have a fond opinion of Yue. However, when I first drew this, I think I was starting to develop a liking for her. THE HAGUE (Reuters) - An international arbitration court ruled in favor of Slovenia in a long-standing maritime dispute with Croatia, granting it direct access to international waters in the Adriatic Sea. The Permanent Court of Arbitration's decision is final and binding. Croatia, which withdrew from the proceedings in 2015, stated it would disregard the ruling. The court determined that Slovenia should have "uninterrupted access" to the shared sea, according to presiding Judge Gilbert Guillaume. Croatia's Prime Minister, Andrej Plenkovic, responded that the decision was not legally binding and they were open to a bilateral dialogue with Slovenia. Slovenia's Prime Minister, Miro Cerar, welcomed the ruling, emphasizing continued cooperation with Croatia. The countries' dispute over a section of their sea and land border, stemming from their independence from Yugoslavia in 1991, delayed Croatia's EU accession for years. The tribunal now confirms that Slovenia gains most of the Piran bay area as its territorial waters and establishes a 2.5 nautical-mile-wide and 10 nautical-mile-long corridor through Croatian waters for direct access to international waters. Croatia's withdrawal in 2015 due to a leaked tape involving a Slovenian judge has raised concerns about the effectiveness of future arbitrations and adherence to EU accession promises.
REC Silicon expects to fall short of its Q3 polysilicon production and sales targets, citing the ongoing solar trade conflict between the U.S. and China, as well as deteriorating PV market conditions. By October 1, 2016, the company plans to operate at about 50% of its full capacity at its Moses Lake facility. Production is anticipated to remain low until market conditions improve. For Q3, the company forecasts polysilicon sales (excluding fines and powders) to total 1,800 tonnes and revenues between $45 million and $50 million, down from $71.1 million in the preceding quarter due to reduced FBR sales volumes. Total Q3 polysilicon production is expected to be 3,900 tonnes, below the previously guided 4,490 tonnes, with FBR production projected at 3,300 tonnes instead of the earlier estimated 3,830 tonnes. Additionally, REC Silicon is discussing with its joint venture partner deferring the $169 million required for the construction of a FBR polysilicon plant in Yulin, China, until after 2018, pending resolution of the trade dispute.
A minister at Phillips Exeter Academy instructed a male student accused of sexual misconduct to bake bread for his alleged victim as a form of "penance," according to a report by The Boston Globe. This unusual arrangement emerged during a broader review of how New England's elite boarding schools handle sexual misconduct cases. Earlier, the Globe revealed that a teacher and administrator at Phillips Exeter had admitted to sexual misconduct from decades ago, yet the school had not disclosed this to students and alumni. However, recent incidents illustrate more immediate concerns. In the fall, Michaella Henry reported to administrators that a male student had touched her without her consent. Instead of involving the police, Rev. Robert Thompson facilitated a meeting between the alleged perpetrator, Chukwudi Ikpeazu, and Henry. They agreed that Ikpeazu would bake and deliver "monkey bread" weekly to her. As part of this agreement, the minister also required Ikpeazu to perform an "act of penance" by baking bread for her throughout the year. Despite the minister's praise for Henry’s acceptance, the arrangement increased her stress, leading her to report the incident to the police in the spring. Ikpeazu is now facing a misdemeanor charge of sexual assault, with arraignment scheduled for August. For the full story, see The Boston Globe.
In 2015, college graduates carried an average of $30,000 in student debt, marking a 4% increase from the prior year, according to a report by The Institute for College Access and Success (TICAS). TICAS president Lauren Asher stated, "We must make college more affordable and reduce the burden of debt for students and their families." The average debt for college graduates in California was $22,000, ranking third nationally, though it was increasing at the same pace as the national average. National University topped the California list with graduates owing nearly $53,000. Debt at University of California campuses ranged from $17,869 at UC Berkeley to $22,580 at UC Santa Cruz. For California State University graduates, debt varied from $10,872 at Fresno State to $23,973 at Humboldt State. TICAS noted that the reported debt averages omit data from for-profit colleges, which often withhold this information, potentially underestimating actual state averages. "State averages are based on voluntary reports from colleges about their graduates' combined federal and private loan debts," explained TICAS associate research director Diane Cheng. "Schools with high debt levels might not disclose all private loans, and some may not have complete data." The institute's analysis also showed that in 2012, graduates from for-profit colleges typically accrued around $40,000 in student debt. Recommendations from the report include using financial need to determine public grant eligibility, informing students about their loans to aid in decision-making, and adopting California's practice of informing students about available federal aid before approving private loans.

According to a DOJ letter released on December 12, the Department of Justice (DOJ) is urging the Census Bureau to incorporate a citizenship status question on the 2020 census forms to aid in enforcing the Voting Rights Act. In the letter, DOJ lawyer Arthur Gary wrote to Census Bureau official Dr. Ron Jarmin that including this question is necessary for accurately calculating the citizen voting-age population in areas where voting rights violations are suspected. The Census Bureau confirmed the existence of the letter and stated that the request will be processed through its standard procedure for considering potential questions. This latest development follows several recent reports suggesting that the Trump administration planned to include an immigration status inquiry in the 2020 census. Opponents argue that such a question could deter participation, while advocates believe it is crucial for maintaining the integrity of future elections.

Bill Gates, co-founder and philanthropist of Microsoft, announced that the Bill & Melinda Gates Foundation will allocate an additional $200 million annually to combat malaria, marking a 30% increase in its malaria-fighting budget. This contribution will join the foundation’s existing investments in the Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria. Gates also revealed plans to dedicate over $500 million this year to battling various diseases like pneumonia and diarrheal and parasitic illnesses in impoverished nations. He expressed confidence in eradicating malaria during his lifetime and outlined strategies including the development of a drug or vaccine to target asymptomatic carriers. The foundation has awarded $156 million to the PATH Malaria Vaccine Initiative to advance vaccine research aimed at interrupting the malarial parasite's transmission cycle. Additionally, the Gates Foundation committed $50 million towards Ebola treatment, testing, and vaccine research, emphasizing the need for enhanced global health infrastructure. Gates warned that future epidemics might be even more contagious, urging all countries to bolster their healthcare systems and invest in new medical solutions.

While NFC is commonly known for digital wallets and simple device pairing, it might surprise you to learn that it can generate a small amount of power. Although this isn't enough to replace your primary electricity supply, it's sufficient for a small E Ink display. Liliputing reported this feature on the NFC Brief site, and while it may seem like a novelty, there are practical applications. Since E Ink screens only need power when refreshing to show new content, tapping an NFC-enabled smartphone to a special E Ink display can both provide the necessary data and power to display it. Intel Labs, the University of Washington, and the University of Massachusetts Amherst collaborated to develop this special NFC tag. While no commercial products currently exist using this technology, the concept and demonstration are promising. Think about how companion displays could be integrated into various environments—such as your car, desk, or laptop bags—to show static, yet useful information without additional power consumption.
A new study, involving 6,250 children from an ongoing government survey tracking kindergarteners through fifth grade, reveals that obese children tend to perform worse in math compared to their non-obese peers. The research, published in the June 14 issue of Child Development, shows that persistent obesity from kindergarten through fifth grade leads to significant declines in math test scores by first grade. For boys, this trend was not observed when obesity developed later, but girls experiencing late-onset obesity showed a temporary dip in math skills. Beyond mathematical performance, the study indicates that persistently obese girls exhibit fewer social and interpersonal skills. Obese children, both boys and girls, reported feeling more sad, lonely, and anxious, potentially influencing their academic outcomes. Study author Sara Gable, an associate professor of nutrition and exercise physiology at the University of Missouri-Columbia, stated, "The findings highlight the intricate links between children's weight, social-emotional well-being, and academic performance." While obesity may contribute to these issues, the reverse could also be true, as noted by Dr. Becky Hashim, a clinical child psychologist. Being overweight might isolate children, leading to poor social skills and emotional distress, yet children with poor social skills might turn to food for comfort, exacerbating obesity. Ultimately, emotional struggles like sadness, loneliness, or anxiety can hinder school performance by making it harder to focus and engage in learning.
Copyright image courtesy of Reuters. In southern Myanmar, an influx of rats has affected villages, leading authorities to offer a reward of 3 pence (about 4 US cents) per rat killed. Locals have been using sticks, slingshots, and rocks to combat the infestation, reportedly eliminating over 4,000 rodents. While there are worries about potential diseases, locals also fear this might signal impending disasters like floods or earthquakes, as per traditional beliefs. A Japanese study suggests rats might sense seismic activity, though no diseases have yet been identified in the current batch. Heavy rains in the Ayeyarwady region are believed to have caused the rat surge, which has consumed substantial food supplies. This scenario is not unprecedented; in 2008, similar events in northwestern Chin State led to a risk of starvation when rats devoured bamboo fruits and crops, a phenomenon recurring approximately every 50 years. During the previous outbreak in the 1950s, it is estimated that 15,000 people died of starvation.
By Mohammed Dhaysane At least 11 individuals, comprising Somali government soldiers and al-Shabaab fighters, lost their lives when the terrorist group launched an attack on an army base in Bulo-gudud on Sunday morning, according to officials. Colonel Mukhtar Abdi Mohamed from Jubaland state reported that at least four soldiers and seven al-Shabaab militants were among the dead, with over ten casualties from both sides. He stated that the attack began with a suicide car bomb explosion followed by intense fighting. General Ismail Sahardid of the Somali National Army confirmed that they had killed more than 20 al-Shabaab militants in the conflict. An eyewitness described hearing a massive explosion, followed by two hours of fierce combat. Al-Shabaab claimed responsibility for the attack, stating they had killed over 26 government soldiers and captured three military vehicles. Bulo-gudud is situated approximately 30 kilometers from the strategic port city of Kismayo, which is about 482 kilometers south of Somalia's capital, Mogadishu.

This year, thirteen states have achieved their lowest-ever unemployment rates, matching or surpassing records dating back over four decades when the federal government began tracking state-level data. Eight years post the trough of the severest recession in recent memory, these states, ranging from traditionally liberal ones like Hawaii and California to more conservative states such as Idaho and Texas, are experiencing robust economic growth. In October, Alabama, Hawaii, Maine, Mississippi, Tennessee, Texas, and Washington all met or exceeded their lowest rates on record, according to the Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS) monthly report. Similarly, California, Colorado, Idaho, North Dakota, and Oregon reached new lows earlier in the year. During the peak of the Great Recession in 2010, six states—California, Colorado, Florida, Georgia, Nevada, and North Carolina—hit unprecedented high unemployment levels. Oregon, Rhode Island, and Kansas also set records that year. The national unemployment rate is currently at 4.1%, the lowest since December 2000. Thirteen states boast unemployment rates notably lower than the national average, while fifteen states have higher rates. Hawaii leads with an unemployment rate of 2.2% in October, followed by North Dakota at 2.5%, Colorado, Nebraska, and New Hampshire, each at 2.7%. Alaska's rate stands at 7.2%, the highest in the nation, trailed closely by the District of Columbia at 6.6% and New Mexico at 6.1%. Over the past year, Alabama saw the most significant drop, by 2.5 percentage points, while Tennessee's rate fell by 2 percentage points. Unemployment rates rose in only two states—Alaska and South Dakota—and the District of Columbia.

A single father and his seven children—five girls and two boys—were discovered deceased late Monday in their home on Maryland’s eastern shore, victims of carbon monoxide poisoning from a gas-powered generator, according to police. The children were found in their beds, appearing to be asleep, said Princess Anne Police Chief Scott Keller. Delmarva Power had cut off power to the home of Rodney Todd, 36, in Princess Anne, after finding it illegally connected to the power grid. There was never a legal connection during the Todd family's residence there. Delmarva Power disconnected the illegal meter for safety reasons and adhered to protocol, stating they did not disconnect service for nonpayment. Following the power outage, Todd purchased a generator to heat his home, informed by Todd’s stepfather, Lloyd Edwards. Unpaid electricity bills frequently compel individuals to use alternative heating methods, sometimes resulting in tragic outcomes, noted Russ Paulsen, executive director of community preparedness at the American Red Cross. He highlighted that impoverished areas face six times the risk of house fires compared to more affluent neighborhoods, and a lack of smoke detectors exacerbates the danger. The Red Cross offers free smoke detectors, which reduce the risk of fire-related deaths by half, according to Paulsen. Carbon monoxide, he explained, impairs judgment and induces sleep, leading to fatalities. Authorities are investigating the incident and have requested records from Delmarva Power related to Todd’s home. Friends and family described Todd as dedicated to his children. "I'm just numb. It's like a nightmare but it's not," Tyisha Luneice Chambers, the children’s mother, told the Associated Press. "If I had known about the lack of electricity, I would have helped." "He was an outstanding dad. To ensure his seven children stayed warm, he bought a generator, which ultimately led to their demise," Edwards told the Associated Press. Todd worked at a nearby University of Maryland Eastern Shore kitchen to support his family and had previously asked Somerset County to assist with heating costs, revealed Tom VanLandingham, director of the county’s Office of Home Energy Programs. "We're puzzled as to why he didn't apply this year," VanLandingham told the Associated Press. A former economic advisor to Alex Salmond, Professor John Kay, has cautioned that an independent Scotland maintaining the pound in a formal currency union with the UK is unlikely due to stringent conditions set by London. Professor Kay, who previously served on the Council of Economic Advisers, informed MSPs that negotiations over such a currency deal would be "intractable." Salmond has not proposed an alternative plan for Scotland’s currency post-independence. Kay also noted that the conventional view, especially in the eurozone, is that a currency union necessitates fiscal backing. He stated that while he doubts this is necessary, the belief in such a requirement makes negotiations challenging. Kay argued that the UK Treasury would impose conditions during negotiations that would be difficult for a Scottish government to accept, including control over Scotland's banking system and fiscal policies. This, he said, would effectively give up most of the "economic policy levers" Scotland sought through independence. Gavin McCrone, a former chief economist for Scotland, further emphasized that a UK chancellor would not risk taxpayers' money in the rest of the UK for Scottish debts or bad loans. This, McCrone suggested, explains why Chancellor George Osborne and others reject the idea of a currency union. However, McCrone acknowledged that negotiations would still occur. The finance committee was gathering evidence on Scotland's public finances following the referendum.

New Delhi: On Thursday, the Supreme Court referred the issue of fixed dose combination (FDC) drugs to the Drugs Technical Advisory Board (DTAB) for a fresh review of their safety, efficacy, and therapeutic justification before any recommendations for action are made. Following the DTAB's examination or a sub-committee's review, along with stakeholder consultations, the expert body must submit its report to the government within six months, as directed by a bench led by Justice Rohinton F. Nariman. The court excluded 15 FDCs licensed before 1988 from this order. It also mandated maintaining the status quo for 329 FDCs referred to the DTAB. Welcoming the order, the All India Drugs Action Network stated that it paves the way for the government to address irrational, unscientific, and potentially hazardous FDCs. S. Srinivasan, co-convenor of the network, noted that while 344 FDCs represent about 5% of India's FDC market, roughly half are deemed irrational. He urged the government to proactively eliminate other irrational FDCs for patient safety. Pfizer Ltd, the Indian subsidiary of a US pharmaceutical company, supported the government's goal of eliminating irrational drug combinations and unapproved medicines through consultation. The ban affected around 6,000 brands from major pharmaceutical companies including Pfizer, Wockhardt, Alkem Laboratories, Cipla, Sanofi India, and Sun Pharmaceutical Industries, following a report by a six-member committee led by Chandrakant Kokate. This panel identified 963 FDCs as "irrational," posing health risks. The Delhi High Court previously quashed the ban, citing insufficient consultation with statutory bodies.
LONDON (Reuters) - Britain's economic momentum is expected to weaken in the second half of 2017, based on a key survey that may disappoint Bank of England officials hoping to raise interest rates for the first time in a decade. A Markit/CIPS survey showed service sector growth slowed to a four-month low in June, with business expectations hitting their lowest point since last July. Sterling weakened after the survey indicated a recovery in the second quarter, with the economy likely expanding at a quarterly rate of about 0.4%, double the pace of the weak first quarter. However, forward-looking indicators suggested caution, with business expectations dropping to their lowest since July 2016 and new order growth hitting a nine-month low. The headline PMI index dropped to a four-month low of 53.4 in June from 53.8 in May, slightly below forecasts. On Tuesday, BoE rate-setter Michael Saunders argued that lower consumer spending could be balanced by increased exports and investment, justifying his vote to hike rates. However, JPMorgan economist Allan Monks noted that the latest PMI survey casts doubt on this premise. He pointed out that while the UK PMI has weakened, broader European PMIs have improved significantly. The mood among services firms was likely dampened by post-election uncertainty and Brexit negotiations, according to IHS Markit. Additionally, a third consecutive monthly drop in car sales underscored a consumer slowdown. Official data revealed a decline in productivity for the first time since late 2015, complicating the BoE's outlook. Weak productivity limits potential wage growth but coincides with rising inflation. "Addressing the country's low productivity is crucial," stated Ian Brinkley, acting chief economist at the Chartered Institute of Personnel and Development, "as it affects wage growth and living standards, and prepares the UK to compete post-Brexit."

A declassified State Department report from May 1964 indicated that India could have developed nuclear weapons as early as 1964. On May 18, 2023, this report and others were released by the National Security Archive and the Nuclear Proliferation International History Project. According to the Press Trust of India, the report mentioned frequent changes in the fuel core of the Canadian-Indian Reactor (CIR) at Trombay, reportedly every six months. At that time, US intelligence questioned India's nuclear ambitions. The State Department’s Bureau of Intelligence and Research (INR) reported, "The Indians are now in a position to begin nuclear weapons development if they choose to do so." It noted that while there was no evidence of an active weapons research and development program, a six-month fuel cycle suggested a more strategic use, possibly for producing weapons-grade plutonium. Although the report found no concrete evidence of a weapons program, it suggested that everything India had done up to that point was consistent with developing such capabilities. The State Department stated, "India's leadership might have had nationalistic motives for building the Phoenix plant, but if it wanted a nuclear weapons capability, it would pursue such a capability." The report concluded that India had made the "first deliberate decision" toward obtaining a nuclear weapon, implying that it had the means to produce or access weapons-grade plutonium. In 2013, India was estimated to have at least 110 nuclear weapons. Despite signing and ratifying the Biological Weapons Convention and the Chemical Weapons Convention, India has not joined the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty, arguing that it permits the US, Russia, China, the UK, and France to maintain nuclear arsenals without commitments to disarm.

Local police in the eastern Punjab province have detained all alcohol vendors from Toba Tek Singh, the location of the incident, for questioning, as stated by Muhammad Shahbaz, a local police official, to the DPA news agency. The intoxicated celebration led to sickness and hospitalization for around 150 people, with many unconscious. Funerals have been conducted for 25 of the victims. Shahbaz noted that one of the suspected organizers of the tainted alcohol supply was among the deceased, making it challenging for police to determine its origin. Similar incidents of death from contaminated liquor, frequently homemade, have occurred periodically in Pakistan, especially around religious festivals. In March, at least 40 people, mainly Hindus, succumbed to toxic alcohol shortly before Holi. Alcohol consumption remains prohibited for Muslims in the country, while non-Muslims require permits to purchase it in limited quantities. Christians constitute about 1.6% of Pakistan’s population of approximately 190 million, with the majority residing in Punjab.

Many Harry Potter enthusiasts generally view Draco Malfoy as a bully deserving no sympathy. Despite his unsavory actions, a theory about the sixth and seventh books may prompt a reevaluation. This theory posits that Draco was bitten by Fenrir Greyback and turned into a werewolf as punishment from Voldemort. Although not novel, the idea gained renewed attention through an Imgur post and persists on websites like Draco Malfoy Is a Werewolf. According to the theory, Lucius Malfoy's failures—such as failing to retrieve the prophecy and allowing a Horcrux to be destroyed—led to Draco's transformation after the events of Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix. Remus Lupin mentions in Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince that Greyback often uses werewolves to punish enemies. After becoming a werewolf, Draco's unusual behavior, such as his paleness, might have been overlooked as him joining the Death Eaters, when in fact, he was struggling with his condition. His close relationship with Severus Snape could be explained by Snape’s ability to brew Wolfsbane potion. Additionally, since Draco was no longer a pure-blood, it clarifies why the Malfoys eventually betrayed Voldemort in the final book. Given these circumstances, the Malfoys lost their loyalty to Voldemort due to Draco's transformation. While this theory is compelling, J.K. Rowling debunked it in 2015 via Twitter, stating that Draco is definitively not a werewolf and that Snape is not a vampire. Nonetheless, many fans still wish this theory were true, as it would offer a deeper explanation for Draco's antagonistic behavior.
A new motorway connecting Gort and Tuam in County Galway has recently opened. Spanning over 57 kilometers, the M17/M18 cost nearly half a billion euros to build. This toll-free highway is anticipated to significantly shorten travel times to and from the northwest by avoiding several previous congestion points. After nearly 15 years of planning, the motorway's construction took several years to complete. The opening of the M17/M18 motorway in Galway aims to reduce journey times for motorists heading to and from the northwest, bypassing the previously congested towns of Tuam, Claregalway, and Clarinbridge. However, there are concerns that traffic issues may now concentrate in Galway city, known for its gridlock on the eastern approaches. To address these concerns, Transport Infrastructure Ireland and Galway County Council view today’s opening as part of a broader plan to manage increased traffic volumes. The next step involves planning a city bypass for Galway, which is already contentious and likely to face challenges during the upcoming planning process.

Despite the El Niño winter, California remains in a drought. In Marin County, although water restrictions are still in place, the drought appears more symbolic than real. Six out of seven reservoirs are full, and the remaining one is at 95% capacity. Despite recent rain breaks, El Niño conditions continue, along with statewide drought concerns. The Marin Municipal Water District reports 98% capacity across its seven reservoirs, a stark contrast to other parts of California. Crystal Yezman, who manages the Tamalpais watershed for the district, notes that Marin County’s near-full reservoirs are particularly noteworthy. This year, Marin County also boasts an additional blessing: over 500 Coho salmon returned to Lagunitas Creek, marking their best return in a decade. These fish managed to swim far upstream in December thanks to well-timed, spaced storms. "For the Coho population on Lagunitas Creek, this has been a perfect El Niño," said fishery program manager Gregory Andrew. He added that while the population is sustainable but precarious, this year's success is a welcome sign.
Rhus javanica, a medicinal herb, has demonstrated oral therapeutic antiviral activity against herpes simplex virus (HSV) in mice. We isolated two primary anti-HSV compounds, moronic acid and betulonic acid, from the herbal extract using ethyl acetate extraction at pH 10, followed by chromatographic separations. Both compounds were then evaluated for their anti-HSV activity in vitro and in vivo. Moronic acid was found to be the predominant anti-HSV component in the ethyl acetate-soluble fraction. The 50% plaque reduction concentrations for moronic acid and betulonic acid against wild-type HSV-1 were 3.9 and 2.6 micrograms per milliliter, respectively. The therapeutic index for moronic acid (10.3-16.3) was higher than that for betulonic acid (6.2). Moronic acid exhibited similar antiviral activity against acyclovir-phosphonoacetic acid-resistant HSV-1, thymidine kinase-deficient HSV-1, and wild-type HSV-2 compared to wild-type HSV-1. When administered orally to mice infected with HSV-1, moronic acid significantly delayed the progression of skin lesions and extended the mean survival times of infected mice without causing toxicity. Moronic acid more effectively reduced viral loads in the brain compared to the skin, aligning with the extended survival times. Consequently, moronic acid was identified as a major anti-HSV compound from the Rhus javanica extract. Its antiviral mechanism differed from that of acyclovir. Moronic acid demonstrated oral therapeutic efficacy in HSV-infected mice and exhibited novel antiviral properties consistent with those of the herbal extract.
Under a new drunk-driving law signed by the governor, drivers with three or more DUI convictions in ten years could face license revocation for up to ten years. Assemblyman Jerry Hill’s legislation, effective January 1, 2012, extends the current three-year maximum to ten years for repeat offenders. Hill estimated the measure could remove over 10,000 repeat DUI offenders from the roads annually. In 2008, nearly 188,000 DUI convictions were recorded statewide, with 9,164 individuals at their third conviction and 3,200 with four or more offenses. Governor Arnold Schwarzenegger stated, “This legislation is a crucial step toward safer roads in California, ensuring that those with multiple DUI convictions do not endanger lives.” The National Highway Traffic Safety Administration reports that California makes 1.5 million DUI arrests annually, with one-third being repeat offenders. Over 310,000 Californians have three or more DUI convictions.
Abnormal behaviors in animals can be described in multiple ways. Statistically, such behaviors are those that significantly deviate—either above or below—from the typical range of occurrences, frequencies, or intensities. In theory, nearly any behavior can be considered abnormal in an individual context. More informally, "abnormal" encompasses activities judged to be outside the usual behavioral patterns for animals of a specific class or age group. For instance, infanticide might be common in one species but rare in another; it would be considered abnormal if it occurs frequently in the second species. This list excludes one-off behaviors deemed abnormal for an individual unless they are repeatedly observed and recognized as part of the species' ethogram. Most abnormal behaviors can be grouped into categories like eliminative, ingestive, or stereotypic, though many may fit into multiple categories, so no attempt is made to categorize them here. Some abnormal behaviors may result from environmental factors (such as captivity) while others might be due to medical conditions. This list does not include behaviors arising from genetically modified animals designed to exhibit abnormal traits. Examples include a polar bear performing stereotyped pacing and an Asiatic elephant exhibiting stereotyped rocking and trunk swinging. References: [1] Abnormal Behavior in Animals. (1968). Edited by M.W. Fox. W. B. Saunders Company, Toronto. Further reading: Behavior Consultation.

The charges were the result of an investigation by both the Baltimore Police Department and the State’s Attorney’s Office.

Retail stores are a result of meticulous spatial planning: essential items like toilet paper and milk are placed at the rear, ensuring customers encounter higher-margin goods before reaching them. Store layouts typically follow a clockwise navigation pattern to facilitate easy access for right-handed shoppers. Many establishments use light fragrances, as studies show that pleasant aromas can increase impulse buying. However, with consumers increasingly focused on specific purchases, these strategies are becoming less effective. "Shoppers are now better equipped to resist retail tactics," a retail consultant noted to The Wall Street Journal. Online shopping has taught consumers to buy only what they need, often leaving the rest behind. To counteract traditional retail strategies, some consumers implement personal rules. For instance, a recent Wall Street Journal observation found that couples often shop together to curb each other's impulses, while others avoid shopping carts to prevent filling them unnecessarily.
Overnight, a fire in a slum area of Manila's Tondo district left more than 15,000 people homeless and injured seven individuals as they attempted to rescue belongings. The fire, which began in a shanty house, consumed 1,200 structures before being extinguished after 10 hours on Wednesday morning. Seven residents suffered injuries. Three evacuation centers were established, providing food and water to about 3,000 displaced families. Despite the fire's containment, many remained on a nearby road with their possessions, including clothing and appliances like washing machines and electric fans. The blaze disrupted traffic, blocking deliveries to and from the port. Authorities are investigating the cause, with previous fires often attributed to faulty electrical wiring due to illegal connections in the area.
A fully accomplished Dzogchen practitioner can achieve the rainbow body at death, a process where the body diminishes, emitting rainbow light, until only hair and nails remain. Through trekchö practice, the body transforms into a Light Body, dissolving entirely into space. Notable practitioners who attained this include Garab Dorje, Manjushrimitra, Shri Singha, Jnanasutra, and Vairotsana. Another achievement through tögal practice is the Rainbow Body of Great Transference, where the master's body dissolves into rainbow light to live long and benefit others, exemplified by Padmasambhava, Vimalamitra, Nyang Tingdzin Zangpo, and Chetsün Senge Wangchuk. Recent examples include Lama Achuk, whose body shrunk significantly before achieving the rainbow body.

Red Robin's 2017 fall menu will be available at participating locations nationwide until December 31, 2017.
Eric Williamson, from Springfield, Virginia, was brewing coffee in his kitchen when a woman and a seven-year-old boy saw him through the window. The woman reported the incident to the police, who arrested Williamson later that Monday morning. Williamson, who is 29, maintained that he had done nothing wrong and that any exposure was unintentional. "I wasn't clothed, but I was alone in my home, just getting out of bed. It was dark, and I didn't realize anyone was watching," he stated. Williamson, who has a five-year-old daughter, added, "I'm a loving father. Anyone who knows me can attest to that; I would never do anything like that to a child." He continued, "I never saw anyone, never spoke to anyone. I simply went to get coffee. If I felt comfortable in my kitchen, it was natural. It's my home." Mary Ann Jennings, a spokesperson for Fairfax County police, explained that Williamson was arrested because officers believed he intentionally wanted to be seen naked by the public. If convicted, Williamson faces up to a year in jail and a $2,000 fine. He is contesting the charge and is seeking damages from the police.
Depending on your use case, MongoDB v3.4 offers the $graphLookup aggregation pipeline operator, which can recursively search within a collection. For instance, using your document hierarchy and values, you might run the following aggregation: ```javascript db.collectionName.aggregate([ { $unwind: { path: "$childrenIdList", preserveNullAndEmptyArrays: true } }, { $graphLookup: { from: "collectionName", startWith: "$_id", connectFromField: "_id", connectToField: "childrenIdList", as: "myparents", restrictSearchWithMatch: { "_id": 7 } }}, { $match: { "_id": 7 } }, { $group: { _id: "$_id", parents: { $addToSet: "$myparents._id" } }} ]) ``` This should yield a result similar to: ```json { "_id" : 7, "parents" : [ [ 1, 2, 4 ] ] } ``` However, for larger collections, this query might not be efficient due to the $unwind operation on each document, which prevents index utilization. Therefore, consider reevaluating your document model structure. Refer to Data Models Tree Structures for optimization based on your specific application logic and querying needs, allowing the flexible document schema to adapt accordingly.
AKRON, Ohio - The holiday shopping season is upon us, and Akron is adding a new shopping destination with the grand opening of Northside Marketplace on November 17, 2023, from 4-10 p.m. in the Northside Arts District. This unique venue, featuring over 40 vendors, offers a blend of established favorites like Rubber City Clothing and Dirty River Bicycle Works alongside emerging local businesses in the Made in Akron section. Shoppers can enjoy a spacious central lounge with nearby eateries and bars, perfect for a break and socializing. Developed by the Testa Companies with assistance from the Downtown Akron Partnership and the Knight Foundation, Northside Marketplace provides a low-risk platform for new and small businesses. Attendees can participate in a raffle for a gift basket containing items from all vendors or enter to win a weekend getaway including lodging, dining, and entertainment. Operating hours are Monday-Thursday from 4-8 p.m., Friday from 4-10 p.m., Saturday from 10 a.m. to 10 p.m., and Sunday from 10 a.m. to 6 p.m. Free parking is available on N. Main St. and Furnace St. For more details, visit the Northside Marketplace website.
Last week, with the generous support of the Freedom of Press Foundation, I traveled to Guantanamo during the peak of a mass hunger strike to visit the detention facility, accompanied by four other journalists. We toured the primary camps—5 and 6—and also saw Camp X-Ray, the detainee hospital, library, and food preparation areas, as well as observed the prisoners' morning prayer. Although the tour was meticulously planned, it was still highly informative. Military personnel emphasized how challenging and unappreciative the prisoners are, while the guards, despite enduring frequent "splashes" of feces and urine, have remained remarkably patient. Medical staff confirmed that no prisoner on hunger strike who has been tube-fed has complained about the procedure, which I detailed in an exclusive Al Jazeera report last week. We departed the island on the 100th day of the hunger strike; during our week-long visit, the number of prisoners refusing food increased by three, bringing the total to 103. According to the government's count, 30 prisoners are currently receiving tube feedings. A Guantanamo spokesperson, Navy Captain Robert Durand, informed me that the military will not negotiate with the prisoners to end their hunger strike. The military reviewed these photographs and, to protect sensitive areas, cropped some to hide surveillance cameras, guard towers, and other landmarks. The uncropped images are available on Flickr.

Oregon suffered its worst record in over a quarter-century last fall, yet a media outlet remains optimistic about the Ducks' prospects. Athlon Sports placed Oregon in its "very early" Top 25 ranking, released on Monday, at No. 21. New head coach Willie Taggart takes over with a promising young roster for his inaugural season in Eugene. Despite their recent losing streak, dating back to 2004, a swift turnaround seems likely. True freshman quarterback Justin Herbert threw for 1,936 yards and 19 touchdowns last season and is supported by talented players like running back Royce Freeman and wide receivers Darren Carrington and Charles Nelson. The offensive line, which underwent a youth movement last year, is expected to return four starters. Left tackle Tyrell Crosby is also back after recovering from an injury. While scoring shouldn't be an issue, the defense needs improvement to compete against Stanford and Washington in the Pac-12 North. Fortunately, Taggart recruited experienced coordinator Jim Leavitt from Colorado, and key defensive players like sophomore linebacker Troy Dye and graduate transfer Scott Pagano provide strength. Oregon's schedule also favors them by avoiding a matchup with USC and hosting games against Washington State and Utah. Notably, Taggart's former team, South Florida, was also ranked No. 24 by Athlon.
On August 21, 2014, Tom Winter reported for NBC News that Ferguson, Missouri, police did not prepare an incident report regarding the fatal shooting of 19-year-old Michael Brown, handing the case over to St. Louis County police almost immediately. Critics and media outlets had wondered why Ferguson police released an incident report from a previous robbery involving Brown but not one from the shooting. According to St. Louis County Prosecuting Attorney Robert P. McCulloch’s office, no such incident report existed for the shooting. Any reports from the St. Louis County police would remain confidential until the grand jury investigating the incident concluded its review. The grand jury, convened until mid-September, would decide if Officer Darren Wilson should be indicted. The prosecutor's office confirmed cooperation with the ongoing federal investigation into Brown’s death. The fatal shooting of Brown, an African American, by Wilson, a white officer, sparked protests in Ferguson lasting over a week. Tensions seemed to lessen, allowing Missouri Governor Jay Nixon to begin withdrawing National Guard troops deployed to maintain order.
On June 17 to July 4, 2011, George Clooney's Satellite Sentinel Project reported alarming findings in South Kordofan, Sudan, indicating a "systematic campaign of mass killings of civilians" in Kadugli. The project, which TIME first covered, used eyewitness testimonies and DigitalGlobe satellite images to identify potential mass graves and piles of bodies near Kadugli. Four eyewitnesses recounted how the Sudan Armed Forces and allied militias searched homes, killing civilians suspected of supporting southern Sudanese forces. The report detailed acts such as throat-slitting and burning homes with occupants inside. It also described mass graves excavated on June 8 by a yellow earth mover, located less than a mile south of the Tilo School in Kadugli. The graves measured approximately 26 meters in length and 5 meters in width. Green trucks were observed transporting around 100 bodies to the site. Some bodies were reportedly wrapped in white plastic before burial. The Satellite Sentinel Project provided evidence of these atrocities through satellite imagery.

Facebook will soon be launching an app on Apple TV for the first time, as announced today. The upcoming app will allow users to watch videos, with personalization features, and is set to debut shortly. In a recent blog post, Facebook detailed the new features of their video app for television, emphasizing that it offers a fresh way to view Facebook videos on a larger screen. With the app, users can watch videos from friends or followed Pages, top live streams from around the world, and receive recommendations based on their interests. Additionally, they can revisit saved videos for later viewing and rewatch content they have already seen, shared, or uploaded. Previously, Facebook recommended using AirPlay from the iOS app to watch videos on Apple TV. Now, the new app will provide a standalone option for enjoying videos on the big screen. Facebook plans to roll out its new video player on Apple TV, alongside Amazon Fire TV and Samsung Smart TV. Other upcoming video features include auto-play sound for videos, which will be enabled by default but can be turned off through settings if desired. Enhanced vertical video playback and picture-in-picture mode within the Facebook app are also in the works. While Android users will be able to use picture-in-picture even when the app is closed, iPad support remains unspecified.

She contends that while political leaders focus on climate change, pollution, and resource depletion, overpopulation is a more pressing and foundational problem. A bail hearing for Christina Noudga, the Toronto-area woman charged as an accessory after the fact in the death of Tim Bosma, will resume on Thursday in a Hamilton court. Noudga, 21, is the third person to face charges following the discovery of Bosma's remains on a Waterloo-area farm in 2013. Bosma, 32, was last seen by his wife when he went for a test drive of a pickup truck he had for sale. Identified as the girlfriend of Dellen Millard, 28, one of two men charged with first-degree murder in Bosma's death, Noudga appeared in court wearing leg shackles, a white sleeveless top, and high-heeled brown boots. Her parents and supporters watched as she entered the prisoner’s box with a smile. Despite discussions about evidence related to the Bosma case, a publication ban restricts media coverage of the proceedings, typical for bail hearings. Noudga was waved off by a group of supporters as she exited the courtroom at the end of the day. Bosma's family, including his father, Hank, was present, while his widow, Sharlene, was absent at the Crown's request. She is expected to testify during the trial as she was one of the last to see Bosma alive. According to Crown Attorney Anthony Leitch, the charge against Noudga pertains to an allegation that she attempted to assist Millard in escaping on May 9, 2013. Leitch did not provide further details. Millard and Mark Smich, 26, from Oakville, are both being held in jail, charged with first-degree murder in Bosma's death. Millard is also accused of first-degree murder in the 2012 deaths of his father and Laura Babcock, 23. Smich shares a charge of first-degree murder in Babcock's death. The police investigations into the deaths of Bosma, Babcock, and Millard's father are now managed by the Ontario Provincial Police through their major case management system, facilitating the sharing of valuable information across police forces.
Thanyarat Doksone, The Associated Press - On Monday, Thai police apprehended three local officials and a Myanmar citizen suspected of involvement in the trafficking and ransom-holding of Rohingya Muslims at a jungle camp in southern Thailand, where 26 bodies were found in shallow graves last week. National police chief General Somyot Poompanmoung stated that the suspects, including two deputy village chiefs and a municipal councillor, were part of a "transnational crime network" active for three to four years, spanning Thailand, Myanmar, and Malaysia. The recent discovery of the clandestine camp in southern Thailand, known as a trafficking hub for migrants, highlighted that despite authorities' assurances, little progress has been made in addressing the issue. This revelation further damaged Thailand's reputation, following recent disclosures of human trafficking linked to corrupt officials, according to rights groups. In June, the United States placed Thailand in its lowest tier for efforts against human trafficking. Thailand pledged to improve its standing, but its image was tarnished by recent reports of Thai fishing vessels employing forced labor or slavery. Somyot announced that police would continue their extensive search across Khao Kaew mountain in Songkla province and other densely forested areas to uncover any additional hidden camps. A single survivor, currently hospitalized due to severe malnutrition, reported that the traffickers had fled with about 100 Rohingya earlier in the week. Rohingya, a religious minority in predominantly Buddhist Myanmar, have faced state-sanctioned discrimination for decades, with mob attacks resulting in up to 280 deaths over the past three years, leading to one of the largest mass exoduses since the Vietnam War.
Dorothy, a devoted elderly fan of the Chicago Cubs, secured her front-row seats at Wrigley Field in 1984. She has remained there ever since, cheering on "my Cubbies." On Saturday night, she witnessed the Cubs defeat the Dodgers in Game 6 of the NLCS, securing the pennant. Ken Rosenthal spoke with Dorothy post-game and inquired about the significance of experiencing this moment in person. Dorothy remarked, "I just wish my brothers were here to see this. One was killed in the war, another was a prisoner in Germany for 21 months, and two others were overseas—they all loved the Cubs. My father did too, but they're all gone now. This old lady is still going strong." When asked about her plans for celebrating, Dorothy replied, "Who knows—I might have a Jagermeister." Truly, Dorothy, you are an American treasure and inspiration. Enjoy your interview.

The free movement of labor is crucial to both the European project and the stability of a monetary union. Drawing inspiration from this topic and the ongoing political discourse, we present four informative charts. Last month, Bruegel hosted an event examining migration within the EU and its societal impacts, as well as its role in fostering sustainable economic growth. The free movement of labor is a cornerstone of the European project and vital for the smooth operation of a monetary union. Guided by this theme and the current political dialogue, we introduce four informative charts. The first chart displays the net migration rate per 1000 inhabitants in Europe for 2012. Data source: Bruegel, based on Eurostat, most recent available data from 2012. This chart illustrates net migration rates, with green representing high net immigration and red indicating high net emigration. For instance, Germany and Belgium exhibit net inflows of 4.3 and 6.5 migrants per 1000 inhabitants, respectively, whereas Spain and Greece show net outflows of 3 and 4, respectively. The relationship between unemployment and net migration is further explored in the subsequent two charts. Note: Luxembourg was excluded as an outlier to maintain chart consistency. Data source: Bruegel, based on Eurostat. The first chart depicts the raw levels, while the second shows changes from 2007 to 2012 (most recent data available). Countries experiencing more severe economic downturns, characterized by higher unemployment rates, tend to see greater outflows of people and lower net migration. Generally, economically weaker countries experience larger net outflows, with migrants typically moving to countries in better economic condition. The final chart reveals the population distribution by country of citizenship within core European nations. The sender countries are located at the edges, while the host countries are in the center. Economic migration serves as a macroeconomic stabilizer, contributing to the formation of an optimal currency area, and offers numerous micro-level benefits, such as improving worker-firm matches, addressing skill shortages, and enhancing international trade through reduced cultural barriers.

He said this during debates preceding the French Republican Party primaries on November 3. According to Sarkozy, "There will be no resolution in the Middle East, especially in Syria, without Russia and Iran’s involvement." He also expressed concerns about the strengthening ties between the current French leadership and Sunni regimes in the region. The first round of internal Republican elections is set for November 30, with a potential second round on December 7 if no clear winner emerges. Seven candidates are competing, with Sarkozy, Alain Juppe, and Francois Fillon considered frontrunners. The French public will choose their next President in the spring of 2017.
A suicide attack by ISIS, a breakaway group from Iraq’s al-Qaeda, struck an Iraqi army base in eastern Fallujah on Sunday, resulting in at least 14 deaths. According to military sources, the attack targeted a base in the al-Harariyat village and also affected members of the Popular Mobilisation Forces, a Shia unit aiding the government in its fight against ISIS. Iraq faces its most severe security crisis since the 2011 US troop withdrawal, with ISIS controlling significant portions of northern and western Iraq, including Mosul and much of Anbar province. The group continues to carry out attacks on government forces and now holds approximately one-third of Iraq and parts of Syria under its declared "caliphate." Since ISIS’s emergence, there have been nearly daily attacks on Baghdad and other major cities, involving roadside bombs, suicide bombings, and assassinations that have caused significant civilian casualties and displaced tens of thousands of people.
Thorsten Jolitz suggests using Visual Studio's batch files to set necessary environment variables for interacting with the MSVS C++ compiler via the command line. He provides a sample `.bat` file named `vc2013.bat`, which sets these variables and then runs the specified arguments as commands. To use this from Emacs, one can invoke it with `M-x compile vc2013.bat <command>`. For beginners in C++, he offers advice on leveraging Emacs alongside Visual Studio, noting that most development work can be done within Emacs, except for occasional debugging sessions in the VS IDE. He also mentions the potential use of CMake to generate VC project files and makefiles, streamlining the build process. He acknowledges the challenges of integrating Emacs and Visual Studio teams but emphasizes that such coexistence is feasible, especially when focusing primarily on coding in Emacs and using Visual Studio mainly for debugging.
BACtrack, a company that produces portable breathalyzers and integrates them with smartphones for safety, recently shared data from nearly 300,000 breathalyzer tests conducted across the United States in 2014. Not surprisingly, the highest BAC levels were recorded on St. Patrick’s Day and New Year’s Eve. However, the data also revealed that the city with the highest average BAC in December was Waltham, Massachusetts. This report indicated that 14 of the top 15 drinking days of the year occurred in winter, with May 3rd being the sole exception due to its proximity to Cinco de Mayo. Waltham’s December BAC average of 0.133% topped those of Jersey City, New Jersey (0.132%), Champlin, Minnesota (0.124%), and New Orleans, Louisiana (0.123%). Despite these findings, the data suggests that Waltham might not actually be the drunkest city in America. Analyzing the sample size, even though BACtrack performed almost 300,000 tests, breaking down the numbers indicates that the sample size per state is relatively small—about 6,000 per state. Given Massachusetts’s 14th-largest population, the actual number of tests in Waltham would likely be much lower, possibly around 1,000 for the entire month of December. If Waltham’s 62,227 residents account for just a fraction of these tests, the sample size becomes even smaller. Assuming 20 tests in December, this still represents a very small sample. Moreover, individuals might use the breathalyzer multiple times over a single evening, further diluting the significance of the results. Thus, while Waltham may have shown high BAC readings, the broader context suggests these results are not representative of the entire city. The lesson here is to critically analyze data and consider the sample size and context when interpreting such findings. For those in Waltham or elsewhere, using a designated driver remains the safest approach to avoid any potential issues.

Attorney General Jeff Sessions was informed of Robert Mueller's appointment as special counsel only after the deputy attorney general, Rod Rosenstein, had signed the relevant letter. The Trump White House received just 30 minutes' notice before the announcement of Mueller's appointment. This sequence of events raises doubts about Jeff Sessions' ability to remain impartial in the Russia investigation. By ensuring Sessions was notified only after the letter was signed, the Department of Justice also prevented both Sessions and President Trump from interfering. These actions suggest that Sessions might be more than just a conflicted AG; he could potentially be a subject of the investigation himself.
California has taken a significant step toward hosting the third presidential primary in the nation, as the state Senate overwhelmingly approved Senate Bill 568 to move future primary votes to March. This bill, one of two under consideration this year, aims to shift California's primary from its current June date—among the latest in the nation—to an earlier March slot. Approved by a bipartisan 32-6 margin, the bill was authored by State Sen. Ricardo Lara (D-Bell Gardens), who argued that a March primary would give California more influence in national politics. "California leads the nation in clean energy, agriculture, job growth, and diversity," Lara stated in a written statement. "The Prime Time Primary Bill would position us as one of the first states to hold a presidential primary and ensure our voters' voices are heard in the national conversation."
In Little Rock, an Arkansas judge ruled that officials must recognize more than 500 same-sex marriages conducted in the state last year, allowing these couples to enjoy benefits such as joint tax filing. On June 9, Pulaski County Circuit Judge Wendell Griffen validated marriage licenses issued to same-sex couples following a previous judge’s decision to invalidate Arkansas’s ban on gay marriage. Although the Arkansas Supreme Court had temporarily halted the issuance of marriage licenses to same-sex couples in May 2014 and was considering an appeal against the voter-approved ban, Griffen's ruling enables couples to file taxes jointly, enroll together on state health insurance plans, appear on a child’s birth certificate as parents, or file for divorce. However, the state retains the right to appeal this ruling. For further details, visit the KTHV - Channel 11 website.

Should we add the following six keycaps in size 1 for 75% keyboards: PG Up (R2), PG Down (R3), End (R4), FN (R4), CTRL (R4), and ALT (R4)? This addition includes only six keycaps, but I believe many users have boards of this size. Alternatively, consider an extra extension set for 75% keyboards that includes these keycaps plus the Arrows (R4) and Win/CTRL/ALT on the left. The 75% keys will be part of the base set, as mentioned earlier. SKIDATA+ will follow the conventional Cherry 75% layout, which includes Home, PgUp, PgDn, and End. Regarding the arrows and Win/CTRL/ALT on the left, these keys will definitely be included in the base set, regardless of whether they are Winkeyless or Winkey versions. The base set will cover 1800, HHKB, 75%, and some additional keys, all in SKIDATA+ colors. You should not lack many keys from the base set. Rest assured, as a keyboard enthusiast, my goal has always been to provide a SKIDATA keyset for the community, ensuring enough keys for every conventional Cherry-style keyboard. Unfortunately, there are some unconventional keyboards like the Filco Minila that use unusual layouts, making it impractical to support them. The Vatican has directed the Catholic Church to be courteous to individuals with "homosexual tendencies" while continuing efforts to oppose equality. Documents released before the Church’s Family Synod dampened expectations that the Church would soften its stance against LGBT+ rights—despite concerns about becoming increasingly disconnected. Plans to engage with gay couples were shelved at last year’s Synod after a embarrassing reversal by the Pope. Although there are hopes such initiatives might resurface this year, the working paper for this year’s synod does not list reaching out to gay couples as a key topic. Still, the document urges respect for these individuals under a section titled “Pastoral care for persons with homosexual tendencies.” It states, “Each person, regardless of their sexual orientation, deserves respect and should be treated with sensitivity and delicacy both within the church and in society.” Additionally, “It would be beneficial for diocesan pastoral programs to specifically address the support of families and individuals with homosexual tendencies.” Despite recent public relations efforts to improve the Pope’s image among LGBT+ communities, he has not abolished the discriminative policies of his predecessors. He continues to oppose same-sex marriage, invited representatives from hate groups to a ‘traditional marriage’ conference, and recently exhorted Slovaks to oppose equal marriage. The Pope has also likened transgender individuals to nuclear weapons.

The delegation includes Lahore Commissioner Rashid Mehmood Langrial, Lahore Development Authority (LDA) Director-General Ahad Khan Cheema, LDA’s strategic policy unit chief Moazzam Sipra, and Mustafa Kamal Chaudhry, an urban infrastructure project consultant. Lawmakers in Louisiana are set to convene on January 21 to examine the "feasibility and effectiveness" of marijuana legalization. This meeting, initiated by State Representative Dalton Honore (D-Baton Rouge), comes amid existing harsh penalties for marijuana possession in the state. Currently, a first-time offense can result in up to six months in jail, escalating to five years and a $2,500 fine for a second offense, and a felony conviction with a mandatory 20-year sentence for a third offense. In the previous legislative session, efforts to mitigate these severe penalties were thwarted in the Senate. Representative Austin Badon (D-New Orleans) has reintroduced House Bill 14, which proposes capping jail time for a second offense at two years and fines at $500, with subsequent offenses limited to a maximum of five years and $2,000. Polls indicate that 53% of Louisiana voters support legalizing marijuana for adults aged 21 and older, with regulated sales.

The Environmental Molecular Sciences Laboratory (EMSL), a national scientific user facility, addresses energy and environmental challenges at the molecular level. Situated at the Pacific Northwest National Laboratory and funded by the Department of Energy’s Office of Science, EMSL supports both open and proprietary research. Each year, it collaborates with nearly 800 scientists from academia, government labs, and industry across almost all U.S. states and international locations to advance their research. EMSL offers in-house tools or allows researchers to design and construct their specialized instruments. Scientists utilize EMSL's advanced high-performance supercomputers, like Cascade, for various studies, including aerosol impacts and water purification. Recently, researchers leveraged EMSL’s unique capabilities, including the Chinook supercomputer, to investigate oceanic cloud types, crucial for climate modeling. Current climate models often simplify ocean clouds into either stratocumulus or cumulus types, covering vast areas. However, distinct cloud types have varying effects on solar energy reaching the sea surface, potentially introducing inaccuracies in large-scale climate models. The research confirmed this, showing that averaging one type of cloud underestimates ocean cloud cover, leading to an overestimation of solar energy reaching the ocean. Additionally, such models underestimate temperature variations and cloud layer movements, predicting faster transitions from stratocumulus to cumulus clouds and introducing uncertainties in climate projections. These insights from EMSL could enhance the accuracy of climate predictions.

Health Minister Peter Dutton on October 30, 2023, refused to rule out using a regulation to reduce Medicare rebates by $5, aiming for the $3.5 billion in savings proposed in the budget. The g2k16 hackathon was clearly very successful, as evidenced by this additional report from Patrick Wildt. He notes that they transitioned from OABI to EABI for armv7, which is now the standard expected by all ports. To facilitate this change, he prepared diffs and snapshots beforehand, integrating them during the event. This move led to the removal of the Zaurus platform due to the ABI incompatibility. As a result, they can focus on armv7 and leverage its benefits, such as the hardware floating-point unit. Meanwhile, jsg@ moved armv7 to PIE and static-PIE configurations, and improvements to C++ exceptions were noted. Next, they worked on incorporating LLVM and the new C++ stack into the project. Patrick imported libc++, libc++abi, and libunwind, while Pascal handled the LLVM import. They successfully completed these tasks before the hackathon concluded, setting the stage for further development. While the future looks promising, much work remains to be done.

After over a year of testing, YouTube will now allow users to enable the Material Design version on their desktop without needing a URL workaround. The redesign aims to bring the desktop experience closer to the mobile one, featuring a simpler layout that highlights content better. Key updates include infinite scrolling, an end-to-end user profile banner, and a larger hero video on the profile page. In theater mode, the search bar turns black to better match the screen. Dark Mode can be activated by clicking the user icon and adjusting settings. An image slider allows comparison between the Material Design and classic versions; the update includes more white space and a lighter color search bar. The preview is open to YouTubers worldwide but is initially limited to a small group. Once a significant portion opts in, the team will close the preview to gather user feedback. According to YouTube's Manuel Bronstein, the redesign will start with about 1% of users and gradually expand. If there's high demand, the team plans to speed up implementation. Users can opt in via YouTube.com/new and revert to the classic version if desired.

Manafort, formerly Trump’s campaign manager, and his associate Rick Gates face charges including conspiracy against the U.S., money laundering, acting as an unregistered foreign agent, and seven counts of failing to file reports of foreign bank and financial accounts. "This is a significant moment revealing how this document was hastily put together," she said, emphasizing that such errors should not occur in a serious investigation. The indictment mentions that Manafort and Gates lobbied members of Congress and their staff about Ukraine sanctions, the legitimacy of Ukraine elections, and the imprisonment of Yanukovych’s rival, Yulia Tymoshenko, who was actually Ukraine’s prime minister. Both Manafort and Gates earned tens of millions from their lobbying work in Ukraine. He was the first person charged and the first to plead guilty in Special Counsel Robert Mueller’s investigation into the Trump campaign’s alleged ties to Russia and Moscow’s interference in the 2016 election. This likely stems from Google's acquisition of GrandCentral in June 2007, with an official announcement and broader rollout expected soon.
The concluding phase of the 2016 Rio Olympics resembles a "Let's Make a Deal" scenario. With 100 million reais (US$32 million) in unpaid debts, the organizing committee is offering suppliers goods like air conditioners and electrical cables instead of or alongside cash payments. This cash shortfall stems from the financial downturn that struck Brazil as Olympic preparations began. According to Mario Andrada, Rio 2016’s communications head, the committee is proposing a 30% reduction in debt to creditors and aims to fulfill its obligations by June, when the organizing committee ceases operations. If this fails, the burden shifts to local and state governments that supported the committee’s financing, which are now also grappling with financial difficulties. Andrada noted that the state government, nearing bankruptcy, struggles to pay public employees. The committee is still awaiting sponsor payments and has downsized plans for the opening ceremony and other non-essential elements due to the economic crisis. This recession coincided with Brazil’s largest-ever corruption scandal, involving convictions of key business and political figures, including Olympic-related construction company executives and Rio’s former governor. Andrada mentioned that some furniture from the Athletes’ Village might be used by jailed officials, such as former police officers. Organizing the games cost around $2.8 billion, with the IOC contributing slightly over half before the scheduled payment, and local and national government promises falling short by 160 million reais. The local organizing committee will dissolve in June 2017. ©2017 Bloomberg L.P.
