Cheese curds may be giving way to gummy bears in Wisconsin. On Thursday, German gummy bear manufacturer Haribo announced plans to open its first U.S. factory in the state, specifically in Kenosha County. The facility is expected to create 400 jobs, as per Wisconsin Governor Scott Walker. Scheduled to commence operations in 2020, the project represents one of the largest foreign investments in Wisconsin's history, according to the governor's office. Walker praised Haribo's choice, noting the state’s business-friendly environment and fiscal stability. Construction is set to begin next year, with the first phase involving a capital investment of $242 million, as stated by Mark Maley, Wisconsin Economic Development Corporation’s Public Affairs and Communications Director. The 500,000 square foot plant will be the third-largest confectionery facility in the United States. Maley expressed excitement over Haribo’s selection, noting the company had been in talks with Wisconsin about the project for about six months. Known for products like Gold-Bears and gummy coca cola bottles, Haribo currently employs nearly 7,000 people worldwide across 16 manufacturing sites in 10 countries. Kenosha County Executive Jim Kreuser hailed the news, calling it a “sweet day” for the county.

The Volkswagen diesel emissions scandal has deepened, with the company now revealing that it detected "irregularities" in carbon dioxide emissions for approximately 800,000 cars in Europe. This number could be even higher globally. The original scandal centered on nitrous oxide (NOx) emissions, which are toxic pollutants from diesel engines, but can be reduced using methods like catalytic reduction with urea. Alternatively, VW cheated in emissions tests, which is cheaper in the short term but problematic in the long run if exposed. VW has identified potential issues with CO2 emissions in 1.4-liter diesel engines, primarily affecting the Polo and Golf models, along with some Audi, Seat, and Skoda vehicles. The company also suspects that some 1.4-liter petrol engines might be involved, though no further details are available. During internal investigations, VW discovered discrepancies between CO2 levels measured during certification and actual real-world driving conditions. A statement from VW noted, "Unexplained inconsistencies were found when determining Type Approval CO2 levels." Approximately 800,000 vehicles from the Volkswagen Group are reportedly affected. While fudging NOx emissions is concerning, CO2 irregularities could be more detrimental for VW because CO2 emissions are closely linked to fuel consumption. If the company falsely reported higher mileage and lower emissions, it could face significant regulatory fines. VW has already allocated €2 billion (£1.4 billion or $2.16 billion) for the CO2-related issues, which is four times the amount set aside for the NOx defeat device. Since announcing the CO2 irregularities, VW's share price has dropped by about 10 percent.

Early intervention when the draining is noticed offers the best chance for recovery.
You can book a wine-tasting trip to Washington state today, but in a few decades, due to rising temperatures, the region could gain almost 80,000 square miles of vineyard-friendly territory—much of which is currently inhabited by grizzly bears and wolves. According to Lee Hannah from Conservation International, climate change will make growing certain grape varieties more challenging in about 60% of California’s current vineyards. This shift will also impact wine-producing areas like the Mediterranean, South Africa, and Australia, while higher altitudes and latitudes, such as parts of New Zealand and northern Europe, will see improvements. Vineyards will likely adapt through methods like shadier trellising and planting heat-resistant varietals. Expect an increase in Zinfandel production, as it thrives in warmer conditions. Some areas will become less suitable for growing wine grapes, while others will become more favorable.

Chanel Dubofsky, a 37-year-old writer living in New York and Massachusetts, has always exhibited overachieving tendencies since childhood. Her mother's two cancer relapses, when Dubofsky was 13 and 17, intensified these behaviors. She remembers waking in the middle of the night with persistent headaches until she completed her homework. In high school, her friends participated in an informal competition about who slept the least, which she joined. Dubofsky's workaholism intensified during her college semester following her mother's passing. Despite her heavy course load of 20 credits and late nights, she maintained high grades, sometimes skipping morning classes due to fatigue, and only later informed her professors about her mother's death. Mental health research suggests that grief manifests differently, and unhealthy responses include extreme life changes or avoidance, but using work to cope can be beneficial if done moderately. Bryan Robinson, a psychotherapist, explains that overwork can be a mechanism to avoid unresolved emotions, especially in those with traumatic stress. A 29-year-old nonprofit worker, identified only by her profession, also describes work as a way to avoid thinking about her feelings. Rebekah Reysen, a researcher at The University of Mississippi, notes that overworking can serve both as a distraction and a means to escape. Journalist Nancy, collaborating with an abusive partner, channeled her emotional distress into her work to cope with her lack of self-care.
Texas Motor Speedway's president, Eddie Gossage, is peculiarly protective of NASCAR dates within Texas, especially after Austin's Circuit of the Americas (COTA) showed interest. Fort Worth and Austin, roughly 221 miles apart by car, would typically be in different states in a smaller jurisdiction. According to Autoweek, TMS has a regional protection clause in its five-year NASCAR contract. Gossage noted, "I don't blame them for wanting NASCAR races, but they're 20 years too late. They don't seem to understand the business." This attitude is absurd and rather dismissive. The distance between the tracks is significant, with most of the journey on the notoriously congested I-35. Comparing this situation to Homestead-Miami or Martinsville's concerns over distances seems apt. NASCAR races at TMS only twice a year, providing ample opportunity for a road course date at COTA. Such a date could attract new fans and potentially boost attendance at TMS. TMS has a strong 20-year relationship with NASCAR, positioning itself as a major client. Therefore, any race several hours away, like at COTA, should not interfere with TMS's schedule.
As of the latest police figures, more than 2,600 individuals remain missing in Japan three years after the country was struck by a major earthquake, tsunami, and nuclear disaster. Search efforts continue along extensive sections of the northeast coastline, where most of the 15,884 lives lost in the March 11, 2011, disaster were claimed by the tsunami. The figures were revealed as Japan marked the third anniversary of the disaster, its worst peacetime loss of life, with 2,636 people officially listed as missing, predominantly from the three hardest-hit prefectures: Miyagi, Iwate, and Fukushima. Additionally, 98 individuals' remains remain unidentified. Despite the clearing of debris and reopening of businesses, many communities still face challenges, particularly for families searching for their loved ones among the missing. Monthly searches on the 11th of each month are conducted by police, Maritime Safety Agency personnel, and local volunteers at the request of the missing's relatives. Yasuo Takamatsu, a 57-year-old bus driver from Onagawa, Miyagi, exemplifies this determination; he learned to scuba dive to search for his wife Yuko, who vanished during the tsunami. Yuko, a 47-year-old bank worker, was among 250 people still missing in Onagawa, where over 800 people perished in the 65-foot tsunami. Yasuo shared that his wife's final text read "I want to go home," and an unsent message on her phone stated "Tsunami huge." He expressed his desire to bring his wife home as soon as possible.

Marvel Comics has officially announced the end of the Luke Cage series. Writer David F. Walker confirmed via Twitter that February's Luke Cage #170 would be the final issue, stating, "Issue #170 is the last (and best) of the series. Oh well, on to other adventures. Thanks to everyone who supported the series." Walker elaborated on the reasons behind the cancellation, attributing it to poor sales and the reality that superhero success in film, television, and video games does not always translate to strong comic sales. He noted that only four out of the top ten best-selling comics in November sold more than 100,000 units, highlighting the challenging state of the comic book industry. Luke Cage joins other canceled titles such as Generation X, Hawkeye, Iceman, Jean Grey, and The Unbelievable Gwenpool. Secret Warriors and Defenders are also absent from Marvel's March 2018 solicitations, though their statuses are still unclear. Margaret Stohl assured fans that The Mighty Captain Marvel has not been canceled, while Mark Waid confirmed that Champions is not ending. The Guardians of the Galaxy series has also been canceled to make way for the Infinity Countdown series.
Less than half of Scots consider themselves well-informed about the independence issues and the 2014 referendum, according to research by the pro-independence campaign group Yes Scotland. A survey of over 1,000 people found that 46% felt adequately informed, with 47% of these planning to vote yes and 1% planning to vote no. The survey also showed that 74% of respondents were interested in the independence debate, while 10% were not. Additionally, 75% expressed high likelihood to vote, and 13% indicated a moderate likelihood. Blair Jenkins, CEO of Yes Scotland, stated, "These surveys, alongside other analyses, demonstrate that increased knowledge leads to greater support for independence. This reinforces our belief that continued efforts to communicate our message can yield positive results. With over a year until the referendum, the data suggests we are evenly matched with the No campaign among those already well-informed."

The Chief Rabbinate of Israel reported a 2% decrease in divorces in 2014, with 11,023 cases handled by batei din compared to 11,249 in 2013. Despite this decline, the number of divorces increased in Jerusalem and Tel Aviv, maintaining their top positions. Jerusalem had 874 divorces in 2014 versus 733 in 2013, while Tel Aviv saw 779 divorces in 2014 compared to 678 in 2013. Haifa ranked third with 629 divorces, followed by Petach Tikvah with 439, and Azor with 29. Overall, 89,551 divorce cases were initiated in the Rabbanut system in 2014, a slight decrease from 90,237 in 2013. Of these, 7,541 cases sought a couple's mutual consent for divorce, 969 involved shalom bayis, and the Rabbanut approved only 2.6% of them. Other cases included 3,437 for alimony, 3,341 for inheritance matters, and 2,501 for child custody. The unit for freeing agunos secured a get for 184 agunos in 2014, up from 159 in 2013. Batei din imposed sanctions on 40 recalcitrant husbands, resulting in 191 decisions and 184 husbands fleeing the country. Sanctions included liens on bank accounts, travel bans, and restrictions on employment and driving. The batei din issued 16 arrest warrants in 2014, down from 19 in 2013, and provided protective orders in 152 cases to safeguard wives from domestic violence, a slight increase from 140 in 2013. The average processing time for cases decreased from 96 days in 2013 to 56 days in 2014. The number of batei din cases referred to the civil judicial system also declined, with only 45 petitions filed against the batei din in 2014, of which 4 were accepted by the Supreme Court
In an innovative move to reduce energy bills and emissions, a German village named Dörentrup has turned mobile phones into remote controls for streetlights. This scheme, known as Dial4Light, allows residents to switch on the village’s lamps by calling a specific code displayed on lamp posts. Dörentrup, located 60 miles from Hanover, has piloted this initiative for a year across several streets, proving successful enough to be rolled out throughout the town and potentially beyond. With all 9,000 residents eligible to participate, the system enables users to activate lights for up to 15 minutes after dialing the relevant code. Mayor Friedrich Ehlert emphasized that while the primary goal is cost savings, the initiative also aims to foster greater community awareness about energy consumption. The project originated from the village council's earlier decision to turn off streetlights due to unaffordable electricity bills, prompting a resident to suggest on-demand lighting. The Lemgo county council, with expert assistance, patented a specialized modem and software to implement the system. Data indicates the scheme will cut annual CO2 emissions by nearly 20 tonnes—equivalent to 11 four-person households. Interest in Dial4Light has grown, with inquiries from various countries, and the system is set to launch internationally later this month.

The U.S. military acknowledged using depleted uranium (DU) ammunition in Syria, a controversial weapon linked to severe health issues. During strikes against alleged Daesh (ISIS) positions in late 2015, thousands of DU rounds were fired. Weapons experts contend that DU usage constitutes war crimes, crimes against humanity, and acts of genocide due to the significant health risks posed to civilians, including genetic damage, birth defects, cancer, and immune system impairment. On February 6, 2017, U.S. Central Command (CENTCOM) spokesperson Major Josh Jacques confirmed the use of DU. He stated, "Depleted uranium rounds, specifically Armor-Piercing Incendiary (DU), were employed to destroy the truck fleet ISIS was using to transport illicit oil." Jacques reported that 5,265 30mm DU rounds were fired on November 16 and 22, 2015, neutralizing around 250 vehicles. On November 16, about 1,490 of 1,790 rounds contained DU, and on November 22, nearly 3,775 out of 4,530 did. In 2003, DU was deployed in Iraq, leading to increased congenital birth defects, cancers, and other health problems in densely populated areas. The Iraqi government raised concerns about the harmful effects of DU. A 2014 UN report deemed DU weapons dangerous to humans and the environment, urging further investigation into their impacts. Iraqi medical professionals and international health scientists attribute new diseases, such as those affecting the kidneys, lungs, and liver, along with a surge in leukemia, renal failure, and anemia cases, particularly among children, to DU contamination.

Puya raimondii, commonly known as the queen of the Andes, reaches heights of up to 15 meters and is the largest bromeliad species. Native to the high Andes in Bolivia and Peru, this plant was first scientifically described in 1830 by Alcide d'Orbigny, who observed immature specimens in Bolivia. The species is named in honor of the 19th-century Italian botanist Antonio Raimondi, who documented it as Pourretia gigantea in his 1874 work. In 1928, Hermann Harms renamed it Puya raimondii. The queen of the Andes has a robust trunk that can grow up to 5 meters, with leaves up to 1.25 meters long and sharp spines reaching 1 centimeter. Its inflorescence can stretch from 4 to 8 meters, and a single plant can produce anywhere from 8,000 to 20,000 flowers over a three-month period. Its reproductive cycle typically spans about 80 years, but one specimen bloomed within 28 years when grown at sea level in California. This species thrives between 3,000 and 4,800 meters in elevation, growing in rocky and shrubby habitats. Puya raimondii is classified as endangered due to threats such as human-caused fires, climate change, and reduced genetic diversity.

In Didsbury, Alberta, the Mountain View Arts Society hosts the Annual Days of Yore festival at Rosebud Park. Spanning two days, the event features numerous historical reenactors, including sword fights, cannon demonstrations, and live combat. Attendees can explore the reenactment village, which includes the Sons of Fenrir Vikings and the Dragons Own Medieval Combat Group, among others. Verizon has consistently pursued Voice over LTE (VoLTE) as a high-tech alternative to traditional circuit-switched voice, conducting test calls as early as early 2011 with the LG Revolution. Initially, the company anticipated commercial availability in 2012, though a Northland Capital Markets analyst suggests that two trial markets are already operational, with a national rollout scheduled for 2013. Light Reading points out that this could still mean an initial commercial deployment this year, given Verizon's likely strategy of rolling out the service market by market. This aligns with the carrier's plan to overlay its entire 3G network with LTE in 2013. The significance of VoLTE lies in its IP-based nature, which necessitates the elimination of legacy calling services and the eventual refarming of spectrum. While this won't occur anytime soon, it is inevitable.

Blind gamers often feel overlooked, both visually and socially. When Brandon Cole, a blind gamer, suggested improvements to THQ’s Smackdown WWE wrestling games to enhance accessibility, he only received a generic thank you for appreciating the game's graphics. The invisibility of some characters in EverQuest II further complicates matters for visually impaired players. However, Alexander Stern, another visually impaired gamer, took a different approach: he filed a lawsuit against Sony, Sony Online Entertainment, and Sony Computer Entertainment America. The lawsuit accuses Sony of violating the Americans with Disabilities Act by neglecting to implement necessary accessibility features in its games. This act ensures that no individual with a disability should be discriminated against in the enjoyment of goods and services, including those provided by places of public accommodation. According to Stern, Sony did not respond to multiple requests for reasonable modifications to make its games more accessible. The suit calls for visual cues to help gamers with impaired visual processing find their way. It also highlights how other companies, like Blizzard with World of Warcraft, and Pin Interactive with Terraformers, have successfully incorporated accessibility aids. The lawsuit argues that Sony’s practices have cost visually impaired gamers, particularly those who miss out on the in-game auction market. "Sony has maintained its products in an inaccessible form and failed to address these issues despite repeated notifications of the discriminatory impact," as stated in the lawsuit. Sony representatives declined to comment on ongoing litigation.

After nearly eight centuries of blaming black rats for the bubonic plague, scientists now present strong evidence to clear these much-maligned rodents. Instead, they have identified gerbils as the likely culprits. As the saying goes, it's often the cutest ones we need to watch out for. A study published in the Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences supports this shift in perspective. Climate data from the 14th century contradicts the traditional view that European plague outbreaks originated from flea-infested rats. "Warm summers without excessive rainfall are necessary," explained Nils Christian Stenseth, a study author, in an interview with the BBC. "Our analysis of various climatic indicators shows no correlation between plague outbreaks and weather patterns." The "Black Death," as the epidemic was known, appears to be linked to climate conditions in central Asia. Tree-ring records spanning 15 years indicate that Europe experienced plague outbreaks whenever central Asia had a wet spring followed by a warm summer—conditions unsuitable for black rats but ideal for gerbils. These rodents, along with their flea-borne bacteria, likely traveled to Europe via the Silk Road, causing periodic epidemics that appeared and disappeared over the centuries, rather than persisting due to rat populations. This isn't the first challenge to the prevailing theory. Last year, researchers found evidence suggesting the plague could spread through the air, not just via flea bites. To validate their findings, Stenseth's team plans to examine genetic material from ancient European skeletons. If the genetic variations suggest new waves of the disease, it would confirm their hypothesis and require rewriting historical accounts. "If we're correct," Stenseth noted, "we'll need to revise that chapter of history."

In which Canadian city do your residents struggle the most with sleep? According to a new study by Sleep-Centre.ca and IPG Mediabrands, Kitchener tops the list of the most sleepless cities in Canada. Saskatoon and Vancouver share the second spot. The study revealed that 62% of Canadians face some form of sleep issues, with pain being the primary cause (50%), followed closely by room temperature (31%). Uncomfortable temperatures, linked to summer's heat and humidity, are surprisingly prevalent. Work stress, illness, snoring, and caffeine consumption are other factors contributing to poor sleep. The most common sleep remedies cited include changing sleeping positions, using the bathroom, screen time, and medication. The survey, which surveyed over 3,000 people, found that Toronto residents enjoy better sleep, likely due to a higher number of singles in the city. Kitchener, described as a tech-savvy community with many young families, tops the list. Sleep deprivation costs Canadian companies nearly $75 million annually in lost productivity. Loraine Cordery, insights and marketing manager for the study, emphasized the importance of adequate rest, noting that people often overlook the significance of a good night's sleep.

While the company is well-known for its involvement in Formula One and some engineering work for other automakers, it has also been active in electric racing. Specifically, Williams built the battery packs for Formula E until McLaren secured the new contract last year. However, Williams continued its electric vehicle initiatives and has raised $125 million to establish an EV battery factory in the UK. This factory will supply battery packs for Aston Martin’s upcoming all-electric RapidE. But Williams aims to expand its offerings beyond this project and today unveiled the FW-EVX, a new lightweight electric vehicle platform concept, to demonstrate their capabilities. The FW-EVX platform follows the skateboard-like design popularized by Tesla, which is now common in electric vehicles. While few details were provided, Williams highlighted several innovations in battery pack design, cooling systems, and lightweight structures. For example, the company has developed a highly automated process for creating fiber-reinforced suspension components, reducing weight by up to 40% compared to conventional aluminum wishbones. Another notable innovation is the use of 3D structures formed from 2D materials to create an exoskeleton for battery modules that also enhances structural performance. Paul McNamara, Williams Advanced Engineering's Technical Director, emphasized that these technologies could significantly improve the efficiency and competitiveness of future electric vehicles. Craig Wilson, the Managing Director, stated that this concept represents a new direction for Williams' advanced engineering business, aligning with the ongoing transition from internal combustion engines to fully electric vehicles.

Is this due to browser and operating system policies that mandate rejecting CAs that don't verify personal details? Or is there another reason why privacy-friendly CAs are scarce? Initially, I was intrigued by the fact that many Internet protocols, such as HTTP and SMTP, are purely text-based. At first glance, this seemed counterintuitive, as text is less efficient for machine interpretation compared to binary. However, I soon appreciated the wisdom behind this design. Text-based protocols allow for easy interaction via simple tools like telnet, especially given the Robustness Principle's prevalence in the network infrastructure. This capability is crucial for understanding how systems work, which is fundamental to using them effectively. Without this understanding, we often rely on higher-level abstractions that obscure the underlying complexity, leading to suboptimal solutions that don't address the real issues at hand. Looking at today's Web development landscape through this lens, particularly with the introduction of HTTP 2.0, which adds unnecessary complexity, highlights the importance of simplicity. REST, for instance, offers a straightforward approach that aligns with the core principles of the web, making it both powerful and easy to grasp. In contrast, SOAP, while nominally text-based, becomes excessively complex due to its focus on human readability, which is rarely achieved in practice. Debugging SOAP transactions is notoriously difficult, whereas older, simpler protocols like EDI remain preferable. Unfortunately, many developers overlook the significance of this simplicity, falling prey to obscurity and excessive abstraction, which hinder effective software development.

Throughout your life, people will offer advice—often repeatedly. Follow the rules, avoid risks, and strive to be a responsible citizen. While some advice comes from good intentions, others may suggest maintaining the status quo to ensure a stable future. The conventional path often includes studying hard, excelling academically, attending a reputable university, securing a steady job, climbing the corporate ladder, and having children while upgrading your home periodically. However, this is just one route among many. What if you chose to drop out of school and travel across the country? Or, perhaps you found that grades weren't essential and instead immersed yourself in fascinating literature? Volunteering in a developing country might lead you to meet someone with a completely different perspective on life. You could explore various tastes, sights, and challenges, gaining experiences and perhaps a few scars along the way. Life is precious; live it according to your desires, but also consider alternative paths. There's a vast difference between the numerous ways you can navigate life and the conventional paths most choose. Even if you veer off the beaten track, you'll likely have memorable stories to share. Do what you wish. I'm not dictating how you should live your life. Still, it's worth remembering that within a century, you and everyone you love will no longer exist. The worries and stresses of today will soon be forgotten. The tide of convention is powerful and overwhelming, but you have the power to decide otherwise.

SAN DIEGO (CNS) - A life-size replica of the San Salvador, the ship Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo sailed into San Diego Bay in 1542, arrived at a shipyard in Chula Vista on Wednesday ahead of its launch next month. The vessel, constructed by about 500 volunteers from the Maritime Museum of San Diego over four years at Spanish Landing Park, was originally slated to be moved to a barge on Sunday but was postponed due to poor weather. With improved conditions, the transfer to Marine Group Boat Works proceeded smoothly. Dr. Ray Ashley, CEO of the Maritime Museum of San Diego, declared, "Today marks a significant milestone for our museum, our volunteers, our donors, and the entire San Diego community and state of California. Recreating the San Salvador has been a decades-long endeavor." The San Salvador, designed to cruise along California’s coast as a floating classroom, mirrors the original in dimensions—weighing 150 tons and measuring 92 feet long by 24 feet wide. Its construction materials were sourced globally, including Angelique wood from Suriname, Sapele wood from Nigeria, Southern live oak from Georgia, and Douglas fir from the Pacific Northwest. San Diego Mayor Kevin Faulconer highlighted the ship’s significance, saying, "Every piece of the San Salvador reflects the dedication of those involved. We are grateful to the Maritime Museum for their commitment to building this vessel and providing educational opportunities for our residents and visitors alike." The San Salvador will be unveiled to the public during the Maritime Museum of San Diego’s Festival of Sail over Labor Day weekend.

As a gesture of gratitude, the guard's family treated the inmates to a free lunch at a local park.

She countered the notion that the BJP-led government had significantly reduced funding for basic science research. Irani highlighted two misconceptions: that no Indian institutions rank highly globally, and that substantial funding is essential for quality research. She emphasized, "More money doesn't equate to better science. A fusion experiment costing millions in Orange County can be replicated in Bengaluru with just 2 lakh rupees." Irani also mentioned that CNR Rao, among other scientists, had criticized the government for purportedly reducing funding for fundamental research. Lastly, she discussed the Global Initiative of Academic Networks (GIAN), which has expanded to include 22 state universities and plans to engage 1,000 foreign academics in teaching government institutions.
Marijuana spot prices have begun to increase gradually after a significant drop last year. Since 2015, Cannabis Benchmarks has tracked wholesale cannabis prices, observing a decline from an average of $1,953 per pound in 2015 to a low of $1,487 in 2016. In the first quarter of 2017, the average price rose to $1,613. Jonathan Rubin, from Cannabis Benchmarks, notes that the wholesale marijuana market behaves similarly to a typical commodity, with prices influenced by supply, which is tied to harvest schedules. The market receives products from three types of sources: indoor growers who can harvest four to six times a year, greenhouse growers who typically produce four harvests annually, and outdoor growers who have only one harvest usually in the fall. This timing leads to price fluctuations; as outdoor crops are depleted around August, prices spike, and then fall again when the large supply is released in the autumn. Rubin explains that outdoor growers often sell their stock in the fall to recoup funds before reducing sales and allowing prices to rise as they gradually bring more product to the market. Weather variations and regional challenges affect prices each year. The biggest drop in prices occurred at the start of 2016 due to increased supply from new and expanded capacities, along with improved cultivation and supply chain management, leading to a $365 per pound reduction or 19.7%. Prices tend to rise during holiday sales and 420 celebrations, increasing from an average of $1,487 in the fourth quarter of 2016 to $1,613 in the first quarter of 2017, marking a 17.4% year-over-year decline but sequential growth. Oregon’s market faced unique challenges with a testing backlog at the end of 2016 followed by a price spike ahead of full adult-use markets starting in January. Currently, there are no trading options for wholesale marijuana like other commodities, but Tradiv operates a marketplace matching cultivators with buyers. Rubin suggests the market is in a bust cycle, where declining prices allow larger, more efficient players to survive, reducing supply and driving prices back up. He predicts that lower wholesale prices and an influx of new growers could lead to market disruptions.

This aligns the business newspaper with thousands of other publications that now market their content through Apple's iTunes store, though Apple takes a 30% cut of sales and manages customer billing details. In the existing descendants of the pre-flood saurians, the crocodile and alligator serve as prototypes for the dragons and hydras of mythological lore. These reptiles, known as Crocodylus and Alligator respectively, are large amphibious creatures with tough, impenetrable scales, except underneath, and can grow up to twenty-five to thirty feet in length. Revered by ancient Egyptians, crocodiles primarily inhabit the Nile and similar river systems in India. Although cumbersome on land, they move swiftly through water, hunting fish—suitable prey—and posing a threat to dogs, other animals, and humans who venture into their territory. The crocodile is scientifically named Lacerta crocodilus, derived from the Greek κροκοδειλος (krokodeilos), a term of uncertain origin. The alligator, or American crocodile, gets its name from the Spanish "el lagarto," meaning lizard, with its Latin equivalent being lacertus or lacerta. According to Miss Millington in "Heraldry in History, Poetry and Romance," the dragon and crocodile were once conflated under a single name, as evidenced by Philip de Thaun in his "Bestiarus," who noted that "crocodille signifie diable en ceste vie" (crocodile signifies devil in this life). Guillim, an early heraldic scholar, commented that "dragons are naturally so hot that they cannot be cooled by drinking water but still gape for air to refresh themselves, as seen in Jeremiah xiv. 6." Young, in his "Night Thoughts," while describing the leviathan (crocodile) in a paraphrase of part of the Book of Job, observed that naturalists believed crocodiles, holding their breath underwater, would burst forth with a hot, fiery exhalation upon surfacing, contrasting this with the milder breathing patterns of horses.

Securing Canada and its borders remains a critical responsibility of the federal government. Thus, any policy that weakens security screening for asylum seekers is unacceptable. According to Sun Media columnist Candice Malcolm, who cited high-ranking former officials in the federal immigration department, the Trudeau government plans to expedite the processing of asylum seekers from countries with high approval rates for refugee claims. This could involve approving claims without hearings or through a streamlined paper-based process. While many asylum seekers from Middle Eastern and African nations, where Canada has historically recognized numerous refugees, may be legitimate, some pose significant security risks, including terrorists and war criminals. In response to Malcolm's report, federal officials stated that security and criminality screening practices would remain unchanged, though some claims might be approved without hearings. These concerns are not new; as highlighted by the Senate Standing Committee on National Security and Defence in its 2015 report, "Vigilance, Accountability and Security at Canada's Borders," there are ongoing worries about the adequacy of immigrant screening. The committee noted that between just 9% and 15% of immigrants undergo face-to-face interviews before coming to Canada. Former Ambassador Martin Collacott testified before the Senate committee, emphasizing that such interviews are crucial for assessing security risks and providing prospective immigrants with valuable information about integrating into Canadian society. Canada is a compassionate nation, yet it cannot afford to be overly trusting when determining who enters. The decision-making process must be rigorous, not arbitrary.
In the last two decades, globalization, digitization, and the Internet's rise have amplified the importance of intellectual property law in global policy discussions. Issues surrounding the control, licensing, use, and reuse of intellectual property are now part of a broader public conversation that extends beyond legal experts. As intellectual property law intersects with economics, culture, health, commerce, creativity, and intellectual freedom, there has been a surge in literature on these topics, authored not only by legal scholars but also by individuals from various disciplines. In 2012, the Centre for Law, Technology, and Society at the University of Ottawa organized a workshop aimed at gathering academics from diverse fields to foster interdisciplinary dialogue, promote collaborative research, and generate a body of work examining intellectual property law from an interdisciplinary perspective. This book compiles the papers presented at that workshop. Both paperback and ebook versions can be obtained from IRWIN LAW.

The Defense Logistics Agency destroyed 16 C-27A Spartan planes, originally purchased for the Afghan Air Force, at Kabul International Airport for just $32,000, after Afghan military personnel were unable to maintain them. These planes, which cost nearly $486 million, flew only 234 hours out of the required 4,500 between January and September 2012. The Defense Department scrapped the aircraft, leaving only four of the original 20 at Ramstein Air Force Base in Germany. The Special Inspector General for Afghanistan Reconstruction, John Sopko, has requested detailed documentation on the decision to destroy the planes and inquiries into whether the remaining aircraft should be sold instead of scrapped. He also seeks information on the disposal of non-scrapped parts, including engines and brass components, due to potential security concerns.

In the final weeks of 2011, several business stories managed to avoid the end-of-year spotlight, but the battle over the Stop Online Piracy Act (SOPA) could prove to be the most impactful development heading into 2012. Introduced in October by Texas Republican Lamar Smith, SOPA aims to tighten restrictions on the copying and sharing of copyrighted material online. However, opinions on SOPA are proving more nuanced than initially perceived. No entity has felt the effects of SOPA more acutely than GoDaddy, the internet domain registrar. Unlike tech giants like Google and Facebook, which publicly opposed SOPA due to its perceived overreach, GoDaddy supported the bill, prompting a massive grassroots backlash. By late December, a Reddit post suggested transferring domains away from GoDaddy, leading to a widespread movement against the company. The bill's provisions give broad authority to enforcement agencies, particularly the U.S. Department of Justice, to penalize alleged copyright infringement. This controversy was significant enough for GoDaddy CEO Warren Adelman to reverse the company's stance on SOPA. In a statement released on December 23, Adelman stated, "While fighting online piracy is crucial, we must work towards refining the legislation. We need the entire internet community to support it."

CLEVELAND, Ohio — Browns coach Hue Jackson is establishing a foundation named after him to combat human trafficking in Cleveland and its surrounding areas. Jackson, who recently joined Jay Z’s Roc Nation, will officially launch the Hue Jackson Foundation on July 20 at the Browns’ facility in Berea. The foundation aims to empower children, teenagers, and adult victims of human trafficking by funding organizations that support and advocate for those exploited. Jackson and his wife Michelle, parents of three daughters, created the foundation “for reasons close to their hearts,” with a commitment to supporting nonprofits that offer hope and empowerment to victims of sexual exploitation and coercion. Ohio ranks among the states with the highest incidences of human trafficking, according to data from the National Human Trafficking Resource Center in Washington, D.C. The foundation will concentrate on raising awareness, preventing human trafficking, and providing healing for its victims. These victims, the release notes, are often subjected to violence, physical and emotional coercion, fraud, debt bondage, and other tactics used by traffickers to subjugate and exploit them for both sex and labor. Victims can be of any age, gender, race, or ethnicity, and trafficking occurs in various settings across different socioeconomic backgrounds. Besides Jackson, the event will feature Ohio Attorney General Mike DeWine, Renee Jones from the Renee Jones Empowerment Center, and Major Lurlene-Kay M. Johnson of The Salvation Army.

In our recent Volca Vibes episode, we explored the Retrokits RK002 active MIDI cable and the Volca Sample. We were impressed by the microprocessor in the Retrokits cable, which allows you to play Volca Sample samples chromatically and access all 10 samples from a standard keyboard. This is achieved through real-time processing of incoming MIDI signals using firmware within the cable. Now, Retrokits has addressed a limitation we found in the Volca FM—specifically, its lack of velocity response over MIDI, which is crucial for capturing the dynamics of DX FM sounds. While you can adjust velocity using a velocity fader and include it in a Motion Sequence, Retrokits has developed new firmware for their cable to map velocity in real-time. The update process involves loading a .MID file onto the cable and using Chrome’s Web MIDI functionality in your browser. All you need is a connected MIDI interface with the cable plugged in. And it works effectively.
The 'High Five Friday' program, which involved police officers greeting students with high-fives each Friday morning, has been suspended at Northampton's elementary schools amid community concerns. Following the program's introduction in December, local police consulted with the school district’s superintendent. While the initiative garnered support, some community members expressed worries, particularly about potential discomfort among minority students, undocumented children, or those with past negative interactions with law enforcement. After discussions, the police chief and school superintendent decided to halt the program. In a Facebook update, the department acknowledged that while the officers enjoyed interacting with the children, "we cannot ignore how this program might be perceived differently by certain members of our community. Our primary goal is for kids to approach school with enthusiasm and readiness to learn." Reactions to the program’s discontinuation have been mixed; some residents are concerned about student safety and suggest alternative activities, while others praise the police department's community engagement efforts. No new program has yet been announced, but the police are optimistic about developing a new initiative with the school district.

She added that while some may find it politically advantageous to misstate facts or make unfounded accusations in the short term, she believes it is detrimental. "We must adhere to the truth in politics," Sinema emphasized. "The facts she cites, both now and previously, are incorrect." UPDATE (6/2/15): Today’s hearing will be broadcast live on the House Judiciary Committee’s website. WASHINGTON, June 1, 2015—Tomorrow, Foundation for Individual Rights in Education (FIRE) President and CEO Greg Lukianoff will present to the U.S. House of Representatives Subcommittee on the Constitution and Civil Justice on the current state of free speech on America’s public college campuses. Joining him will be Wendy Kaminer, an attorney and author; Kim Colby, director of the Christian Legal Society’s Center for Law and Religious Freedom; and Jamie Raskin, a professor at American University’s Washington College of Law. The hearing will commence at 2 p.m. ET in Room 2141 of the Rayburn House Office Building. “I commend the Subcommittee on the Constitution and Civil Justice for convening this hearing to highlight the critical issue of censorship on today’s public college campuses, and I am privileged to offer my testimony,” stated Lukianoff. In his remarks, Lukianoff will delve into why many public colleges and universities maintain speech codes that violate constitutional principles and the detrimental impact these codes have on students, who frequently attempt to suppress speech they find objectionable. His testimony will also scrutinize threats to faculty speech and the ambiguity surrounding the Supreme Court’s 2006 Garcetti v. Ceballos ruling regarding faculty expression. Lukianoff has previously testified on free speech issues. Last July, he appeared before the United States Commission on Civil Rights to discuss how the federal government’s interpretation of Title IX endangers student and faculty expression. In 2003, he testified before the U.S. Senate’s Health, Education, Labor, and Pensions Committee about university speech codes and free speech zones and their effects on campus discourse. “Protecting free speech on campus remains a priority for Congress,” said Lukianoff. “I hope lawmakers will take decisive steps to safeguard the First Amendment rights of students and faculty at our nation’s public institutions. FIRE is prepared to collaborate with legislators to ensure that our campuses remain vibrant forums for diverse ideas.” FIRE is a nonprofit organization that brings together civil rights and civil liberties advocates, scholars, journalists, and public intellectuals from across the political spectrum to defend individual rights, free expression, academic freedom, due process, and freedom of conscience at America’s colleges and universities. More information on FIRE’s efforts to uphold these values can be found at thefire.org. Contact: Katie Barrows, Communications Coordinator, FIRE

The Saudi Arabian government has warned it might sell off trillions of dollars' worth of American assets if the U.S. Congress passes a bill that could hold the kingdom accountable for potential involvement in the 9/11 attacks, according to The New York Times. Last month, Saudi Foreign Minister Adel al-Jubeir informed U.S. lawmakers that "Saudi Arabia would be compelled to sell up to $750 billion in Treasury securities and other assets in the U.S. before any risk of asset freezing by American courts." The bill, which recently cleared the Senate Judiciary Committee, aims to remove diplomatic immunity for foreign governments in cases involving terrorist attacks that result in American fatalities on U.S. soil. Administration officials and congressional aides told The New York Times that intense discussions about the Saudi threats have occurred in recent weeks among politicians and representatives from the State Department and the Pentagon. The Obama administration has also sought to prevent the bill's passage. The State Department stated its unwavering support for the victims of such violent acts and their families, asserting, "We remain dedicated to bringing terrorists and those who use terrorism to justice."

This 1969 Lotus Europa was stored in a garage for 30 years before the seller acquired it. During the seller's two-year ownership, the car underwent a full restoration, including the use of nearly $1,000 worth of penetrating oil. Apart from some fasteners and carpet, the vehicle is claimed to be in complete condition. You can find it listed on Craigslist in Rocky Top, Tennessee for $3,500 or trade it for other listed vehicles. Thanks to BaT reader Spike M. for the submission. Limited body angles are available, but both the fiberglass and paint show no visible cracks. After a wash, the paint might look quite good. All trim, wheels, and windows appear to be present. The seats, steering wheel, and other interior accessories are not visible but should be included in the claim of completeness. New carpet has been installed, and while the dash shows signs of damage, it may require replacement. The Renault four-cylinder engine, which was seized and partially disassembled, offers potential for reuse or swapping. The chassis has been stripped and primed, and suspension components have been media blasted and powder coated, with all bushings being new. Although these vehicles are often found as affordable projects, this particular example stands out due to its completed restoration. With an additional $3,500, it could very well become a roadworthy vehicle.

Glide 0.11.0 introduces several enhancements to simplify working with dependencies and versions. Notable features include: - **Test Imports**: Glide now automatically resolves and adds missing test imports to the `testImports` section of the `glide.yaml` file. You can manage this section manually or opt to have new dependencies added via the `glide get` command with a specific flag. - **Config Wizard**: A new configuration wizard assists in determining semantic versions and version ranges for dependencies within the `glide.yaml` file. It can be run independently or following `glide init`, providing flexible guidance through an interactive process. - **Easier Release Installations**: Additional installation methods have been introduced. Besides downloading the binary or using Homebrew, you can now use a shell script provided on the Glide website for installation into your `$GOPATH/bin` or `$GOBIN`. Alternatively, a PPA maintained by Francisco Guimarães allows installation via package managers, as demonstrated by the commands: ``` $ sudo add-apt-repository ppa:masterminds/glide && sudo apt-get update $ sudo apt-get install glide ``` - **More Additions**: This version includes 10 new additions and 12 modifications. Detailed information on all changes is available in the updated release notes, which offer greater depth compared to previous versions.
Excessive internet use can contribute to school burnout, which in turn might lead to more internet use or digital addiction. A longitudinal study called Mind the Gap, funded by the Academy of Finland, has linked digital addiction and school burnout among both middle and high school students. Published in May 2016 in the Journal of Youth and Adolescence, the Finnish study found that school burnout can eventually result in depression due to adolescents' excessive internet use. Digital addiction is more likely when adolescents lose interest in school and feel cynical about it. To address these issues, fostering a love for learning is crucial. The research indicates that the most critical period to tackle digital addiction and school burnout is between ages 13 and 15. Supporting adolescents' mental health and reducing excessive internet use can be achieved by enhancing school engagement, boosting their motivation to learn, and preventing school burnout. Girls tend to experience higher levels of depressive symptoms and school burnout compared to boys, while boys are more prone to excessive internet use. The study involved over 3,000 Helsinki adolescents from 51 educational institutions. This Academy-funded project is the first to explore the reciprocal relationship between excessive internet use, school engagement, school burnout, and depression among adolescents. Today's youth are often referred to as 'digital natives,' having grown up with mobile devices and social media. The digital transformation has both positive and negative aspects; it offers valuable social experiences and educational tools but can also lead to burnout and depression in adolescents.
While Nevada isn't scheduled to begin selling recreational marijuana until mid-2018, State Senator Tick Segerblom is preparing a bill to be submitted at the start of the legislative session. This bill aims to allow Nevada's medical marijuana dispensaries to sell recreational products temporarily, pending the establishment of a full retail system. Following the passage of Question 2, marijuana use became legal in Nevada starting January 3, 2018, but consumers will still rely on the black market until regulations are finalized, a process expected to take at least a year. Inspired by Oregon’s approach, Segerblom intends to expedite legal access through the medical marijuana market. He believes this can help reduce the black market and maximize tax revenues, estimating potential tax earnings from the initiative to be nearly $100 million. Unlike other states that have legalized recreational marijuana, only Oregon has enacted a plan enabling early retail sales, a strategy Segerblom hopes Nevada will adopt. If successful, Nevada’s medical dispensaries could begin selling recreational marijuana to adults by fall 2017.

President Donald Trump is set to issue a broad anti-climate executive order to overturn significant regulations introduced by the Obama administration, according to the Washington Post. The order will direct Cabinet members to revise rules on carbon emissions from both new and existing power plants, revoke a coal leasing ban, and adjust how climate change is considered in federal decision-making—key components of the Obama administration’s climate strategy. Under pressure to act swiftly, due to an ongoing lawsuit contesting the Environmental Protection Agency’s (EPA) carbon emission limits, the administration aims to release the order soon. The EPA’s rule sought to reduce emissions by one-third by 2030. Climate scientists have warned that rising carbon dioxide levels are irreversible, with NOAA data showing a record-breaking increase in atmospheric CO2 concentration to 405 parts per million. This surpasses the symbolic 400 ppm threshold. Recent studies highlight the urgent need for climate action, revealing that the Amazon rainforest is entering a “death spiral” due to drought and deforestation, the Great Barrier Reef is experiencing severe bleaching, and Australia’s mangroves are dying from lack of water. Meanwhile, a climate-driven late-season blizzard is moving across the U.S. East Coast, and global sea ice is melting to its lowest levels in millennia. Research indicates that even if nations meet their international climate goals, the Arctic could become ice-free in summer. Scientists attribute these changes directly to human activities, as they urged EPA head Scott Pruitt to acknowledge the link between increased CO2 levels and climate change.

Defense Secretary Delfin Lorenzana stated on Tuesday that President Duterte had approved the construction of temporary military facilities under the Enhanced Defense Cooperation Agreement (Edca) after mutual agreement with the United States. The Edca, which was deemed constitutional by the Supreme Court last year, bolstered the military pact between the two nations under the 1951 Mutual Defense Treaty. During a press briefing at Malacañang, Lorenzana clarified that the President had been misinformed about American soldiers importing war materials in Palawan, Pampanga, and Cagayan de Oro City. He explained that no Edca camp constructions had taken place yet and that the agreement did not permit stockpiling of weapons or items for war games. The defense secretary noted that the U.S. equipment mainly consisted of supplies for humanitarian aid and disaster response, like rubber boats, which would be strategically placed across the country to facilitate immediate assistance during emergencies. Lorenzana also recounted that he sought the President's permission to proceed with Edca construction, to which the President responded, "Okay, let's allow it, but ensure there's no stockpiling of ammunition."
At the beginning of the year, concerns abounded about a potential trade war between China and the U.S., driven by Trump's aggressive stance on the U.S. trade deficit with China. These worries have since subsided as the status quo has remained intact, with trade continuing as usual. However, one year later, signs suggest that tensions might be escalating again. The Financial Times reported that the Trump administration has shelved its key strategy to strengthen economic ties with China, citing complaints about the growing trade imbalance and indicating that China's efforts to liberalize its economy have regressed. This decision, as revealed in an interview with David Malpass, a senior economic diplomat and undersecretary for international affairs at the U.S. Treasury Department, marks the end of the Comprehensive Economic Dialogue (CED) with Beijing, which has seen no meaningful progress since its last meeting in July. The sudden shift in relations is peculiar given Trump's ongoing efforts to pressure China to address North Korea's nuclear and missile programs. Simultaneously, the White House is adopting a more adversarial approach, opposing China's bid for market economy status within the World Trade Organization. Malpass emphasized that the CED was meant to advance market liberalization and economic dialogue but has now come to a halt because China is not moving toward a market-oriented path. He stated, "Without changes in China's economic practices to align with global rules, the CED remains stalled," and added, "There is no plan to restart the dialogue." For now, China is likely to respond with occasional angry editorials in the Global Times. A formal Chinese reaction is expected only if Trump implements additional tariffs on Chinese imports. Whether a full-scale trade war would significantly affect market trends remains uncertain.
The largest medical cannabis dispensary in the U.S., known as the "marijuana superstore," has been released from a long-standing legal conflict with federal authorities over medical marijuana. After a four-year legal battle, federal prosecutors have withdrawn their action to shut down Harborside Health Center's Oakland and San Jose locations. Steve DeAngelo, the executive director of Harborside, celebrated this as a sign of the end of federal prohibition. Despite federal laws classifying marijuana as a Schedule I drug, California legalized medical marijuana in 1996. In 2012, U.S. Attorney Melinda Haag targeted Harborside as part of a crackdown on what she saw as illegal pot suppliers. However, Harborside and its supporters argue that the center provides compassionate care to patients while generating significant tax revenue for the city. Opened in 2006, Harborside, which occupies 8,000 square feet, serves over 1,000 people daily at its Oakland location and employs 150 people. Last year, the Oakland store alone generated $28 million, making it the city's second-largest retail taxpayer. Oakland officials preferred regulating and taxing the cannabis industry rather than driving it underground.
This would create the world's first cashless society if fully implemented. A special committee, led by Harel Locker, Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu’s chief of staff, has proposed a three-phase plan to virtually eliminate cash transactions in Israel. Currently, about 20% of Israel's national budget is lost annually due to tax evasion and money laundering, and the aim is to recover as much as possible. Reuters reports that the government panel, chaired by Locker, presented its interim recommendations on transforming Israel into a cashless society on Monday. The plan includes reducing the initial cash transaction limit for businesses to 7,500 shekels (from the current 20,000 shekels) and lowering it further to 5,000 shekels after a year. Private citizens would be allowed cash transactions up to 15,000 shekels. Checks would also face restrictions. To facilitate this shift, the panel suggested issuing debit cards instead of credit cards, as these involve lower costs. Locker believes most citizens will comply with the new rules, as violations would be considered crimes and most transactions are under 5,000 shekels. The committee outlined the following short-term guidelines: - Business transactions in cash or by check should be limited to 7,500 shekels immediately, and reduced to 5,000 shekels one year after the legislation is passed; - Private transactions should be capped at 15,000 shekels; - Violations of these limits would be treated as criminal offenses with significant fines. The new regulations are expected to take effect by the end of 2014.
A longstanding White House practice involves a division of labor between a chief of staff, responsible for ensuring smooth administrative operations, and a political adviser who advises the president on the electoral impact of policies. This dynamic is not new, yet President-elect Donald Trump’s decision to establish dual lines of authority, with Reince Priebus as chief of staff and Stephen K. Bannon as "chief strategist and senior counselor," stands out. Bannon's selection is particularly noteworthy due to his ties to the alt-right, a previously marginal conservative faction that has gained prominence through Trump’s campaign. At Breitbart News, which Bannon oversees, the alt-right presents itself as a middle-class movement against perceived corruption, though it is more accurately characterized as a reactionist group rooted in white chauvinism, with troubling anti-Semitic undertones evident in Breitbart’s content. Bannon’s appointment sends a negative message to those who did not vote for Trump but still respected the outcome of the election. It risks exacerbating divisions rather than fostering unity among the disaffected half of the country. Given Bannon’s extreme views and past efforts to challenge Republican leadership, his inclusion within the establishment may prove contentious. Republican leaders hope Priebus can guide Trump towards mainstream policies and rein in Bannon, though Priebus and others have struggled to curb Trump’s more controversial actions. More robust measures will likely be necessary to counter the intolerant forces now entering the White House.
Minecraft developer Mojang's upcoming game, Scrolls, will require an initial payment followed by additional charges for more content. Markus "Notch" Persson explained that players can start for free after the initial cost, which covers a lifetime subscription to new scrolls released periodically. Additional scrolls can also be obtained through participation in ranked tournaments and other activities. Notch clarified that while the game includes elements of a freemium model, it won't be labeled as such due to its non-free nature. The game is a fantasy-based collectible card game and has been involved in a high-profile trademark dispute with Bethesda. Notch expressed skepticism about the freemium model, arguing that it often exploits players to maximize profits, turning games into mechanisms for continuous spending rather than enjoyable experiences. He stated that he is comfortable with paying for certain game enhancements but believes that most game developers advocating for freemium models are motivated by financial gain rather than player satisfaction.

South Carolina has joined other states in restricting local efforts to establish their own broadband networks. A recently passed bill significantly hinders the creation of municipally owned ISPs capable of delivering at least 190Kbps. Opponents argue that this legislation, pending the governor's signature, aims to shield large carriers such as AT&T from competition. In North Carolina, Time Warner Cable had previously engaged in a lengthy legal dispute to halt a municipal broadband network offering superior speeds. Critics also suggest that the bill was drafted and promoted by ALEC, a conservative think tank with AT&T as a board member. Proponents contend that local broadband initiatives, which may benefit from tax funding, could undermine free-market principles and limit government intervention. While recent stimulus packages have supported broadband expansion through public-private partnerships, the U.S. still trails in overall broadband speed and accessibility, making such restrictions potentially detrimental.

Speaker John Boehner believes the resolution—effective 15 days after adoption—could harm the NATO mission against Muammar Qaddafi, according to Politico. The resolution becomes eligible for a vote next week, following the upcoming congressional recess. House Republicans plan a special meeting on Thursday to decide their next move, possibly rescheduling the vote for later, when its passage seems less likely.

On a cool Friday afternoon, about a month before the 45th president was set to move into the White House, I visited President Lincoln's Cottage, a stucco villa located on a 250-acre tract that has been a home for retired military personnel since the 1850s. Situated high above much of the city, the site now serves as a quiet and evocative retreat from Washington’s daily political drama. Open to the public since 2008, the cottage stands tall and simple, reminiscent of Lincoln, who drafted the Emancipation Proclamation here amid the sound of cannon fire. Each morning, he would travel the three miles to the White House on horseback or in a carriage, passing through the city's wartime landscape, which included wagons full of wounded soldiers, graves being dug at the first national cemetery, and the voices of freed slaves singing spirituals. This journey reinforced the immense responsibilities of his presidency. Although Lincoln's Cottage is just a few miles from where I live, I had only recently discovered its significance. After moving to Washington in 2005 to write about President George W. Bush, my first visit to the White House left me impressed by the understated nature of the West Wing.

TRIPOLI (Reuters) - A tanker previously used by Libya's eastern government to defy the Western-backed administration in Tripoli returned to the country on Saturday, after being blacklisted by the United Nations, the state oil company announced. The eastern government's oil company had aimed to sell the 650,000-barrel cargo, but the UN measure mandated a ban on the tanker's entry into any port. Since 2014, two competing governments, one in Tripoli and one in the east, each supported by armed factions, have vied for control of Libya, an OPEC member. The eastern administration established its own National Oil Corporation alongside the Tripoli-based NOC. A UN-backed unity government, aiming to replace the rival administrations, arrived in Tripoli last month and seeks to exert authority nationwide. Western powers worry that any independent crude exports by the eastern NOC could weaken the Tripoli government and deepen regional divisions. "This incident serves as a clear warning to all ship owners and trading companies that oil exports from Libya by any entity other than the National Oil Corporation of Libya are illegal and will be halted," NOC Chairman Mustafa Sanalla stated. "Those behind this attempt risked splitting the country with their reckless actions." The Distya Ameya tanker departed Marsa el-Hariga port on Monday, was blacklisted on Wednesday, and headed to Zawiya port in western Libya. Sanalla indicated the tanker would offload soon, pending favorable weather conditions. The eastern NOC asserts legitimacy from the government and parliament in eastern Libya, which gained international recognition after armed opponents seized Tripoli in 2014. The new UN-backed unity government, which aims to resolve the conflict, encounters resistance from hardliners in both factions, whose rivalries intensified following the 2011 uprising against Muammar Gaddafi. A UN Security Council resolution last month affirmed the unity government's primary responsibility for preventing illicit oil sales, urging it to inform the UN committee overseeing Libya-related sanctions of any such attempts.

Spirit Lake faces the risk of overflowing due to a narrowing tunnel built after the 1980 Mount St. Helens eruption. This tunnel, crucial for draining the lake, has seen its opening shrink from eight feet, six inches in October 2013 to just six feet, eight inches by April 2015. Experts attribute this to shifting rock formations beneath the tunnel. If the tunnel fails, it could flood the lake, potentially inundating Interstate 5 and disrupting critical transportation routes in Washington state. The U.S. Army Corps of Engineers is developing plans for emergency repairs and has received support from local senators and representatives who emphasize the potential catastrophic impact.

SINGAPORE - With Singapore's rail system expanding and becoming more complex, there is a growing need for additional rail engineering talent, according to representatives from SMRT's technical advisory panel. Formed in 2013 to bolster SMRT's engineering capabilities, the nine-member panel, which includes experts from Hong Kong MTR and London Underground, discussed training more rail professionals and enhancing SMRT's in-house engineering expertise. Nanyang Technological University's Alfred Huan, who chairs the panel, noted that SMRT Trains now employs over 400 engineers, a 96% increase since 2014. SMRT's Chief Technology Officer, Ng Bor Kiat, emphasized the importance of nurturing these professionals to maximize capacity and capability for operating an expanded train network. Kristin Wood from the Singapore University of Technology and Design highlighted the necessity for SMRT to develop its own engineering skills rather than relying solely on external vendors. She stated that engineers should possess both deep technical expertise and a comprehensive understanding of all aspects of rail engineering. Chua Kee Chaing, Dean of Engineering at the National University of Singapore, underscored the criticality of this deep expertise in managing a complex system. He also pointed out that hiring many young engineers is a positive development. To ensure the transfer of knowledge to the rail network, engineering students need to be encouraged to work with the two local rail operators and the Land Transport Authority, suggested See Kye Yak, Director of the SMRT-NTU Smart Urban Rail Corporate Laboratory. The panel also addressed the use of condition monitoring devices and data analytics to enhance predictive maintenance. Lee Kang Kuen from Hong Kong Polytechnic University noted that initial delays during the new signaling system's testing were typical for such upgrades. Clive Roberts from the Birmingham Centre for Railway Research and Education proposed that closing down a line for extended maintenance could expedite project completion, citing the Victoria Line's example on the London Underground. However, this option may not be feasible in Singapore due to the MRT lines' critical role in transportation.

In many states, a significant hurdle in prosecuting rape and sexual assault cases is statutory limitations on when charges can be filed. Across the country, 34 states and Washington, D.C., have statutes of limitations ranging from 3 to 30 years. For example, in New Hampshire, charges must be brought within six years, while in Connecticut, the deadline is five years, and in Minnesota, it's just three. Some states link these limitations to reporting deadlines. In Illinois, if a survivor reports within three years, the state has ten years to file charges, but this period resets if reporting is delayed. Twenty-seven states allow extensions or suspensions of these limitations if DNA evidence can identify a suspect, though the specifics vary widely. In Georgia, there is no time limit for rape cases with a DNA match, whereas in Indiana, charges must be filed within a year of a DNA match, and in Connecticut, the initial report must be made within five years for any future DNA evidence to be considered.
American farm incomes have declined for four consecutive years, leading to the bankruptcy filing of one of North Dakota's largest high-value crop farms. McMartin Farms (McM Inc.), based just 30 miles south of the Canada-US border in St. Thomas, voluntarily filed for Chapter 7 bankruptcy in Fargo on February 10. McM Inc. was a major player in sugar beet, potato, and dry bean cultivation, employing over 150 workers annually. In 2016, the farm operated on about 39,000 acres, including 2,000 acres of sugar beets and over 4,000 acres of potatoes, according to Agweek magazine. This was a significant reduction from the 59,000 acres it managed in 2012. Speculation about the farm's financial health emerged last year, prompting Agweek to feature its president, Ron McMartin Jr., who acknowledged the challenges faced by farmers in the Red River Valley. The first creditors' meeting is set for March 16 in Grand Forks. Despite the trend of larger farms, profitability often hinges on factors beyond mere acreage. The Department of Justice (DOJ) has submitted court documents supporting former Maricopa County, Arizona, Sheriff Joe Arpaio's request to have his criminal conviction for contempt dismissed, just weeks after he received a pardon from President Trump. According to a filing by DOJ lawyers, the pardon nullifies any punitive consequences from Arpaio's non-final conviction, making the case "moot." They argue that because of the "unpredictable grace" of the presidential pardon, it would be "just and appropriate" to vacate the conviction. In late August, the White House announced Trump's decision to pardon Arpaio, stating, "Throughout his time as Sheriff, Arpaio continued his life’s work of protecting the public from crime and illegal immigration. Sheriff Joe Arpaio is now eighty-five years old, and after more than fifty years of admirable service to our Nation, he is a worthy candidate for a Presidential pardon." Following the pardon, Arpaio sought to overturn his conviction, and he also launched a fundraising campaign for his legal defense.
In 2018, China intends to land its first probe on the moon's dark side, marking a significant achievement in its ambitious space program, according to Xinhua, the official news agency. This follows the successful "soft landing" of the Chang'e-3 craft and its Jade Rabbit rover in 2013, nearly four decades after the last such landing. Previous missions have imaged the far side of the moon, which is never visible from Earth, but none has attempted a landing there. The upcoming Chang'e-4 mission, similar to its predecessor, will carry a larger payload and aims to investigate geological conditions on the far side. This could pave the way for deploying a radio telescope, given that Earth's radio emissions do not interfere with this region. China first declared its intention to land on the moon’s dark side in September 2015, with a goal of launching the mission by 2020. The early 2018 target highlights the significance of the space program to China's leadership, with President Xi Jinping emphasizing the country's aspiration to become a global space power. While China asserts its space endeavors are for peaceful purposes, the U.S. Defense Department has noted China's growing space capabilities, including concerns over anti-satellite weapons. Nine years ago, China destroyed an orbiting satellite with a ballistic missile, sparking worries about a new space arms race. Recently, the Chinese government has opened its lunar exploration program to private companies to foster innovation. In early 2015, China reportedly sent a letter of intent to collaborate on its latest mission to several foreign countries, though no partnerships were confirmed.
Three weeks before telling a BBC radio interviewer that he had learned about bushfires and global warming from Wikipedia, Environment Minister Greg Hunt received detailed briefings from the Bureau of Meteorology about the impact of climate change on Australia's weather patterns. Confidential Bureau of Meteorology briefings, obtained by Fairfax Media through freedom-of-information laws, reveal that senior officials warned Hunt that the extreme heat in 2013 was unprecedented and inconsistent with previous patterns. Initial briefings indicated that recent extreme heat aligned with a trend of global warming, while later advice in November highlighted that climate change had increased the likelihood of severe weather conducive to bushfires. These documents contradict claims made by Prime Minister Tony Abbott, who previously denied any connection between global warming and bushfires, and illustrate the extent to which the government was informed about climate change's role in recent extreme weather events in Australia.
The Carlisle United Football Club directors met on Sunday with team manager Graham Kavanagh after holding several discussions. Unfortunately, it was decided to part ways with Graham following a challenging and unsatisfactory start to the season. Over the past year, Graham led significant changes within the club, such as youth management, achieving Category 3 in the EPPP process, introducing strength and fitness coaching, diet control, and overhauling the first-team squad in the summer. Despite these efforts, the team's poor performance—averaging just one point per game since Greg Abbott's departure last season and through the first five games of this season—resulted in relegation to League 2 in May 2014. The board believes the team is still heading in the wrong direction. Saturday's loss to Cambridge served as a 'tipping point' for those managing the club. The directors wish Graham and his family well, acknowledging his hard work, determination, and contributions. They have begun the process of hiring a new team manager, and in the interim, club captain Paul Thirlwell and goalkeeping coach Tony Caig will manage training and team selections.
On Wednesday night, a serious pedestrian-vehicle collision occurred on Albro Lake Road in Dartmouth, closing the street between Victoria Road and Chapman Street while Halifax Regional Police conducted an investigation involving patrol, forensic, and accident reconstruction units. At approximately 8:50 p.m., a 47-year-old driver traveling westbound on Albro Lake Road struck a 26-year-old pedestrian at the intersection with Victoria Road. The injured pedestrian, from the metro area, was transported to the hospital by ambulance. By Thursday morning, the police reported that the pedestrian's condition had improved, though it was still not considered life-threatening. Authorities stated that charges would be decided after completing the investigation. This was the second pedestrian-vehicle collision reported by Halifax Regional Police on the same day; the first involved a 33-year-old man hit at Oxford Street and Norwood Street around 5 p.m., whose injuries were also described as non-life threatening. Police are seeking witness statements. Albro Lake Road was reopened around midnight.
