Alibaba's founder, Jack Ma, emphasized the importance of women during his speech at the Gateway 17 event in Detroit, stating, "Women are Alibaba’s secret sauce." Ma, one of the world's wealthiest individuals, explained that one of Alibaba's keys to success lies in its female employees. He noted that women tend to care more for others compared to men, who often prioritize themselves. Ma predicted that women would become increasingly powerful in the 21st century, attributing this to the shift from physical strength to intellectual prowess. He advised entrepreneurs to hire more women and to closely watch young people, small businesses, and women in the upcoming decades. During his talk, Ma offered several pieces of advice to young entrepreneurs. He suggested that those in their twenties should join reputable companies to learn about business, and by their forties, they should focus on areas where they excel. By the age of fifty, Ma recommended spending time nurturing younger talents. He also shared his personal experience of being turned down after waiting in a long queue on a hot summer day for a hotel job. In addition to his entrepreneurial tips, Ma discussed the future of technology, asserting that firms adept at using the internet will thrive in the coming years. He believed that while artificial intelligence might initially lead to job losses, it would ultimately create numerous new opportunities. Ma concluded by emphasizing that while machines will become smarter, human wisdom remains unparalleled. His leadership advice centered on prioritizing users and products over shareholders and stressed the importance of maintaining an optimistic outlook.
A call center in Thane, near Mumbai, tricked over 6,000 Americans into paying millions of dollars by posing as IRS agents. FBI officers, including Suhel Daud, a cybercrime expert of Indian origin, are collaborating with Thane police to investigate this scam. The Thane police expect assistance from the IRS and Department of Homeland Security. The scam involved around 2,000 workers at nine call centers who threatened Americans with home raids if they did not pay. The alleged ringleader, 24-year-old Sagar Thakkar, and his sister Reema, are believed to have fled. The fraudsters used the extorted funds for luxury items like cars and property investments. Thane police arrested 72 out of nearly 800 workers after shutting down the call centers. With FBI support, they aim to trace the money trail from the U.S. to Indian accounts. Similar operations in other cities might also face scrutiny.
HANS BADER examines the frequently cited statistics on earnings disparities between men and women. Laurence Butler notes that the economic argument against the claim that women earn just 77 cents for every man's dollar, working the same job, is flawed because many jobs are not truly equivalent; he points to varying fatality rates as an example. Nonetheless, Butler finds it entertaining to engage with liberal arguments, particularly when discussing economics. He questions why, if corporations are as large and profit-driven as liberals assert, and if men and women are performing identical tasks, companies wouldn't save money by paying women less. Laura adds that corporations prioritize male employees' profits and suggests that morality should be considered in business motivations, noting that liberals correctly identify issues with modern capitalism but propose the wrong solutions, such as increased bureaucracy and social engineering.

SPRINGFIELD, Mass. — The Roman Catholic Bishop of Springfield, Mitchell Rozanski, honored Marine Gunnery Sgt. Thomas Sullivan, a native of Springfield, as "exemplary" and "a leader and a man of true courage" during a private funeral Mass at Holy Cross Church on Monday. Sullivan, who turned 40, was among five service members killed by a gunman in Chattanooga on July 16. The shooter was subsequently killed by police. At the Mass, held at the church Sullivan had attended since childhood, Rozanski highlighted Sullivan's deep love for his family, his selfless dedication to the Marine Corps, and his unwavering faith. Sullivan, who trained for service, deployed to Iraq, and bravely protected his comrades on July 16, faced numerous challenges throughout his career. The service, attended by family, friends, active-duty Marines, and dignitaries like Governor Charlie Baker, Senator Elizabeth Warren, and Representative Richard Neal, included a procession down Springfield's streets, where hundreds of residents lined up, waving American flags. A bagpiper played the Marine Corps hymn outside the church. Rozanski emphasized Sullivan's faith, noting that as a follower of Jesus, it was his faith that made him an exemplary Marine, a leader, and a man of true courage. Sullivan will be laid to rest at the Massachusetts Veterans Memorial Cemetery in Agawam. Thousands of people paid their respects at a public wake held the previous day.
An Airman at Buckley Air Force Base, Brian Lebron-Rivera, 21, faces a manslaughter charge after telling police he accidentally shot and killed his wife, Genesis Rodriguez, 20, during a gunplay session at their apartment. Lebron-Rivera was arrested that evening after the incident occurred in the 17100 block of East Ohio Place. He reportedly informed officers, "I killed my wife, it was my fault," according to an arrest affidavit. Lebron-Rivera claimed that while demonstrating how to disarm someone with a gun, his wife was handling the weapon when he accidentally discharged it. He stated he had not loaded the gun before they began playing with it. After retrieving the weapon, he chambered a round and fired once, resulting in her death. Police received a report around 6 p.m. Thursday and discovered Rodriguez deceased at the apartment. Lebron-Rivera, an Airman First Class in the 460th Security Forces Squadron, appeared in court the following morning for arraignment on the charges. He is currently held in custody with $50,000 bail pending further investigation.

Samsung is leveraging the upcoming BBM launch for Android to promote its Galaxy devices, Samsung App Store, and Messaging Hub, specifically targeting the African market. BlackBerry is collaborating in this effort, having entered into an agreement to jointly market BBM to African mobile customers. This move signals BlackBerry's strategy for BBM, now open to non-BlackBerry platforms. BBM has traditionally been a core feature for one-to-one communication, and recently, BlackBerry introduced BBM Groups, enabling one-to-many messaging. In regions like Africa, BBM has facilitated both personal and business communications, offering a reliable and cost-effective alternative to SMS. The collaborative promotional activities underscore that BlackBerry is expanding BBM's reach to iOS and Android, despite potential conflicts with its own device sales. For Samsung, this partnership offers new users a familiar communication tool, encouraging them to switch from dedicated BlackBerry devices. While BlackBerry stands to gain access to a growing market, the deal might seem less advantageous given its declining user base. However, BlackBerry hopes to secure more users for future revenue streams, such as data analytics and advertising, through this expanded platform. Even if some users switch platforms, BlackBerry views this as a necessary step to tap into emerging markets.

LONDON — In reality, Mr. Darcy, the enigmatic hero from Jane Austen's renowned novel "Pride and Prejudice," would not resemble Colin Firth's portrayal. Instead, the authentic Mr. Darcy would have had a pale complexion, a pointed chin, and a long nose on a narrow, beardless face. Interestingly, his hair would have been powdered white. Additionally, he would have appeared somewhat undernourished with sloping shoulders, more akin to a ballet dancer than a muscular hero. Thus, far from the steamy romantic figure envisioned by many today, Mr. Darcy would have been a less appealing figure. As the 200th anniversary of Austen's death approached, a study by John Sutherland, a professor of modern English literature at University College London, and Amanda Vickery, a professor of early modern history at Queen Mary University of London, unveiled a historically accurate depiction of Fitzwilliam Darcy. This revelation shocked fans and may alter their perception of English literature's most eligible bachelor.
Netflix has finally introduced offline playback, a feature users have long requested since the service's inception. Starting Wednesday, users can download selected Netflix content for viewing without an internet connection. This includes airplane mode, road trips, and even those unexpected subway delays. With a "download" button now available for some films and TV shows, Netflix plans to expand this offering, particularly focusing on its original content due to licensing considerations. The initial lineup includes popular shows like Orange is the New Black, Narcos, and The Crown. Offline viewing is supported on both Android and iOS devices running versions 4.4.2 or higher of Android or iOS 8.0 or later, with two quality settings to choose from based on your preference for video quality or storage space.
Good afternoon, St. Louis! Today, we'll explore the future of transit in North St. Louis County. Metro invites transit passengers and the public to learn about the new North County Transit Center and share thoughts on a proposed MetroBus service plan at four upcoming informal meetings. The new transit center, set to open next spring at 3140 Pershall Road in Ferguson, Missouri, will host these events. Based on research, customer data, and feedback from previous public meetings, Metro has developed a new service plan for MetroBus routes in North St. Louis County, which will go into effect after the center opens. The open-house style meetings will give Metro commuters a chance to comment on the proposed service plan and engage with Metro staff to discuss how the new plan will meet their needs. Here’s the schedule: - Tuesday, November 10, 6 a.m. – 9 a.m., Riverview Transit Center, 9021 Riverview Drive, St. Louis, MO 63137 - Wednesday, November 11, 2 p.m. – 6 p.m., North Hanley Transit Center, 4398 Hanley Road, Berkeley, MO 63134 - Thursday, November 12, 11 a.m. – 2 p.m., St. Louis Community College - Florissant Valley, 3400 Pershall Road, St. Louis, MO 63135 (Student Center Multi-Purpose Room) - Tuesday, November 17, 4 p.m. – 6:30 p.m., Trinity Catholic High School, 1720 Redman Road, St. Louis, MO 63138 (Library) Metro secured federal funding to plan and build the North County Transit Center, which will include an indoor waiting area, public restrooms, concessions, and a free Park-Ride lot. This new hub will enhance bus service in North St. Louis County, offering better connections, faster transfers, and improved amenities. North St. Louis County is one of Metro's fastest-growing public transit markets, contributing 19% of total MetroBus and MetroLink ridership.
Earlier this week, Nicholas Chum from the Substratum team shared screenshots showcasing an upcoming feature for the popular theme engine. These images revealed the theme engine installed on a custom ROM with its own Customization option within the main Settings app. A theme was successfully applied, and a newly compiled theme appeared without errors. The most significant revelation came from the fourth screenshot, which displayed a non-rooted Nexus 6P running Android 7.1.1 Nougat. Typically, Substratum requires root access, but it seems this will change in an upcoming update. Mr. Chum acknowledged Ivan Iskandar for Substratum commits and Randall Rushing for platform commits that enabled this new feature. This rootless functionality will not work on stock Android versions but should be compatible with all custom ROMs that integrate the special masquerade job engine and new Substratum version. While many XDA users might prefer rooting to use Substratum, others avoid it. Chum notes that the transition from root to rootless is still untested, and a statement will soon be issued to custom ROM developers detailing how to incorporate this new version into their builds. If successful, users can easily update to these new custom ROMs through a dirty flash.
Pump failures have led to significant water shortages in Cibecue, Arizona, prompting the White Mountain Apache Tribe to declare a state of emergency. Navajo County reports that the community's water supply is now only five percent of its usual amount due to these failures. The county is requesting donations of hand sanitizer and water, which can be dropped off at the Navajo County Board of Supervisors Office in Holbrook or at the Reception Desk in Show Low. Yavapai County also declared a state of emergency in Cordes Lake, where despite operational equipment and wells, the water system cannot meet demand due to intense heat. Customers are advised to reduce their water usage by about 50%. Water is being transported from Prescott Valley to replenish storage tanks, and Cordes Lake has instituted a nightly shutdown of the water system from 11 p.m. to 3 a.m. to conserve resources. Limited bottled water is available at the Mayer Fire Station in Cordes Lake.

UPDATE: Attorneys representing Honeywell retirees have sought an injunction to stop the company from terminating medical coverage. This request was made to the U.S. District Court for the Eastern District of Michigan. Earlier, David Lymangrover, a Honeywell retiree from Mishawaka, looked forward to his retirement, secure in the knowledge of his pension and supplemental insurance, which included prescription coverage. "I thought we'd be set," he recalled. However, his outlook darkened when he received a letter from Honeywell on April 3, stating that the company would end health coverage for retirees as of June 30, 2017, following a reevaluation of its "health care offerings." The letter suggested that the Medigap market had matured, enabling Medicare-eligible retirees to find "affordable and comprehensive health insurance and prescription drug coverage." Retirees were directed to call the Honeywell Retirement Service Center for assistance. Charlotte Lymangrover, David's wife, expressed concern about being unable to find comparable insurance given their permanent retirement status. Their current coverage included benefits for blood pressure medication and inhalers. Honeywell spokespersons stated, "We are providing ample time for retirees to review individual marketplaces to identify suitable alternative health insurance options based on cost and coverage." They noted that state or federally operated online marketplaces offer opportunities to purchase medical coverage from private insurers, with potential federal subsidies for those with lower incomes. UAW Local 9 President Todd Treder is investigating the situation, and retirees can contact him at 574-209-2201 if they have questions. Honeywell issued the following statement: "After thorough review, we have decided to terminate medical and prescription drug coverage for certain retirees, effective June 30, 2017. We are providing ample time for retirees to review the individual marketplace to identify alternative health insurance options that best suit their needs from a cost and coverage standpoint."
In 1978, the Supreme Court's decision in the Bakke case invalidated racial quotas in higher education. Justice Lewis Powell highlighted Harvard’s inclusive admissions policy, which considered race among multiple positive factors rather than setting aside specific slots. Thirty-six years later, this approach is under scrutiny in a federal district court in Boston. Plaintiffs argue that Harvard’s admissions policy amounts to a covert quota system discriminating against Asian-Americans. This marks the first such challenge targeting a private university, spearheaded by Edward Blum, who aims to overturn Bakke. His organization, the Project on Fair Representation, recruits students alleging unfair rejections due to racial preferences. The complaint, filed by Students for Fair Admissions (SFFA), features an exemplary candidate—a Chinese immigrant descendant with perfect test scores, top academic standing, leadership roles, and community service—who was rejected by Harvard, allegedly to control the Asian-American student population. Blum asserts that Harvard’s policy is a guise for racial balancing and quotas. Despite Asian-Americans comprising more than 27% of applicants to the three most selective Ivy League colleges from 2008 to 2012, their admission rate was only 17-20%, a disparity SFFA deems intentional discrimination under Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964. Blum believes this lawsuit could lead to the abolition of race-based admissions at colleges.

Star veteran Reggie Wayne has departed via free agency, leaving the Colts and creating an unusual absence. Wayne remains undecided about his future but has ruled out playing another season with the Colts. This marks the first time since before the 2001 season that Wayne isn't with the team, and for the first time since before the 1996 season, neither Marvin Harrison nor Reggie Wayne will be part of the Colts lineup. However, the Colts have a promising young star, T.Y. Hilton, who is set to take on a larger role in 2015. Not only will Hilton be the primary receiver for Andrew Luck’s offensive strategy, but he will also lead the younger players, including Donte Moncrief and Duron Carter, after discussing his new responsibilities with Wayne. Safety Mike Adams will also step up, aiming to fill the leadership void left by Reggie Wayne and Cory Redding. While some key leaders are departing, the Colts have a blend of experienced veterans and emerging leaders ready to guide the team in 2015.

The European Commission has given Poland, Hungary, and the Czech Republic one month to reconsider their decision not to participate in the EU's migrant relocation program. Brussels initiated legal proceedings against these countries and warned that Poland might lose its voting rights if it does not comply with EU demands. EU Migration Commissioner Dimitris Avramopoulos stated, "There is still time to change everything and return to normality." It's noteworthy that Austria, which also refuses to accept migrants, is not facing similar legal action, possibly due to its status as a net contributor to the EU budget, unlike the other three countries. Neither side appears willing to back down, and the matter could eventually reach the European Court of Justice. Avramopoulos insists that the relocation of migrants will continue beyond the current scheme, making it unclear which country will yield first.
Following a gunman's fatal shooting of nine people at a historic black church in Charleston, South Carolina, hate crimes in the state are facing renewed attention. The state, without a hate crimes law, hosts 19 active hate groups, including two Ku Klux Klan chapters. According to the Hate Crime Statistics Act, a hate crime involves evidence of prejudice based on factors such as race, gender, religion, disability, sexual orientation, or ethnicity. Such crimes include murder, non-negligent manslaughter, rape, assault, intimidation, arson, and property damage. Federal authorities are investigating the attack as a potential hate crime. Among the 19 groups listed, white nationalist, Ku Klux Klan, Neo-Nazi, black separatist, neo-Confederate, and anti-LGBT organizations are included. Nationally, the number of hate groups has decreased in recent years, from 1,018 in 2011 to 784 in 2014, according to the Southern Poverty Law Center. In 2007, South Carolina reported 127 hate crimes, increasing to 153 the following year but dropping to 51 in 2013. In July 2014, the KKK distributed leaflets in a South Carolina neighborhood urging people to join their cause. Nationally, nearly half of the 5,922 hate crimes reported in 2013 were racially motivated, followed by those targeting sexual orientation at 20.8 percent. Rev. Al Sharpton, president of the National Action Network, questioned societal values in light of this incident. The alleged shooter stated, "You rape our women and are taking over our country and you have to go," before the interview.
Parents angered by a 10-year-old boy's plea for raping an 8-year-old are keeping their children away from a northern suburb primary school. The 10-year-old pleaded guilty to sexual penetration of a child and threatening to kill. He must remain at school under close supervision pending court proceedings. Although the 8-year-old victim attends a different school, around 50 parents met outside on Monday to voice safety concerns, citing the school's failure to inform them about the December incident. Some parents have withdrawn their kids due to perceived inadequate supervision. The school now has two security guards at the entrance and an announcement board stating "all students are safe." An Education Department spokesperson confirmed the court did not impose restrictions on the boy's school attendance and noted that two staff members continuously supervise him. The spokesperson emphasized the Education Act's guarantee of educational rights regardless of criminal charges. The school is taking all reasonable steps to protect its students, and the boy faces further court appearances.

HUNTSVILLE, Alabama – Despite the recent collapse of the world's largest cupcake company, Huntsville's sole cupcake truck, Sugar Belle, is flourishing. The business, founded by Andrew and Lee Judge in February 2013, is set to unveil a second vehicle next week in Madison and at Redstone Arsenal. After a year of operating with a gas-guzzling RV, they've acquired a 2000 Ford high-top van for better long-distance travel. This teal van will sport Sugar Belle’s recognizable smiling cupcake logo, complemented by hot pink rims. Andrew explained, "We wanted a smaller, more fuel-efficient option that’s easier to maintain and perfect for events." Their current silver truck, stationed at Below the Radar in downtown Huntsville since July 2013, will undergo maintenance and kitchen upgrades to operate as a mobile bakery. Downtown construction, limited utilities, and parking issues have presented challenges. "It was exciting to start, but the noise, dust, and trash from construction made it less appealing for customers," Andrew noted. While searching for a permanent spot, they aim to find a location with utilities and a patio. They encourage public input on potential locations through their Facebook page or by emailing info@sugarbelletruck.com. Although a proposed food truck park in Cummings Research Park couldn’t proceed due to zoning restrictions, they’re in discussions with the city of Huntsville to establish such a facility. According to NPD Group, while overall cupcake servings decreased slightly, Sugar Belle continues to see strong customer demand. Once upgrades are complete, they plan to expand the menu beyond cupcakes. Andrew said, "I wasn't sure we could sustain ourselves just with cupcakes, but it’s been more successful than expected." Paul Lester, who owns Something Sweet Bake Shop in Daphne, believes location plays a crucial role in cupcake business success.

We now live in a dramatically different era for pesticides compared to the past. It's often forgotten that before the advent of stringent regulations, pesticides could be used extensively and with little oversight from 1940s through the early 1960s—years prior to Silent Spring, the Clean Water Act, and the establishment of the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA). The Clean Water Act and the EPA marked significant milestones in ensuring safer chemical usage today. However, despite this progress, pesticides continue to contaminate waterways, particularly in the Midwest, where they leach into rivers and streams. A comprehensive US Geological Survey study, recently published in Environmental Science and Technology, analyzed water samples from over 200 locations across the US between 1992 and 2011, revealing widespread presence of insecticides and herbicides. While current pesticide levels are generally safer than in the past, with fewer instances exceeding human health benchmarks since 2002, there has been an increase in pesticide pollution in urban streams. Two specific pesticides, fipronil and dichlorvos, accounted for this rise; both are harmful to aquatic life at detectable levels. Notably, the study did not assess certain widely used pesticides like Roundup due to cost constraints. As Karen Ryberg, a study co-author, pointed out to the New York Times, the development of new pesticides introduces a delay in creating detection methods, posing challenges for staying current in environmental monitoring.

CARACAS, Venezuela — Due to an electricity crisis, Venezuela's public employees will work only on Mondays and Tuesdays. President Nicolas Maduro announced that the government would reduce work hours for at least two weeks to conserve energy. He cited a severe drought, which has depleted the water levels behind the country’s largest dam, as the primary cause. Experts also attribute the issue to inadequate planning and maintenance. Earlier this month, the government had already granted nearly 3 million public workers Fridays off and introduced four-hour daily blackouts. Now, it has extended the Friday holiday to include grade school teachers, although those in public hospitals and state-run supermarkets will continue to work. Many Venezuelans were skeptical about the effectiveness of this measure, noting that some have used their free time to queue for essential goods and run air conditioners, which may not significantly reduce power consumption. Chronic power outages have long been an issue in Venezuela, with previous administrations failing to address the problem effectively.

The current Ebola outbreak is the worst on record. Liberia has shut down most of its borders, prohibited public gatherings, and imposed quarantines on certain communities to control the spread of the virus. As of now, there have been 1,201 confirmed, suspected, or probable cases of Ebola in West Africa this year, resulting in over 670 deaths. There is no vaccine or cure for Ebola, which has a mortality rate as high as 90% in severe cases. The virus is transmitted from wild animals to humans or through contact with infected individuals. Fruit bats, commonly consumed by people in West Africa, are believed to harbor the virus. Symptoms begin with flu-like signs and can progress to damage kidney and liver functions, and in severe cases, lead to external and internal bleeding. The outbreak originated in southeastern Guinea in February and expanded to Liberia in March and Sierra Leone in May. Nigeria recently reported its first probable case, triggering heightened alertness after a Liberian patient died in Lagos. An outbreak is deemed over only after 42 days, the duration of the maximum incubation period, without any new confirmed cases, so the current outbreak is expected to persist until at least September.
Media playback is unsupported on your device Image caption Expedition organizers at base camp spoke to the team atop K2, as reported by Shahzeb Jillani The first team of Pakistani climbers to reach the summit of K2, the world's second-highest mountain, has arrived at the top. K2 is located in Pakistan, close to the northern border with China, and the climbers achieved their goal at 2:30 AM (10:30 PM GMT on Friday). Climbers consider K2 more challenging than Mount Everest, the world’s highest peak. Descending from the summit is deemed even riskier. This expedition, named K2 60 Years Later, marks the 60th anniversary of the first successful ascent of K2, which was achieved by two Italians, Achille Compagnoni and Lino Lacedelli, on July 31, 1954. The current team consists of six Pakistanis—Hassan Jan, Ali Durani, Rahmat Ullah Baig, Ghulam Mehdi, Ali, and Muhammad Sadiq—and three Italians. Previous individual Pakistani climbers have reached the summit, but this marks the country's first successful team effort. Our correspondent in Islamabad, Shahzeb Jillani, notes that many have perished on the descent due to its inherent dangers. In June, the Italian organization backing the Pakistani team announced the installation of a weather station providing data to climbers and researchers monitoring high-altitude activities. Sydney Gholston was waiting in line at a Kentucky Walmart with a cart full of Thanksgiving turkeys when a friendly, white-haired man behind her initiated a chat. When Gholston turned around, she was stunned to see Jon Voight. Voight, who mentioned he was in town filming a movie, noticed the six frozen turkeys in her cart and asked if she had a large family. Gholston, 28, chuckled and explained that the turkeys were intended to feed children at Home of the Innocents, a local nonprofit shelter and pediatric convalescent center. Immediately after her explanation, Voight offered to pay for her groceries. With his assistance, Gholston was able to return the turkeys to the Home, where they would feed approximately 70 of the 196 residents during the Thanksgiving holiday. Meredith Pack, the marketing manager for Home of the Innocents, informed CBS News that "Some medically fragile children do not eat the same Thanksgiving meal, and some residents will have other arrangements with family." After voicing her gratitude to Voight, Gholston requested a photo with the actor. The Home of the Innocents shared the picture and Gholston's inspiring story on their Facebook page, which quickly went viral, garnering over 4,200 shares and 11,000 likes. Comments on the post praised Voight's generosity, with one user stating, "That is an awesome act of kindness; makes one grateful that there are good people out there." Another added, "Way to go sir, thank you for taking care of those families." The nonprofit expressed its appreciation, noting, "We were so appreciative of his kindness! He was very interested in the Home and the services we provide."

The first known case of whirling disease in Canadian fish was discovered in Johnson Lake within Banff National Park. Parks Canada has restricted access to the lake to prevent the spread of the disease, which affects trout and salmon, causing them to swim erratically and die prematurely. Fishing and recreational activities have been prohibited. The disease, caused by the microscopic parasite Myxobolus cerebralis, can survive in lake mud for decades. To contain the outbreak, officials are urging people not to move fish between waters and to thoroughly clean, drain, and dry their equipment. This is the first confirmed case of whirling disease in Canada, and the Canadian Food Inspection Agency, along with Parks Canada and Alberta Environment and Parks, is coordinating a response. Fish from other lakes in Banff National Park are also being tested, and AEP is sampling fish downstream. Anyone suspecting the presence of the disease should report it to 1-855-336-BOAT.
A conflict between a property developer and the relatives of a deceased person whose grave lies within a construction site has led to an unusual scene. Villagers were compensated to relocate their loved ones from the cemetery to accommodate the construction. However, one family declined the compensation, refusing to move the grave. As a result, the solitary grave remains on a pile of earth, elevated 10 meters above ground level, while construction proceeds around it. According to Britain's Daily Mail, the tomb is the ancestral grave of a villager from nearby Longbao. The Sun newspaper notes that developers are now willing to pay nearly £100,000 ($160,675) to relocate the grave and its headstone. This 'nail grave,' as termed by Asian media, is part of a series of resistance acts against land dispossession in China, including instances where freeways were built around single houses and lone houses stood in the midst of construction sites.

Today marks Indonesia's National Music Day, and to celebrate, we present one of the country's most overlooked yet remarkable facets of musical history—Indonesian psychedelic rock from the 1970s. This genre, which thrived underground due to the stringent censorship under President Suharto, produced a wealth of music that was largely forgotten until recent rediscovery. Thanks to enthusiasts and dedicated researchers, including Canadian hip hop producer Jason Moss Connoy and Indonesian rock legend Benny Soebardja, much of this music is now available. One of the standout compilations is "Those Shocking Shaking Days," released by Now-Again Records. This collection captures the rebellious spirit of the time through relentless fuzz, politically charged lyrics, and strong rhythms, offering listeners a glimpse into a period when Indonesian music faced significant challenges but still flourished.
Wars invariably present unforeseen challenges. Examples include Germany's deployment of mustard gas during World War I and North Vietnam's surprisingly effective air defense system during the Vietnam War. Throughout these conflicts, U.S. troops have had to adapt to unexpected threats using the resources at their disposal. However, the part of the Defense Department responsible for training and equipping these troops has often been slow to respond. This paradox is surprising to many outside the Pentagon, which generally excels at long-term strategic acquisitions, resulting in a significant qualitative edge over potential adversaries. Despite ongoing cost issues, the department has improved purchasing efficiency for taxpayers. It has also made strides in medical advancements, particularly in prosthetics and treatments for traumatic brain injuries and posttraumatic stress disorder. However, this same system struggles to quickly provide necessary technology and equipment to troops in the field. Over the past five years, as undersecretary of defense for acquisition, technology, and logistics, and then as deputy secretary, I have worked to address this gap. With the end of the Iraq and Afghanistan wars, it is crucial to understand what hindered the Pentagon's ability to meet immediate needs, what lasting lessons can be gleaned from its efforts to improve responsiveness, and how to establish the right structures for future agility. It's astonishing that knowledgeable, experienced, and highly regarded individuals continue to advocate for "return to growth" despite witnessing the interconnectedness and limitations of our global system. It's clear that we inhabit a natural, interdependent world, and we've reached a point where further quantitative growth is constrained. Humanity has matured to the point where we can no longer merely expand in quantity; instead, we must focus on qualitative development. Yet, we persist in measuring progress quantitatively, eagerly awaiting renewed growth as if it were the sole path to advancement. This mindset is akin to a teenager or even an adult measuring their height to define success, ignoring the need to develop the skills necessary for a mature, integrated existence. We must now embrace a deeper understanding of our global environment, learn to coexist sustainably, and ensure our actions align with the natural systems around us, rather than relying on our individual egos to dictate our future.

A recent study characterizes Eagles fans as stable, a descriptor seldom applied to them. This doesn't mean loyal or dependable, but rather emotionally stable—less prone to extreme mood swings. Using Twitter data from the 2012 NFL season, Emory University researchers Mike Lewis and Manish Tripathi assessed fan happiness, sadness, and stability. Saints fans were happiest after wins, Steelers fans saddest after losses, and Cowboys fans showed the least emotional波动。Emory concluded that Eagles fans could also be seen as resigned, looking forward to change and a new coaching staff rather than dwelling on recent losses.

It also announced plans to conduct further nuclear tests and ballistic missile launches. In recent months, North Korea has fired over 20 ballistic missiles, aiming to enhance its ability to deliver payloads accurately. American intelligence agencies remain skeptical of these claims. OREGON HOUSE, Calif. — Deputies responded to a report of an agitated man damaging plants at a Rastafarian church's marijuana farm and engaged in a shootout, resulting in the death of the suspect and injuries to two deputies. Sheriff Steve Durfor of Yuba County reported that three deputies arrived at the remote farm around 8:40 a.m., with one deputy locating the suspect. After the suspect fled, deputies entered a nearby home where shots were fired, prompting a third deputy to rescue his colleagues. SWAT teams later entered the home and found the deceased suspect. Neither the deputies' involvement in the suspect's death nor the cause of their injuries were confirmed. Both deputies were hospitalized and expected to recover post-surgery. Heidi Lepp, leader of the Sugarleaf Rastafarian Church, informed authorities that a new farm worker named "Sawyer" had become erratic and damaged marijuana plants. The church considers marijuana sacred, though it lacks a permit to grow medical cannabis in Yuba County. The incident followed a similar event in Los Banos, where police officers were injured when confronting a man who had broken into his ex-wife's apartment.

Steve Little, born on July 1, 1972, is an American actor, voice actor, and comedian recognized for his roles in Eastbound & Down, Adventure Time, The Grinder, and Haters Back Off. Currently, he co-stars in the Adult Swim series Neon Joe, Werewolf Hunter. His most notable role is Stevie Janowski, a middle school band teacher on Eastbound & Down, where he served as Kenny Powers' personal assistant. Little is part of The Groundlings, an improvisational and sketch comedy group in Los Angeles, and was tapped by Joe Murray to voice the "Dung Beetle" characters Chip and Skip. He has appeared in movies like Accepted and TV shows such as 30 Rock, The Office, and Romantic Encounters. Little has also voiced characters on Camp Lazlo, Flapjack, and Adventure Time, including Chip and Skip, Lemmings, Dr. Barber, Lolly Poopdeck, The Duke of Nuts, Turtle Princess, Abracadaniel, and Peppermint Butler. He starred in The Catechism Cataclysm and wrote and starred in a Nickelodeon pilot titled Cosmic Signals. In 2014, he starred in the short film Rat Pack Rat, which won a jury award at the 2014 Sundance Film Festival. From 2015 to 2016, he played Todd in The Grinder and Cleve Menu in Neon Joe, Werewolf Hunter. In 2016, he joined the cast of Haters Back Off as Miranda Sings' uncle Jim.

Barbara Loden is a distinctive figure in American independent cinema. Prior to directing her sole feature film, she had achieved success on Broadway with a Tony win and had minor roles in Hollywood films. However, none of these experiences felt entirely fulfilling. Fortunately for us, she was compelled to create her own project, resulting in one of the most impactful independent films ever made—Wanda (1970). This film is perhaps the most emotionally resonant portrayal of a woman's struggle I have encountered. The authenticity of the story is deeply intertwined with Loden’s personal experiences and the real-life events it is based on. Additionally, Loden infused the film with her own life story, making it a deeply personal and poignant work. Sadly, this was her only feature, as she passed away from cancer ten years later without completing another project. Wanda is a powerful and tragic tale, both within the film and beyond its boundaries. Loden was a trailblazer, and her work remains a monumental achievement. I encourage you to watch it. You will encounter elements like divorce court, outlaws, in-laws, cheap motels, life on the run, and the sad fate of the prettiest girl in town. – Cole Links and Recommendations: - Watch Wanda on IMDb. - Ericca’s further viewing recommendation: Housekeeping. - Cole’s further viewing recommendation: Harlan County U.S.A. - Visit the website of the Pennsylvania Anthracite History Museum. - See Barbara Loden on the Mike Douglas show.
If a planned "super WiFi" trial behaves well, British mobile users won't need to reduce their data usage any time soon. Led by Microsoft and supported by major UK TV providers, this enhanced wireless network operates on the unused 150MHz spectrum that terrestrial TV broadcasts avoid. Known as "white spaces," these frequencies are utilized in other countries to avoid signal interference. Microsoft’s Dan Reed refers to spectrum as a "finite natural resource," suggesting that this trial could provide a significant opportunity. The test will be conducted in Cambridge, which has a mix of old and new buildings. This network can penetrate walls more effectively than weaker mobile signals (up to 16Mbps). With a similar BT rollout already in progress in Scotland, the technology appears poised for widespread adoption in Britain, though the US continues to face regulatory challenges.
Between 1607 and 1625, during the harsh conditions at Jamestown, Virginia, the first American colonists resorted to cannibalism, according to new findings by scientists at the Smithsonian’s National Museum of Natural History. In 2012, during an excavation, remains of a 14-year-old girl were discovered. Her skull showed signs of being split open posthumously and then buried alongside those of slaughtered animals. Researchers dated these bones to the winter of 1609-1610, known as the "starving time," when many colonists perished. "This discovery was immediately recognized as unusual due to the location and visible damage to the skull," stated archaeologist Bill Kelso. The girl is now known as Jane, and her injuries confirm the colonists' desperate measures. Historical documents mentioned widespread cannibalism, but these findings provide the first concrete evidence. "The treatment of Jane's body reflects the colonists' dire circumstances," explained Smithsonian's Dr. Douglas Owsley. "The bone fragments show attempts to remove brain and flesh from her face." Jane's facial reconstruction, based on forensic techniques, will be displayed at the National Museum of Natural History on May 3.

Following the evaluation of the static code analyzer PVS-STUDIO, we'll now assess the new C/C++ compiler zapcc from Ceemente Software, which uses a modified LLVM/clang with an innovative caching system. Available on Mac OS X, Linux, and Windows, zapcc supports Unix projects based on cmake or autotools. To gather meaningful data, I'll use two significant projects: LMMS, a professional music production platform, and OpenCV, known for its lengthy build times. The tests will run on Linux Mint with an i5-5200U CPU and 8GB of RAM, using both the default clang and zapcc. First, let's examine the results with clang: ``` Output with 5 parallel jobs ``` Next, we'll increase the default memory cache in zapccs.config from 1200 to 2000 and exclude specific files from caching. The compiler executables are zapcc and zapcc++, but their clang heritage is evident in the output. There's a clear reduction in compilation time. For comparison, let's try OpenCV: ``` Clang output Zapcc output ``` Again, the difference is substantial. Zapcc would be particularly beneficial for large projects like Qt4/5, which often require several hours to compile. In a professional setting, the time savings can be redirected to other tasks. However, the caching mechanism necessitates balancing memory usage according to the target hardware. Given that zapcc is based on clang/LLVM, it might be feasible to port it to FreeBSD, considering the growing popularity of this platform in professional environments. PITTSBURGH (KDKA) – Police are investigating an alleged hazing incident at Highlands High School, where a 16-year-old autistic student named Austin Babinsack was reportedly duct-taped to a goal post by a coach and several players. The incident occurred on Sunday night at the school's soccer fields. Austin, who was left taped for about 15 minutes, was eventually freed by an off-duty Pennsylvania State Trooper. His mother, Kristy Babinsack, expressed deep concern: "He was terrified; he could have died or had a heart attack from stress. He was screaming." The district has suspended coach Jim Turner and two players for at least five days. Babinsack describes the event, saying, "They taped my hands, legs, and waist, and tried to take a picture. I told them to stop and they left disappointed." The school district issued a statement, "Highlands School District does not tolerate hazing and bullying. Strict disciplinary action is taken against students who engage in such behaviors." Babinsack's mother hopes Austin understands that the situation may worsen before improving. She also called for holding the adult coaches accountable first, noting, "The coach knew what was happening and should have intervened. We need to address the adults' roles before focusing on the children's actions." Austin attended a school soccer game afterward, where players had previously mocked him. Harrison Township police are investigating the incident, and Austin plans to return to school tomorrow.

Utah-based electric vehicle manufacturer Nikola Motor Company has recently unveiled its initial two models. The first, the Nikola Zero, is a practical four-wheeler boasting a range of 125 miles, though it’s not particularly remarkable. The star of the show is undoubtedly the Nikola One, a big rig with an impressive and distinctive design. Despite the limitations imposed by trailer attachments, the Nikola One presents a striking appearance. Its specifications seem almost otherworldly—using a turbine to maintain a massive 320 kWh battery, offering up to 1,200 miles of range before recharging. Buyers can opt for various turbine fuel options, and the interior features a large touchscreen similar to those found in Teslas. However, the most significant aspect is the truck’s futuristic aesthetic, especially its wraparound windshield. Unfortunately, both models are currently just renderings available for reservation on the company’s website for $750 and $1,500. The Zero would retail at $42,000, and the One at $375,000, should they ever enter production—a feat fraught with challenges given the history of electric vehicle development. As for the world’s first self-driving big rig, that remains to be seen.
A man from Surrey has been engaged in a prolonged dispute with the Insurance Corporation of British Columbia (ICBC) over his right to wear religious headgear in his driver's license photo. OBi Canuel, 36, a Pastafarian minister who wears a colander as part of his religious observance, faced an ultimatum from ICBC on Friday. Unless he removed his headgear for a photograph, he would not be allowed to drive beyond the end of the day. "I was willing to wait until they changed their stance, but they didn't hesitate to issue me temporary licenses," Canuel said. "Today, this has become a significant issue." Canuel obtained a one-day permit when he visited an ICBC office, highlighting the inconvenience caused by the situation. He believes his rights under the Canadian Charter of Rights and Freedoms are being violated. "The Charter guarantees religious expression, not just for mainstream religions but for unique ones like mine," Canuel stated. "I want everyone to feel free to express their religion without shame or embarrassment." Canuel's conflict began almost a year ago when he attempted to get his license photo taken with his headgear, which ICBC claimed did not interfere with facial recognition technology. However, ICBC later informed him that there was no religious prohibition against removing the colander. Adam Grossman, an ICBC spokesperson, declined to disclose if the insurer maintains a list of recognized religions or criteria for accepting religious headgear. Grossman noted that Canuel does not appear to wear his headgear in videos on his YouTube channel.
Three years ago, a significant shift occurred in economic policymaking, both in the West and across Europe. Despite the financial crisis having abated, economies on either side of the Atlantic continued to struggle with high unemployment. Yet, policy makers collectively prioritized reducing budget deficits over addressing unemployment. In my previous writings, I contended that concerns over deficits are largely overstated and have detailed how deficit hawks persistently stoke fears. Now, I want to discuss another aspect of this situation: the desperate quest to find instances where austerity measures actually worked. Advocates of fiscal austerity, known as austerians, made bold claims that austerity would prevent crises and promote prosperity. Their search for success stories led them to the Republic of Ireland, which implemented severe spending cuts following its housing bubble burst. For a time, Ireland was hailed as a paragon of economic virtue. According to Jean-Claude Trichet of the European Central Bank, Ireland served as a model for all of Europe's indebted nations. American conservatives pushed this narrative further, with Alan Reynolds, a senior fellow at the Cato Institute, arguing that Ireland's approach could guide the United States as well.

According to Barran Liebman, the Portland City Council has established proposed rules for the new Sick Leave Ordinance. Public written comments will be considered before the finalization of these rules by November 1, 2013. Starting January 1, 2014, Portland employers with six or more employees must provide up to 40 hours of paid sick leave annually for employees working at least 240 hours. Employers with fewer than five employees must offer 40 hours of unpaid sick leave. This leave can be used for personal illnesses (including pregnancy, childbirth, and medical appointments), caring for ill family members, or handling medical emergencies. It also applies to situations involving domestic violence, harassment, sexual assault, or stalking. For further details on the proposed rules, see the full article on the Barran Liebman website.
On October 4, the International Monetary Fund released its World Economic Outlook, which contained significant negative economic forecasts. However, this news went unreported by the major broadcast networks that evening. The IMF revised its projections for global economic growth and specific countries, including the United States. Bloomberg noted that the IMF had reduced its forecast for U.S. growth to 1.6% for this year and 2.2% for next year, marking a 43% decline from the previous year's estimate of 2.8% for 2016. The IMF had continually lowered its economic forecasts throughout the year, attributing some of these downgrades to "backlash against globalization" and "increasing protectionism." Despite this worrisome news, CBS Evening News, NBC Nightly News, and ABC World News Tonight did not cover it. The networks also largely overlooked other economic reports, such as the Commerce Department's second quarter GDP growth estimate of 1.4%, announced on July 29. CNBC pointed out on September 29 that this expansion's pace was the weakest since 1949. Nonetheless, the broadcast networks have mostly steered clear of reporting on these economic indicators. If the IMF's predictions hold true, the U.S. could experience a period of low-growth stagnation reminiscent of the 1940s.
Bitcoin, the leading cryptocurrency by value, is excluded from both Google and Yahoo's currency converters, despite its widespread popularity. Microsoft's Bing and Oanda, however, do include Bitcoin but not other cryptocurrencies like Litecoin or Dogecoin. When pressed, neither Google nor Yahoo offered concrete plans or reasons for this omission. Google’s Jason Freidenfelds stated that no specific plans were in place and that the company typically does not announce product launches in advance. Freidenfelds also mentioned that Google continually improves its features, noting over 890 improvements in search quality in 2013. Similarly, Yahoo’s Bahareh Ramin declined to comment on future plans. In contrast, Microsoft and Oanda were eager to discuss their inclusion of Bitcoin. A Microsoft spokesperson explained that the addition was due to high public interest and the company's responsiveness to emerging trends. Courtney Gibson from Oanda highlighted that Bitcoin was added to their converter last spring, viewing it as a noteworthy experiment in financial innovation and a way to acknowledge growing interest in virtual payment systems. While Gibson confirmed that Bitcoin remains the most popular cryptocurrency, Oanda is considering adding other cryptocurrencies to their converter based on client interest.

Xlevus, a dedicated member of /r/VFIO and developer, has transferred his virsh-patcher to The Passthrough POST’s GitHub repositories, marking a significant step forward for our VFIO automation project. Read also: vfioselect streamlines device binding. The virsh-patcher simplifies common adjustments such as error 43 fixes or hugepages through the command line interface (CLI). It's accessible on all distributions via pip from our GitHub repository: `pip install -U https://github.com/PassthroughPOST/virsh-patcher/archive/master.zip`. Ensure you have a valid Python installation and pypi/pip set up. Usage instructions: After installation, run `virshpatcher [FLAGS] [/path/to/target/VM/xml.xml]` with flags like `--error43`, `--hugepages`, `--host-passthrough`, or `--patch` alongside the path to your XML patch file. This applies the patches to the XML. Further native patches, including performance optimizations, automatic hook-helper registration, and a "trimmer" to remove unnecessary default devices, are planned. We extend our gratitude to Xlevus for his contribution, which helps prevent redundant efforts and brings us closer to developing a fully automated VFIO deployment system. His work significantly benefits the community. Reach him on GitHub or our Discord server. We're seeking testers for all our VFIO-Tools projects, including hook-helper, vfio-select, and virsh-patcher. Don't hesitate to give them a try and share your feedback. Our ultimate aim is to create a user-friendly, graphical front-end for tweaking and configuring systems, along with a guest-side client for seamless changes. However, substantial effort and time are required to launch such extensive projects. If you appreciate our work and wish to contribute, consider becoming a Patron. You'll gain access to exclusive content on our site, private channels on our Discord, and additional perks. Images courtesy of Pixabay.

Nintendo's Shigeru Miyamoto has confirmed that the Wii U supports only one touch-screen controller per console. However, if a game requires more controllers, a Nintendo 3DS could be used instead. Miyamoto stated, "Our basic premise is that you can use one [Wii U controller] with a system. If the need arises for multiple controllers, it might be more convenient for users to employ their 3DS and connect it." To date, multiplayer Wii U games have utilized up to four Wii Remote Plus controllers for additional players. Restricting the Wii U to one controller would indeed reduce costs for consumers, given the expense of spare touch-screen controllers. Whether the Wii U can technically stream to two controller screens simultaneously remains under investigation by Nintendo. Miyamoto mentioned, "We are researching the possibility of allowing a player to bring their controller to a friend's house and play together on Wii U."

It's a truth universally acknowledged that writers face blocks. When this happens, how should we respond? Should we succumb to a deep depression akin to "Requiem for a Dream," or do we muster courage like John Wayne and forge ahead? Brainstorming can be helpful—research suggests that our creative minds work best in chaotic environments. Try jotting down random thoughts and words without worrying about completing sentences. Another effective method is to draw inspiration from other authors, though navigating the legal and ethical boundaries can be tricky. While online resources provide guidelines, court cases often hinge on subjective interpretation. Studying history offers an easy and safe way to find inspiration with minimal risk of copyright infringement. History is replete with fascinating figures and cultures, from the extreme practices of foot-binding in China to the Aztecs' unique rituals. Exploring these narratives helps us understand our past and our identities, providing insight into coping mechanisms across different eras and societies. Moreover, history is vast and freely accessible, allowing writers to draw from various periods and cultures, adding their unique perspective without legal concerns. Just as those who ignore history are destined to repeat its lessons, so too are those who overlook its rich tapestry of stories.

As the prevalence of antibiotic-resistant bacteria grows, scientists continue to explore novel sources for potential new drugs. A promising candidate has emerged from the freshwater polyp Hydra: a protein named hydramacin-1, discovered by Joachim Grötzinger, Thomas Bosch, and their colleagues at the University of Kiel. Hydramacin-1 is distinctive because it bears little resemblance to other known antibacterial proteins, with the exception of two found in leeches. Despite its unique nature, hydramacin-1 proved highly effective in laboratory tests, capable of eliminating a broad spectrum of both Gram-positive and Gram-negative bacteria, including clinically significant, drug-resistant strains such as Klebsiella oxytoca, a frequent cause of hospital-acquired infections. Hydramacin functions by adhering to the bacterial surface, facilitating the clustering of nearby bacteria, and ultimately disrupting their cell membranes. Grötzinger and his team further elucidated hydramacin-1’s three-dimensional structure, revealing its closest structural similarities to a superfamily of proteins present in scorpion venom. Based on these findings, they propose classifying hydramacin-1 and the two leech proteins into a new family of antibacterial proteins called the macins.

Tinder has indicated it may consider native advertising as a potential revenue strategy. The dating app, in search of monetization methods for its free platform, sees opportunities within its user experience that align with native advertising. According to Tinder's chairman, Greg Blatt, the app’s nature offers unique possibilities that some of its other services do not. This move is not surprising, given Tinder’s past involvement in advertising campaigns; for instance, Fox used fake profiles to promote "The Mindy Project," and Domino's Pizza ran saucy promotions on the platform. Recently, security experts highlighted a flaw that could have exposed user locations, although the issue was quickly addressed by Tinder. ITProPortal speculates that Tinder's rapid growth could make it a candidate for the next major tech acquisition, similar to WhatsApp.
In March, Twitter announced that TweetDeck AIR, TweetDeck for Android, and TweetDeck for iPhone would be discontinued. They initially set an early May deadline but have now pinpointed the exact date: May 7th. On this date, the apps will be removed from app stores and will no longer function. The Facebook integration with all TweetDeck products will also be terminated at that time. According to Twitter, TweetDeck for Mac and PC will remain available for now, closely following updates from the Web and Chrome versions of the app. However, the Web editions will serve as the primary platform, receiving new features and updates more quickly. Twitter acquired TweetDeck in May 2011 for $40 million in cash and stock. TweetDeck, founded by Iain Dodsworth in 2008, had received $3.8 million in funding before the acquisition. It's likely that popular iPhone apps like Tweetbot will see a surge in users who previously relied on TweetDeck, while Android users may turn to alternatives such as Carbon and Hootsuite. From the desk of Executive Producer Michael Brookes: Hi everyone, This week marked the release of the 2.04 minor update, and we're planning another minor update next week to tackle some stability issues and fix problems with barnacles and certain settlements not appearing consistently. Development continues on 2.1 and beyond, and this week's update focuses on upcoming changes to NPC behavior in 2.1. The AI control of ships aims to offer a balanced experience, ensuring lower-ranked NPCs provide an enjoyable yet manageable challenge while higher-ranked opponents present a significant challenge. For 2.1, we've introduced numerous improvements and fixes to enhance the AI of NPC ships. We've adjusted the skill curves for AI pilots, making the progression more gradual for lower to mid-levels, with substantial improvements for higher-level opponents. These changes include the AI using missiles and torpedoes more effectively, especially at higher ranks, and waiting until targets' shields are down before engaging. The range of tactics available to AI pilots is now tiered by skill level, offering a broader array of strategies. Higher-ranked pilots will also prioritize damage avoidance to increase their chances of survival and reduce unnecessary errors. The AI can no longer use over-heated energy weapons to manage heat better, and they will use chaff only when under attack from gimbals or turrets. High-ranked ships will retreat when shields drop to recharge and will remain out of weapon range until shields are restored before resuming attacks. Skilled AI have learned to counter the tactic of flying ships in reverse, so be prepared! Alongside these enhancements, we've addressed several known AI issues, such as avoiding getting stuck rotating in space, preventing continuous firing of hatch breakers, and improving pip management. This includes better behavior for situations like fleeing or pursuing. Additionally, there's been an overhaul of the different states to ensure the AI exhibits appropriate behaviors in various scenarios. Thanks! Michael
A recent study from the Cass Business School in London, the University of Warwick, and the University of Wisconsin - Oshkosh examined the pay gap between men and women and found that women were just as likely as men to request salary increases. However, men were more successful in securing these raises. Specifically, the study revealed that men received a raise 20% of the time they asked, whereas women received one 16% of the time. Approximately 70% of both men and women in the sample reported having asked for a raise. While the study did not provide solutions, co-author Dr. Amanda Goodall suggested that this finding narrows down potential explanations for the pay disparity.
Six years ago (CNN) – Conservative commentator Ann Coulter defended her decision to call President Barack Obama a "r word" in a tweet, questioning whether the term is truly offensive. On an interview with CNN’s “Piers Morgan Tonight,” she said, "Maybe Vice President Joe Biden should be upset with me calling the president a retard, but not an actually disabled person." Coulter's tweet followed the third presidential debate between Obama and Republican nominee Mitt Romney. She tweeted, "I highly approve of Romney's decision to be kind and gentle to the retard," choosing the word, she said, "because it's a synonym for 'loser.'" She claimed to have used the term since. Her post drew criticism, including a viral blog from Special Olympic athlete John Franklin Stephens, who wrote, "Come on Ms. Coulter, you aren’t dumb and you aren’t shallow. So why are you continually using a word like the R-word as an insult?" Stephens explained, "I’m a 30-year-old man with Down syndrome who has struggled with the public's perception that an intellectual disability means that I am dumb and shallow. I am not either of those things, but I process information more slowly than the rest of you." Stephens appeared on "Piers Morgan Tonight" and said, "The word retard is offensive, and that I should not be a symbol for someone who is dumb and shallow. If they wanted to use me as a symbol, use me as a symbol for someone who fights adversity." Coulter argued that the term is not offensive and that language policing dictates which words should be avoided. "It's offensive according to whom? Moron, idiot, cretin, imbecile, these were exactly like retard, once technical terms to describe people with mental disabilities," she stated. "Changing the word doesn't change the definition. I was not referring to someone with Down syndrome; I was referring to the president of the United States." She also suggested those offended have little ground. "No disabled people are saying it, the spokesmen for the disabled," she said. When pressed if the word carries a similar stigma to another offensive term, she replied, "I wouldn’t use the n-word because it's a curse word."

At the Security China exhibition in Beijing last month, I saw this innovative armored spherical cabin electric patrol vehicle designed for anti-riot operations by police and paramilitary forces. The most striking feature is its 360-degree viewing capability provided by the spherical cabin. It is equipped to Level-A armor standards set by the Chinese Ministry of Public Security, offering protection against pistol bullets but not machine guns. The vehicle’s doors and windows are robust and open in a unique manner, reminiscent of Aston Martin designs. The interior, while basic and monochrome, accommodates two officers. Powered by an electric motor, it has a 15 kWh battery, a claimed top speed of 80 kilometers per hour, and a range of 120 kilometers. With a curb weight of 1200 kg and a maximum load of 300 kg, its turning radius is 4.5 meters. For enhanced riot control, the vehicle can be fitted with smoke grenade launchers mounted on the front fenders, and the occupants can shoot through holes in the windows. Only the lower two windows have wipers, and the roof-mounted camera appears small and vulnerable. Manufactured by Suzhou Zijing Qingyuan New Energy Vehicle Technology Corporation, trading as Zhijing Qingyuan, based in Suzhou, Jiangsu Province, the company is a joint venture between Tsinghua University and the Suzhou Automotive Research Institute. Zhijing Qingyuan specializes in electric vehicles for law enforcement. During my visit, police were interested in this vehicle, though no sales had been made yet. By the end of the day, a police delegation was thoroughly examining the vehicle, suggesting potential future adoption.

Calvin recounted a vivid dream where he discovered he could lift himself off the ground by extending his arms and pushing down. He flew effortlessly over trees and telephone poles, delighting in the sensation of soaring. As he swooped low over his neighborhood, people were amazed and ran alongside him. The exhilaration continued as he shot upward, his eyes watering from the wind. He laughed, making wide loops in the sky. But then, reality intruded when his mother woke him, warning that he would miss the bus if he didn’t hurry. Twenty minutes later, standing in the cold rain, Calvin was late for school and realized he had forgotten his lunch. It was shaping up to be a particularly tough Tuesday.
In a report published in Nature Cell Biology, researchers detail the identification of a key protein named disabled-2 (Dab2), which initiates epithelial-mesenchymal transdifferentiation (EMT). This process enables cancer cells to detach from the primary tumor and migrate to form new tumors elsewhere. TGF-ß, a compound previously linked to EMT, was found to stimulate the production of Dab2. The activation of Dab2 triggers EMT; removing it prevents the process from occurring. "This fills a crucial gap in our understanding of cancer metastasis," stated Ge Jin, who co-led the study alongside Philip Howe. Jin's team, comprising six researchers, conducted experiments using animal models to explore the mechanisms underlying cancer spread. Understanding the signaling pathways involved could pave the way for developing therapeutic strategies to inhibit EMT and potentially slow tumor progression. The discovery might also offer insights into disease progression beyond cancer.
A recent report from Katz Media Group indicates that digital subchannels surpass many top cable brands in terms of audience reach and household ratings. As cord-cutting and cord-shaving decrease cable channel subscriptions, digital subchannels are becoming increasingly more accessible compared to traditional cable networks. The report highlights that among the eight leading digital subchannels—MeTV, Grit, Antenna TV, Laff, Escape, This TV, Bounce TV, and Create—their wide availability exceeds that of well-known cable networks like Food Network, CNN, Discovery Channel, and TBS. Furthermore, Nielsen live-plus-seven household ratings show that MeTV ranks 20th among all cable and broadcast networks, outpacing several major cable channels including A&E, FX, Lifetime, TLC, Bravo, and MTV. According to Stacey Schulman, executive VP of strategy and analytics at Katz Media Group, these digital networks are often undervalued for advertising investments, despite their performance matching or exceeding that of cable networks commonly sought after for such investments. The report, released on Monday, also reveals that digital networks experienced significant growth in their audiences during a period of stability or decline for both cable and broadcast media. During the year from May 2016 to May 2017, average Nielsen live-plus-seven household shares increased by 42% for digital networks, whereas cable saw a 2% increase and broadcast experienced a 4% decline. Digital subchannels originated post-2009, following the transition of broadcast TV from analog to digital transmission. Most subchannels are operated by local broadcast stations, with airtime leased to digital networks, which frequently air library programming tailored to specific genres.
This article critically examines the dichotomy between incentives and access in copyright discussions. Traditional copyright theory posits that copyright aims to strike a balance between encouraging creators to produce cultural works and making these works accessible to the public. However, this paper contends that prevailing copyright theory may overlook the potential for developing a copyright framework that supports creators while simultaneously expanding access to cultural works. The internet's vast resources suggest that enhancing access to cultural products for educational, sharing, and creative purposes should be a core objective of copyright policy. The piece explores various non-exclusivity models for supporting and coordinating cultural production, such as crowdfunding, tipping, levies, restitution, and service-based approaches. Despite their current limitations, each model fails to offer a comprehensive and compelling perspective on the dual roles of copyright: funding cultural production and fairly remunerating creators. The article identifies three areas for future research to explore alternative copyright models: (1) refining theories of fairness in copyright rewards; (2) conducting more empirical studies on commons-based models of cultural production; and (3) critically assessing the noneconomic harms addressed by exclusive rights in copyright.

LAS VEGAS—The Virtuix Omni aims to revolutionize virtual reality for the feet, much like the Oculus Rift transformed the visual experience. This 360-degree treadmill allows users to walk and run in a virtual world while remaining safely stationary. Like the Rift, the Omni was initially funded through crowdfunding and garnered significant attention; it is now set to deliver to early supporters later this year. I tested it at CES 2015. The Omni consists of a body cage with a large, shallow bowl for walking, supported by arms forming a waist-high ring. Users wear slip-on shoes with sensors, and a harness keeps them centered and upright. In my demo, I navigated a shooting gallery using the Oculus Rift, running through corridors and shooting targets with a gun-shaped controller. Although the pre-production model only allowed forward walking, the final version will permit movement in all directions. Initially, walking on the Omni felt awkward due to the minimal friction between the shoes and the floor. After adapting, I achieved a comfortable pace, though at first, I moved erratically, reminiscent of a Scooby-Doo character running for dear life. The harness ensured I stayed within the waist-high ring, preventing excessive forward or backward movement. With practice, I mastered the right lean to move efficiently without appearing to flail. Despite the slippery sensation, the demo provided reliable control, and the experience seemed promising. While physically running through levels in first-person shooters might be impractical, virtually walking through fantasy landscapes or exploring museums appeared entirely feasible. The Virtuix Omni is currently available for pre-order at $499, with the price increasing to $799 upon shipment.

Analyzing Amazon's Buckets: As promised, here's an analysis of the data from my Bucket Finder tool. I tested common names since most users likely name their buckets after themselves. Using a list of 2,268 names from Packet Storm, the results showed that 1,206 buckets don't exist, while 848 are private and 131 are public. This 5% hit rate of existing public buckets seems promising. With Packet Storm's larger word lists, if the same success rate holds, we could expect to find over 5,000 public buckets to investigate. Files in Public Buckets: Of the public buckets found, there are 15,699 total files, with 6,016 in private buckets and 9,683 in public ones. This indicates that about one-third of users store private files in public buckets, suggesting intentional sharing or possibly default settings by applications managing these buckets. File Types Found: Based on file extensions, the breakdown of public files includes 7,086 images (jpg, png, gif, tiff, psd, bmp), 1,377 web files (html, css, js), 436 video and music files (mp3, mp4, flv, mov, avi, wmv, m4v, aa, mpg), 80 document files (pdf, doc, xls, ppt), 57 SQL files, and 646 other files. A pie chart visualizes this distribution. Most image files on S3 appear to be personal photo collections, often of babies, indicating users are sharing personal content. Document files contained sensitive data like training requisitions and company accounts, which should not have been publicly accessible. Video files mostly consisted of training and motivational content. Music files revealed large collections from various artists. Overall, the findings are diverse, with valuable data potentially hidden within the vast amount of information. Automating the process to identify valuable data would be beneficial, so any suggestions for automation are welcome.
A critical report reveals serious mistakes in obtaining search warrants for suspected sex offenders, resulting in innocent individuals being targeted and families being split apart during sexual offenses investigations. The errors, highlighted by the Interception of Communications Commissioner, Sir Stanley Burnton, during his annual report to the Prime Minister, involved some of the most invasive powers the state can exercise against citizens. For instance, two children were mistakenly separated from their parents for a weekend while the parents were interrogated as suspects in a child sexual exploitation case; it was later discovered that the police had executed the warrant at the wrong address, a mistake caused by incorrect documentation. Digital devices belonging to innocent people were also subjected to forensic examination. These errors largely stemmed from inaccuracies in the software used to determine the geographical locations associated with specific IP addresses. Burnton cautioned against relying on IP addresses to identify internet users behind crimes, noting that they frequently change hands. He emphasized that such errors are alarmingly frequent, particularly in cases involving child sexual exploitation, with severe impacts on victims. Of the 731,000 applications for intrusive powers, 29 serious errors occurred, representing 0.004%. These mistakes led to multiple instances of innocent people being treated as suspects and detained, having their homes and devices searched, and even being arrested and interviewed under caution. Incorrect interpretation of communications data resulted in the wrong individual being detained and questioned in one investigation, and in another, a police murder investigation contacted the wrong person after recording a telephone number incorrectly.
