North America's expanding marijuana industry shows no signs of slowing down, as Kwantlen Polytechnic University in Metro Vancouver is offering a comprehensive 14-week course on growing and selling cannabis. The curriculum, led by Tegan Adams from Experchem Laboratories, covers cannabis cultivation, legal navigation, and facility management, with a second part focusing on marketing, sales, and drug development. The course, priced at $3,000, aims to provide insights similar to those in the manufacturing sector rather than traditional agriculture. The Canadian National Medical Marijuana Association helped design the course, which aligns with Canada's 25 licensed growers. Meanwhile, other educational institutions like the Northeastern Institute of Cannabis in Massachusetts and Anne Arundel Community College in Maryland are also integrating marijuana studies into their curricula, preparing students for careers in this burgeoning industry.
During an interview on CNBC on May 3, 2017, Apple CEO Tim Cook announced the company's intention to launch a $1 billion fund aimed at fostering advanced manufacturing jobs within the United States. Cook emphasized that the fund would play a catalytic role, stating, "If we can generate many manufacturing jobs, the ripple effect will be significant, as these jobs will spawn additional employment through supporting industries." This initiative aligns with President Trump's repeated advocacy for reshoring American manufacturing jobs from overseas. However, Cook did not specify plans for Apple to establish a major manufacturing facility in the U.S. for producing its products. Currently, Apple manufactures only the Mac Pro in its California headquarters, with the bulk of its production remaining in China due to lower operational costs there. Apple’s $1 billion fund might be interpreted as a strategic move to align with the Trump administration’s policies, potentially enhancing the company’s leverage in negotiating favorable terms for its business. Other pressing concerns for Apple and similar corporations include the recent suspension of expedited H-1B visa processing, which limits the quick recruitment of skilled workers from abroad, and the possibility of more advantageous conditions offered by the Trump administration to encourage repatriation of profits from foreign bank accounts. Given that 93% of Apple’s $256.8 billion cash reserve is held outside the U.S., such initiatives could be crucial. In the same interview, Cook discussed broader strategies, including efforts to expand Apple’s workforce, developer community, and manufacturing base. He also highlighted plans to promote coding among Americans, with details expected to be revealed in the coming months. When asked about corporate responsibility in job creation, Cook responded that companies should contribute to society by generating employment, among other actions. He confirmed that Apple’s $1 billion fund plan is already set and pledged to provide comprehensive details soon. Notably, other tech companies like Amazon and Intel are also investing in local job creation; Amazon has pledged 100,000 new full-time positions by mid-2018, while Intel is investing $7 billion in a new Arizona chip factory.

Nestle plans to reduce nearly 300 jobs and transfer Blue Riband chocolate biscuit production to Poland, according to union reports. Job cuts will primarily impact sites in York and Newcastle, with smaller reductions in Halifax and Girvan. Unions, including the GMB and Unite, have criticized the decision, stating that Nestle should "export chocolate, not jobs." The company proposes cutting 143 jobs in York, 110 at Fawdon, 15 in Halifax, and seven in Girvan. GMB general secretary Tim Roache noted, "Shifting the production of a British icon like Blue Riband to Poland is unacceptable. These factories should be exporting chocolate, not people's jobs." He also called on the government to intervene to protect workers. In a statement, Nestle said these changes aim to enhance operational efficiency and competitiveness. Unite national officer Julia Long vowed to campaign to save jobs and urged Nestle to invest in its UK operations instead. GMB northern region officer Valerie Scott likened the situation to "the worst kind of Brexit," highlighting the negative impact on northern regions.

UMass guard Derrick Gordon, the first openly gay player in NCAA Division I men's basketball, recently informed ESPN of his decision to transfer to another school for his final college season. Gordon, a 6-foot-2 guard who started his career at Western Kentucky, averaged 9.8 points and 4.9 rebounds per game last season. He publicly came out as gay in April. "I thank the coaches and my teammates for their support," Gordon stated. "My departure has nothing to do with my sexuality; everyone was incredibly supportive." Last year, UMass reached the NCAA tournament but had an overall record of 17-15 this season, with a 10-8 mark in the Atlantic 10. "This is a personal choice to pursue my goals," Gordon explained. "I want to be in the best position to succeed and win as many games as possible."

As the US elections draw near, the White House is focused on ensuring a seamless transfer of power, including the handover of all presidential social media accounts. This involves transferring access to the @POTUS Twitter account, established in May 2015 and boasting over 11 million followers, resetting it for the incoming president's fresh start on January 20. Similarly, the White House’s Facebook, Instagram, YouTube, Medium, and Tumblr accounts will be handed over. During Obama's tenure, all content will be preserved by the National Archives and Records Administration (NARA) and made accessible via new handles such as @POTUS44 on Twitter. The current WhiteHouse.gov website will be archived and accessible at ObamaWhiteHouse.gov. Additionally, the Obama administration plans to release all archived content for public download and invites suggestions on how to enhance accessibility. While President Obama may not mind losing some social media influence, his @POTUS44 account still garners around 78.5 million followers. It will be intriguing to observe how the next president leverages technology to engage with the public. For updates on the White House’s archival process, follow @WHWeb on Twitter.

Gnome Shell Lock Screen: - Lock - Slide up (currently achievable only with the mouse, not via a shortcut) - Unlock - Pin Unlocker placement GDM and the Lock screen share a similar design but are distinct modules. Both can be themable, allowing customization beyond the current blue curtain appearance. Ubuntu: While Gnome is currently bound to Ubuntu, most users access Gnome Shell through Canonical's products. This extends beyond Unity, involving compatibility issues and discussions about Nautilus and SystemD. Ultimately, achieving a vanilla Gnome experience in Ubuntu seems impossible, regardless of who is at fault.
This article is from the archive of our partner. Born in 1896, Walter Breuning's life story vividly reflects the evolution of modern America. Breuning, who passed away at 114, was just 26 days younger than Besse Cooper of Georgia, who holds the record for the world's oldest living person. He could recall events from the early 1900s, including his father’s tales of the Civil War. A native of Minnesota, Breuning began working for the railroad at 16 and attempted to enlist in World War I at 20, although he was not called to serve. In 1919, the year women won the right to vote, Breuning purchased his first car, which he found so noisy that it frightened horses. During the Great Depression, he felt fortunate to maintain his employment, and he believed President Franklin Roosevelt’s establishment of Social Security to be the country’s most significant accomplishment. By the time America entered World War II, Breuning was too elderly to join, and by the time the Beatles released their first album, the long-time railroad clerk had retired. The advent of computers transformed the railroad industry, and despite many of his colleagues losing their jobs, Breuning viewed these changes positively.

Stugotz believes that since Michigan can afford to pay its top three football assistants over $1 million each, it should also be able to compensate student athletes similarly. Ann Arbor, Mich. — Michigan has committed to paying Jim Harbaugh’s top three football assistants $1 million annually, making them the first public institution, among those required to disclose contracts through Freedom of Information Act requests, to do so. Defensive coordinator Don Brown and offensive coordinator Tim Drevno each have contracts valued at over $10 million over the next five years, while passing coordinator Pep Hamilton, previously with the Cleveland Browns, was lured with a $4.25 million, four-year deal. Brown's contract stipulates $1 million annually for the first four years, increasing to $1.4 million in 2021, with retention bonuses of $300,000 in 2018 and 2019, and $400,000 in 2020 and 2021. Drevno's deal includes $1 million annually plus a $150,000 signing bonus. Michigan extended these offers to Brown and Drevno in December, shortly after losing to Florida State in the Orange Bowl. Hamilton, an associate head coach for the Browns, joined the staff in January with a $1 million salary for the first three years, rising to $1.25 million in 2020, along with a $150,000 signing bonus and retention bonuses of $450,000 in 2018 and $250,000 in 2019. Both Drevno and Brown have been part of Harbaugh’s staff since his arrival. Michigan also announced plans for its football team to conduct spring practices in Rome, following the NCAA's ban on combining spring breaks and football practices.

Initially, both players are expected to contribute primarily as rotational pieces.
In 1975, David Bowie received a Kirlian photography machine from Thelma Ross, a researcher at UCLA's parapsychology lab, to capture images of people's "auras." This device creates a high-voltage field that produces a glowing corona discharge image based on the object placed on a photographic plate. Factors like humidity and the object's grounding can affect the image's appearance, but Bowie's fascination with the occult and the mysterious nature of these images led him to experiment. According to The Daily Grail, Bowie documented his experiments by taking Kirlian photographs of his fingertip before and after consuming cocaine, comparing them to a crucifix given to him by his father. He even used one of these images as cover art for the "Little Wonder" single and in the booklet of his 1997 album, Earthling.

Most of us use laptops to charge our cell phones daily, but Intel is exploring ways to simplify this process with inductive charging. Simply place your phone beside the laptop, and it will start charging. According to The Verge, Intel’s new all-in-one PC design includes inductive charging for the keyboard, and the company envisions a future where ultrabooks can recharge smartphones. Demonstrated with an Acer Aspire laptop, the wireless charger is compact, adding minimal bulk to the device. When charging, you’ll hear a confirming beep, and a notification appears on the laptop’s screen. While this eliminates the need to carry extra cables, concerns remain about efficiency and the increased energy needed for the transmitter installed on the laptop and the receiver on the phone. Some argue that inductive charging might even necessitate more frequent charging of the laptop itself. A commenter notes that often, people connect their phones to laptops to access storage, not just for charging. Inductive charging could be more environmentally friendly, but we’re not there yet.

Noam Chomsky, an intellectual and self-described libertarian socialist, told BBC News that the Republican Party is the most dangerous organization in human history due to their inaction on global warming. Chomsky, 88, acknowledged, "When I made that statement, I noted it was a very bold claim, but one that must be considered." The interviewer compared this to the threat posed by figures like Kim Jong Un or ISIS, to which Chomsky countered, "Is ISIS genuinely working to end all organized human existence?" Chomsky maintained that Republicans are worse because they are not merely indifferent to climate change but actively exacerbating it. "They’re not just not acting; they’re pushing us toward disaster," he argued. When the interviewer mentioned that ISIS is engaged in a civil war and has committed atrocities, Chomsky emphasized that the Republican stance on climate change is more alarming. "Whether they believe it or not doesn't change the fact that their actions are accelerating the crisis," he insisted. A professor emeritus at MIT, Chomsky has long critiqued American imperialism, opposing the Vietnam War and viewing the fall of the Soviet Union as a victory for socialism.

Patrick Brown, the newly appointed Progressive Conservative Leader, won a seat in the Ontario legislature in a by-election four months after securing the party leadership. Garfield Dunlop, a longtime Progressive Conservative MPP from Simcoe North, stepped down from his position in the summer, allowing Brown to contest the election. In May, Brown had previously resigned his federal seat in the nearby riding of Barrie to focus on the leadership race. Although Dunlop was one of Brown's most vocal critics during the leadership contest, he later endorsed Brown in Simcoe North upon resigning his seat. Brown utilized his canvassing and campaign organization skills, which helped him defeat Christine Elliott, the caucus favourite, for the leadership. Early results indicated that Brown received over 50% of the votes, defeating Liberal candidate Fred Larsen and NDP candidate Elizabeth Van Houtte, a social work professor at Lakehead University.

Previously, we examined the primary factors contributing to job losses due to EU membership. Today, I aim to provide a reasoned estimate of the number of jobs lost due to our current EU status. The main factor is the impact on manufacturing, where high energy costs have led to the closure of petrochemical plants, aluminum smelters, steel facilities, and other energy-intensive industries. This has resulted in the UK importing some power from France through interconnectors rather than producing all its own. If we had energy prices similar to the US, alongside increased domestic production of oil, gas, and shale gas, and adopted German-style coal-fired power stations, we could potentially gain around 15% more jobs in manufacturing—approximately 450,000 additional jobs. Additionally, this could lead to more jobs in the energy sector, potentially adding around 10% or 50,000 jobs. Agricultural and fishing sectors have faced constraints due to EU quotas and policies, but domestic policies could add about 10% more jobs—around 30,000. Altogether, this suggests that the UK could have over 500,000 more jobs if it had greater control over its industries, energy production, and business regulations. There may also be further gains in the services sector, which is the largest part of our labor market.

The Canadian Army reports that the 5th Canadian Division has received its first Textron TAPV (Tactical Armoured Patrol Vehicle) at Gagetown, New Brunswick. These six vehicles will be utilized for training operators and maintainers. The army plans to distribute a fleet of 500 TAPVs across seven bases and 24 units over a 17-month period. Full operational capability is anticipated by mid-2020 after comprehensive training and user trials confirming readiness. The TAPVs are delivered in two variants: General Utility and Reconnaissance. Each vehicle features a remote weapons station, enabling gunners to operate and fire from inside. This system includes a 40-mm automatic grenade launcher and a C6 machine gun. On March 21, the suspected murderer of RTI activist Vinayak Pandurang Baliga in Mangalore is a 39-year-old former convenor of the NaMo Brigade, a youth organization established in Karnataka to support Prime Minister Narendra Modi's 2014 Lok Sabha election campaign. An Indian Express report states that the police are searching for Naresh Shenoy, one of the NaMo Brigade's founders and a close RSS associate. Investigations indicate Shenoy and three associates were involved in Baliga's murder, which occurred just 75 meters from his home on the morning of March 21. Mangalore Police Commissioner M Chandrashekhar reported that Baliga was hacked to death by unknown assailants near his house. Shenoy's residence was searched as part of the murder investigation on Thursday, and he has been missing for over a week with his phone turned off. Two individuals, Nishith Devadiga and Vinith Poojary, were initially arrested; further investigations linked them to a contract killing orchestrated by Shenoy's associates. Police sources claim Shenoy hired Shivu and Shrikanth, a former Hindutva activist and temple manager respectively, to carry out the crime. Another employee of Shenoy named Vignesh, who was driving a Qualis car, was reportedly present at the scene to assist the killers in their escape. Baliga, a BJP worker, was involved in a dispute with the Venkataramana Temple authorities over alleged misuse of temple funds, prompting police to suspect this as the primary motive for his murder. Shenoy was also connected to the temple and aligned with those Baliga had opposed.
On June 10, 2016, Mitt Romney spoke to CNN’s Wolf Blitzer and harshly criticized Donald Trump’s campaign. Romney stated, "I don't want to see a U.S. president espousing views that alter the character of future American generations." He added, "Presidential actions shape our nation, and spreading racism, bigotry, and misogyny pose grave risks to America’s core values." Romney also considered supporting the Libertarian candidate, Gary Johnson, saying, "If Bill Weld were running, I'd find it easy to support him." He planned to get to know Johnson better before deciding whether to back him. However, Romney reaffirmed his stance against both entering the race and voting for Hillary Clinton, the Democratic nominee. In response to Blitzer’s question, Romney clarified, "My duty is to articulate my beliefs regarding the party’s nominee. The people made their choice, and I respect that. Personally, I cannot align with someone promoting racism, xenophobia, misogyny, or vulgarity repeatedly."
The New England Patriots will face the Buffalo Bills on November 11 at Gillette Stadium, maintaining at least a share of the lead in the AFC East. This game comes just over a year since their lone loss at home in the 2011 season against the New York Giants. Following that setback, there were doubts about the Patriots' ability to compete with the NFL's elite. However, they went on to win eight games in eight weeks, solidifying their status as the league's top team and earning a Super Bowl appearance. Now, with the Patriots back at 5-3 and having won four of their last five games, some continue to highlight their defensive weaknesses and inconsistent offense. Has anything truly changed?

Lee Kleinman initially supported the fee-based ordinance on Friday but reversed his stance five days later, stating he would concentrate on his own district's issues. "I think I should focus on North Dallas redevelopment projects rather than helping other areas improve their quality of life," he explained, surprising his colleagues. Vonciel Jones Hill, previously opposed to any bag ban or tax, was absent from the vote. Monica Alonzo voted against the measure but remained silent. The American Progressive Bag Alliance criticized the decision, claiming it would harm 4,500 Texas jobs and consumers. Lee Califf, the executive director, asserted that the vote exemplifies environmental misinformation leading to bad policy. Whether the state will permit Dallas's new bag "ban" or tax remains uncertain. Attorney General Greg Abbott will review the legality of such bans at the request of the Texas Retailers Association. Dallas City Attorney Warren Ernst stated they would defend the ordinance if passed, though uncertainty lingered. Opponents argued for better enforcement of existing litter laws. Council member Scott Griggs concluded, "This is just one step; we'll address Styrofoam and other trash issues next."
A 23-year-old man named Jared Kelly, who nearly starved his dog to death after losing interest in it, has been banned from owning animals for five years and fined over $850. Kelly admitted to ill-treating an animal at the Papakura District Court. In June of the previous year, an SPCA inspector discovered Kelly's boxer/staffordshire terrier cross chained without shelter, severely malnourished, and infested with fleas, worms, and overgrown nails. The dog also had open sores on its legs and rear. Kelly confessed to having lost interest in the dog and considering having it euthanized. He handed the dog over to SPCA Auckland. SPCA Auckland's executive director, Bob Kerridge, described it as a tragic case where an animal dependent on its owner for care was neglected and left in distress simply because the owner had "lost interest." Kerridge emphasized that neglecting an animal is unacceptable and noted that the dog had to be humanely euthanized due to serious behavioral issues that made rehoming impossible. This outcome was likely a direct result of the dog's past neglect.
This CCTV image from Brussels Airport surveillance cameras, provided by the Belgian Police, shows individuals believed to be suspects in the March 22, 2016, attack. According to U.S. government sources, two brothers involved in the Brussels bombings—Khalid El Bakraoui and Brahim El Bakraoui—were on U.S. counterterrorism watchlists prior to the March 18 arrest of Salah Abdeslam, who is accused of playing a key role in the November 13, 2015, Paris attacks. Belgian prosecutors have identified Brahim El Bakraoui as one of the suicide bombers at Brussels' Zaventem Airport, while Khalid El Bakraoui is believed to be the bomber at the Maelbeek Metro station, close to EU headquarters. Elizabeth Warren takes the stage for her Senate acceptance after defeating incumbent Sen. Scott Brown on November 6, 2012. Photograph by Darren McCollester/Getty Images. Maybe they should have allowed her the position she initially sought. The Huffington Post reports that nearly two years after Wall Street successfully prevented consumer advocate Elizabeth Warren from heading the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau, she will join the Banking Committee, as confirmed by four informed sources. This is a triumph for progressives who fought to secure her a seat on the panel responsible for overseeing Dodd-Frank and other banking regulations. Warren had established the consumer protection bureau but was ultimately blocked by banking lobbyists and their Republican Senate allies. By running successfully for Senate in Massachusetts, she ended moderate GOP Sen. Scott Brown's tenure in the upper chamber. Now, she will hold a key position to question Wall Street bankers and executives during congressional hearings.

Following a visit by Russian President Vladimir Putin, Indian Prime Minister Narendra Modi announced that Russia will assist in constructing at least 10 additional nuclear reactors, part of a series of significant energy agreements signed between the two nations on Thursday. Modi also noted that Russia remains India's primary defense supplier. The agreements come as India grapples with energy shortages and Russia seeks to strengthen ties in Asia amid Western sanctions. During the talks, both countries outlined an ambitious vision for nuclear energy, with construction slated to commence over the next two decades. A $1 billion joint venture for hydroelectric power projects was also agreed upon. Additionally, Russian oil company Rosneft signed a deal to supply India with 10 million tons of oil annually. Putin highlighted Russia’s intent to increase oil and gas exports to Asia due to challenges in the European market. In the wake of the cancellation of the South Stream gas pipeline project and tensions arising from the Ukraine crisis, which has led to wide-ranging sanctions against Russia, the defense sector remains a focal point. India is pleased with plans for Russia to manufacture its most advanced helicopter in the country, despite recent losses of lucrative defense contracts to the U.S. and Europe. Russia and India were once close allies during the Cold War but have experienced some tension in recent years. India hopes to secure a greater share of Russian rough diamonds, given that Russia is the world's leading producer and India is the global center for diamond cutting and polishing.
The Punjab and Haryana High Court issued a notice to the Kapurthala district's SSP, directing them to explain why contempt proceedings should not be initiated for failing to act on a complaint against self-styled 'godwoman' Sukhwinder Kaur, also known as Radhe Maa. The single bench of Justice Daya Chaudhary gave this direction based on a complaint filed by Phagwara resident Surinder Mittal. The matter will be heard on October 13. Counsel for the complainant, Krishan Singh Dadwal, stated that the high court had issued a show-cause notice to the Kapurthala SSP regarding the intentional non-compliance with an earlier court order. In 2015, Phagwara-based Surinder Mittal had filed a complaint against Radhe Maa, requesting police action for alleged offenses, including hurting religious sentiments and threats. Despite being reminded of the court order, no action was taken by the police, prompting Mittal to file another contempt petition.

China’s leaders have imposed a five-year moratorium on government building construction as part of an anti-corruption drive aimed at curbing wasteful spending. On Tuesday, directives were issued by the Communist Party’s central committee and the State Council, as reported by Xinhua News Agency. Publicly visible government structures, often criticized for their grandiosity, are now subject to a comprehensive ban. President Xi Jinping’s efforts to reduce ostentatiousness and eliminate waste among high-ranking officials have faced criticism from some citizens. The directives mandate a complete halt to the construction of both official buildings and ostentatious facilities like training centers, hotels, or government guesthouses. In certain cases, government agencies have constructed such buildings in scenic areas to provide perks to officials and staff, sometimes even profiting from them. According to Liu Shanying, a political scientist from the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences, these lavish structures contribute to corruption since they consume public funds. This five-year ban represents a substantial step in combating corruption, he noted. Additionally, the directives stipulate that officials holding multiple positions should maintain only one office, and vacated offices must be returned promptly. The measures encourage thriftiness and emphasize that government expenditures should focus on economic development and social welfare. Officials are allowed to allocate funds for the maintenance of existing government offices. Despite previous limitations, some departments and regions have continued to construct government complexes without adhering to regulations.
